Ijarah — Hire and Lease
beginner
6 min
Definition and Permissibility of Ijarah
Defines ijarah and establishes its permissibility with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah and explain its permissibility using Quranic and hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a contract on benefits for compensation; validity requires both benefit and wage to be known.

This passage opens the Book of Ijarah with its definition and the evidence for its permissibility. The matn presents two key points: the definition as a contract on benefits for compensation, and the condition that both the benefit and the wage must be known. The commentary elaborates using the Quranic story of Musa (AS) and hadith warnings against withholding wages. Understanding the definition and foundational proofs is essential before proceeding to detailed rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first line of the matn: 'الاجارة عقد على المنافع بعوض'. This is the definition. Write it down.
The definition directly from the primary text.
2
Find the conditions for validity
The second line states: 'ولا تصح حتى تكون المنافع معلومة والأجرة معلومة'. This means the contract is not valid until the benefit and wage are known.
These are conditions (shurut) that must be satisfied.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The commentary cites Surah al-Qasas 28:27, where Musa (AS) is hired for eight years. This shows a historical example of ijarah.
The verse is used as dalil for permissibility, though its dalalah is zanni (interpretive).
4
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith from Bukhari states that Allah will oppose three types of people, including one who hires a worker, takes full work, but does not pay the wage. This condemnation implies the contract is permissible and must be honored.
A second hadith from Bayhaqi adds that the wage must be informed to the worker.
5
Understand the legal reasoning
The commentary explains that benefits are non-existent at the time of contract but are considered existent due to necessity and textual evidence. This permits leasing and hiring despite the benefits being future.
This is a key Hanafi principle: al-manafi' tu'tabaru mawjudatan li al-hajah.

Source Text

[۱۱۵۶) (۱) اجاره عقد ہے منافع پر عوض کے بدلے۔

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شعیب نے فرمایا میں چاہتا ہوں کہ میری دونوں بیٹیوں میں سے ایک کا آپ سے نکاح کر دوں اس بدلے میں کہ آٹھ سال تک اجرت کا کام کریں۔ پس اگر دس پورے کریں تو آپ کے پاس سے ہوگا (ب) حضور فرماتے ہیں کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا کہ قیامت کے دن تین آدمیوں کا میں مدعی ہوں گا۔ ایک آدمی جس نے میری وجہ سے عہد کیا پھر دھوکہ دیا۔ دوسرا آدمی جس نے آزاد کو بیچا اور اس کی قیمت کھائی اور تیسرا آدمی جس نے کسی مزدور کو اجرت پر رکھا اور اس سے پورا کام لیا پھر اس کو اجرت نہیں دی (ج ) آپ سے روایت ہے کہ کسی نے اجیر کو اجرت پر لیا تو اس کی اجرت کتنی ہے اس کی اطلاع دینی چاہئے۔
Book of Ijarah
[1156] (1) Ijarah is a contract on benefits in exchange for compensation.
[1157] (2) And it is not valid until the benefits are known and the wage is known.

Essential note: One side is benefit and the other side is a specific item, like a pound, dirham, or a measured or weighed thing, then it is called Ijarah. In Ijarah, the benefit is non-existent, but due to necessity and hadith, with some conditions it is considered existent and Ijarah is deemed permissible. Its proof is in this verse: 'He said: Indeed I wish to marry you to one of these two daughters of mine on condition that you work for me for eight years; if you complete ten, then it is from you.' (Surah al-Qasas 27) In this verse, the marriage of Musa (peace be upon him) was contracted on the wage of herding goats for eight years. (2) And its proof is also in the hadith: From Abu Huraira from the Prophet that Allah said: 'Three are those whom I will oppose on the Day of Judgment: a man who made a covenant in My name then betrayed, a man who sold a free person and consumed his price, and a man who hired a worker and took full work from him but did not pay his wage.' (Bukhari, Bab Ithm man mana'a ajr al-ajir) This hadith shows that taking work and not paying wages is condemned, proving that Ijarah is permissible.
[1156] (1) Ijarah is a contract on benefits in exchange for compensation.
The meaning of Ijarah is that one side is benefit and the other side is a specific thing, like dirhams, dinars, wheat, or any measured or weighed item. This is called the contract of Ijarah. The reason for its permissibility is the above verse and hadith.
[1157] (2) Ijarah is not valid until the benefits are known and the wage is known.
The benefits must be known in terms of quantity and period, and the wage must also be known. If they are not known, dispute will arise, so both must be known. (2) In the above verse, 'eight years' makes the benefit known, and 'marriage' (?) makes the compensation known, indicating both must be known. (3) In the hadith: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage.'

Footnote: (a) Shu'ayb said: I wish to marry one of these two daughters to you on condition that you work for me for eight years; if you complete ten, then it is from you. (b) The Prophet said: Allah said: Three are those whom I will oppose on the Day of Judgment: a man who made a covenant in My name then betrayed, a man who sold a free person and consumed his price, and a man who hired a worker and took full work from him but did not pay his wage. (c) It is narrated that if someone hires a worker, he should inform him of his wage.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Ijarah (Leasing/Hiring) by defining the contract and establishing its permissibility. The matn states two foundational points: (1) Ijarah is a contract on benefits (manafi') in exchange for compensation ('iwad). (2) It is not valid (la tasihh) until both the benefit and the wage are known. The commentary explains that 'benefits' are non-existent at the time of contract but are considered existent due to necessity and textual evidence. The primary proofs are the Quranic verse from Surah al-Qasas where Musa (AS) was hired for eight years, and the hadith from Bukhari where Allah declares opposition to three types of people, including one who does not pay the hired worker. A second hadith from Bayhaqi further emphasizes that the worker must be informed of his wage. The commentary also clarifies that Ijarah requires the benefit to be from one side and a specific item (like money or goods) from the other, distinguishing it from other contracts. This ruling establishes the validity and conditions of Ijarah in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
اجارة (ijārah): A contract on benefits (manāfi') in exchange for compensation ('iwad); includes hiring of services or leasing of properties.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or utility derived from an object or service; in Ijarah, it is the subject matter of the contract.
عوض ('iwaḍ): Compensation or consideration given in exchange for the benefit; it can be money, goods, or other valuable items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is one essential condition for the validity of an Ijarah contract?
A) The wage must be given in advance.
B) The benefit must be known and the wage must be known.
C) The contract must be written.
D) The worker must be a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is a contract on known benefits for known compensation; its permissibility is proven by Quran and Sunnah.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

The Definition and Proof of Ijarah
Defines ijarah and gives its proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah and identify the Quranic and Hadith proofs for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a contract on benefits (manāfi‘) for a price, proven by the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Before we dive into the specific rulings of ijarah (hire/lease), we must first understand what it is and why it is valid. The Hanafi school defines ijarah as a contract on benefits, not on the physical asset itself. This lesson presents the core definition and the primary textual evidence—a verse from Surah Al-Qasas and a powerful hadith about the rights of workers—that establish its legitimacy.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Hanafi definition of ijarah
Identify ijarah as a contract whose subject matter is benefits (manāfi‘) in exchange for compensation (‘iwad). Note that the benefit is non‑existent at the time of contract but is considered existing due to need and textual evidence.
The commentary stresses that the benefit is 'non‑existent' but elevated to existence by necessity and hadith.
2
Locate the first proof – Quranic verse
Read the verse from Surah Al‑Qasas (28:27‑28) where Prophet Shu‘ayb offers marriage to Musa on condition that Musa works for him for eight years. This verse shows a valid hire arrangement.
The verse uses the verb 'ta’jurna' (you hire yourself), indicating a contract for services.
3
Locate the second proof – Hadith
Examine the hadith where Allah declares Himself the opponent of three people on the Day of Judgment: one who breaks a covenant, one who sells a free person, and one who hires a worker, takes full work, and does not pay him.
This hadith implies that the hiring itself is valid; otherwise Allah would not threaten the employer for withholding wages.
4
Understand the legal implication
Both proofs together establish the jawaaz (permissibility) of ijarah. The Hanafi school relies on these naqli proofs to overcome the original objection that benefit is non‑existent at contract formation.
The ruling is that ijarah is sahih (valid) when its conditions are fulfilled.

The Book of Ijarah. [1156 (1)] Ijarah is a contract on benefits in exchange for compensation. [Commentary: Essential note: When one side is a benefit and the other side is a concrete item like a pound, dirham, or a measureable or weighable thing, it is called ijarah. In ijarah, the benefit is non-existent, but due to need and hadiths, with certain conditions it is considered existing, and ijarah is deemed permissible. Its proof is in this verse: He said, 'I intend to marry you to one of these two daughters of mine on condition that you hire yourself to me for eight years; if you complete ten, it will be of your own accord' (Surah Al-Qasas 27-28). In this verse, Prophet Musa's marriage was on the hire of herding sheep for eight years. And there is proof in the hadith: From Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: Allah said, 'Three are My opponents on the Day of Judgment: a man who made a covenant in My name then betrayed, a man who sold a free person and devoured his price, and a man who hired a worker and took full work from him then did not give him his wage.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Sin of One who Withholds the Wage of a Worker, p. 302, no. 2270). This hadith indicates that ijarah is permissible. [1156) (1) Ijarah is a contract on benefits for compensation. Explanation: It means that on one side is benefit and on the other side is a concrete item like dirham, dinar, wheat, or any measureable or weighable thing. This is called a contract of ijarah. The reason for its permissibility is the above verse and hadith. Footnote: (a) Prophet Shu'ayb said: I intend to marry you to one of these two daughters of mine on condition that you work for me for eight years; if you complete ten, it is from you. (b) The Prophet said: Allah said, 'I will be the opponent of three people on the Day of Judgment: one who makes a covenant in My name then betrays, one who sells a free person and eats his price, and one who hires a worker and takes full work then does not give him his wage.'
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, defining the contract of ijarah (hire/lease) and establishing its legitimacy. The author defines ijarah as a contract on benefits (manāfi‘) in exchange for a consideration (‘iwad). The commentary explains that the benefit is non-existent at contract formation but is considered existing due to need and prophetic evidence, with certain conditions. The primary proofs are a Quranic verse (Surah Al-Qasas 27-28) where Prophet Mūsā is hired for eight years, and a hadith where Allah warns against withholding wages, implying the validity of hiring. The footnote clarifies the Quranic and hadith references. The text emphasizes that ijarah is fundamentally permissible (jā’iz) based on naqlī evidence.

Key Terms
الاجارة (al-ijarah): A contract on benefits (manāfi‘) in exchange for a consideration (‘iwad).
منافع (manāfi‘): Benefits or usufruct of an asset, considered as subject matter of ijarah.
عوض (‘iwad): Compensation or consideration given in exchange for the benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Condition for Valid Ijarah: Benefit and Rent Must Be Known
States condition of knowledge for valid ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a valid ijarah contract and identify the proofs (Quran, hadith, and legal maxim) that establish these conditions.

Core Idea
Ijarah is valid only if both benefit and rent are known — uncertainty invalidates.

This lesson examines a foundational condition for the validity of ijarah (lease/hire) contracts in Hanafi fiqh. The text states clearly that ijarah is not sahih unless both the benefit being contracted and the rent paid are known (ma‘lūm). You will see the textual proofs from the Quran, the Sunnah, and the general legal principle that anything delivered in the future must be specified to avoid gharar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the condition: ijarah requires known benefit and known rent. The text begins by saying 'Ijarah is not valid unless the benefits are known and the rent is known.'
2
Examine the Quranic Proof
The author cites the verse mentioning 'eight years' (Quran 28:27) as implicit evidence that the duration (and thus the benefit) was known, and 'marry' indicates the consideration was known.
The verse is about Musa working for eight years; the specified duration makes the benefit known.
3
Examine the Hadith Proofs
Two hadiths are quoted: (1) 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage' (Bayhaqi) – this makes the wage known. (2) The hadith of the cupper where the benefit (cupping) and wage (a known measure of wheat) were both specified.
The cupping hadith demonstrates that both benefit and wage were explicitly known.
4
Apply the General Legal Maxim
The author applies the principle from the salam hadith: anything delivered later must be specified in measure, weight, and term. Since ijarah involves future benefits, they must be described clearly.
This is a qiyas from salam to ijarah based on the common illa of future delivery.
5
Determine the Consequence
If the condition is not met (benefit or rent unknown), the contract is fasid because ignorance leads to dispute. The text says 'then there will be dispute, therefore both must be known.'
Fasid means the contract is invalid and must be renegotiated with known terms or terminated.

Source Text

[1157) (2) نہیں صحیح ہے اجارہ یہاں تک کہ منافع معلوم ہوں اور اجرت معلوم ہو۔

From OCR: on page 183, before [1158] there is more text: "وما جاز ان يكون ثمنا في البيع جازان يكون اجرة في الاجارة" appears, but that belongs to matn (3). So the commentary on (2) ends with a hadith from Bayhaqi and the footnote. For completeness, we include here the full commentary on (2) as per OCR:]

اس حديث سے معلوم ہوا که جس کا اجرت پر رکھو اس کو اجرت معلوم هونی چاہئے ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اجرت معلوم ہو۔ اور عمل اور منافع معلوم ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک قال دعا النبي الله غلاما حجاما فحجمه وامر له بصاع او صاعين او مد او مدين وكلم فيه فخفف من ضريبته (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب من کلم موالی العبدان مخففوا عنه من خراجہ ص ۳۰۴ نمبر (۲۲۸) اس حدیث میں تجام ابو طیبہ کا عمل اور منافع معلوم ہے کہ ان کو حضور کی حجامت کرنی ہے اور اس کے بدلے میں ایک صاع یا دو صاع گیہوں دیا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ منفعت بھی معلوم ہوتب اجارہ صحیح ہوگا۔ اصول اصل قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو چیز بھی موجود نہ ہو بعد میں دی جائے یا آہستہ آہستہ وجود میں آئے گی اس کا کیل، وزن اور صفت معلوم ہو تب عقد ہوگا ۔ اجارہ میں منافع بعد میں آہستہ آہستہ وجود میں آئے گا اس لئے وہ معلوم ہوں تب اجارہ درست ہوگا ، ثبوت اس حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس ... فقال من اسلف في شيء ففي كيل معلوم ووزن معلوم الى اجل معلوم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب السلم فی وزن معلوم ص ۲۹۸ نمبر ۲۲۴۰ / مسلم شریف ، باب السلم ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۱۶۰۴) اس حدیث میں بیع سلم کے سلسلے میں ہے مگر اجرت کے معلوم ہونے کا بھی اندازہ ہوتا ہے۔
[1157) (2) Ijarah is not valid unless the benefits are known and the rent is known. Explanation: How many benefits will be, what their quantity will be, must be known, and the rent in exchange must be known; then ijarah will be valid. If the benefits are not known and the rent is not known, then there will be dispute, therefore both must be known. (2) In the above verse, 'eight years' is mentioned, from which the benefit is known, and 'marry' indicates that the consideration is also known. This indicates that both must be known. (3) In the hadith: From Abu Huraira from the Prophet: 'Whoever hires a worker, let him inform him of his wage' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter: Ijarah is not valid until the benefit is known and the wage is known, vol. 6, p. 198, no. 1165; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, etc.). Footnote: (c) It is narrated from the Prophet that whoever hires a worker should inform him of how much his wage is. Then: From this hadith it is known that when you hire someone, his wage must be known. And the proof that the work and benefit must be known is the hadith: From Anas ibn Malik: The Prophet called a slave who was a cupper, and he cupped him, and the Prophet ordered that he be given one or two sa‘s or one or two mudds, and spoke about him (i.e., the slave's tax) so that it was reduced (Bukhari, Chapter: Whoever speaks to the masters of slaves to reduce their tax, p. 304, no. 2280). In this hadith, the cupper Abū Taybah's work and benefit are known, i.e., he will perform cupping for the Prophet, and in exchange he was given one or two sa‘s of wheat. From this it is known that the benefit must be known for ijarah to be valid. The basic principle is: Whatever is not physically present now but will be delivered later or will come into existence gradually, its measure, weight, and description must be known for the contract to be valid. In ijarah, the benefit comes into existence gradually later, so it must be known for the contract to be valid. The proof is in the hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet said: 'Whoever gives a salaf (advance payment) in something, let it be in a known measure, known weight, and known term' (Bukhari, Chapter: Salaf in known weight, p. 298, no. 2240; Muslim, Chapter: Salaf, p. 131, no. 1604). This hadith is about salam sale, but it indicates the necessity of specification for the rent as well.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, stating a key condition for the validity of ijarah: both the benefit (manfa‘ah) and the rent (ujrah) must be known (ma‘lūm). The author explains that ignorance of either leads to disputes, so specification is necessary. The proofs include: (1) the Quranic verse specifying 'eight years', indicating the duration (and thus the benefit) was known, and the marriage indicating the consideration; (2) a hadith from Bayhaqi that the hirer must inform the worker of his wage; (3) the hadith of the cupper where the benefit (cupping) and the wage (a known measure of wheat) were both specified; (4) a general principle derived from the hadith on salam (advance sale) that things which are not present must be described in measure, weight, and term. The commentary emphasizes that since ijarah involves future benefits, they must be described clearly to avoid gharar (uncertainty).

Key Terms
منفعت معلوم (manfa‘ah ma‘lūmah): Known benefit – the benefit being contracted must be specified in terms of type, quantity, duration, etc.
اجرت معلوم (ujrah ma‘lūmah): Known rent – the compensation must be specified in amount and type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what happens if the benefit or rent is not known in an ijarah contract?
A) The contract is valid but makruh
B) The contract is invalid (fasid) due to dispute potential
C) The contract is valid if the parties agree later
D) The contract is void (batil)

Key Takeaway
An ijarah contract is valid only if both the benefit and the rent are clearly known; otherwise it is fasid due to gharar.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

6 min
Conditions of Ijarah: Knowledge of Benefit and Rental
Ruling with proof on two conditions for valid ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a valid ijarah contract and explain how benefits become known according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In ijarah, both the benefit and the rental must be precisely known; uncertainty invalidates the contract.

Every valid contract requires clarity to avoid future disputes. In ijarah (hire/lease), the Hanafi school insists that both the benefit (manfa'ah) and the rental (ujrah) be known at the time of contract. This lesson explains these conditions and the methods by which benefit can be made known—through duration or through specific work. We will also see the proof from hadith and analogy to sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the opening sentence: 'المنافع معلومة والاجرة معلومة' — benefits and rental must be known. Note that these are conditions (shurut) for validity.
These conditions parallel the requirement in sale that the price and commodity be known.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author cites the principle that whatever can be a price in sale can be a rental in ijarah, and the hadith of the cupper where the Prophet specified the wage. Identify that the proof is based on analogy (qiyas) and ahad hadith.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut, but the ruling is strengthened by ijma.
3
Understand how benefits become known
The text gives two ways: (1) by duration (muddah), e.g., renting a house for a month; (2) by specifying the work (al-‘amal), e.g., hiring a tailor to sew a garment, or by specifying weight and distance for an animal.
Without such specification, the contract is fasid (defective).
4
Apply the conditions to examples
Consider cases: renting a car without stating the rental period or amount. The contract would be invalid because the benefit or rental is unknown. Contrast with a valid contract: 'I rent this car to you for one month for $500'.
The key is to eliminate gharar (uncertainty).
5
Note the consequence of ignorance
If either benefit or rental is unknown, the ijarah is fasid (defective) according to the Hanafi school. A fasid contract may still generate rights to rental for the portion used, but the contract is not binding beyond that.
This nuance is important for dispute resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثاني 178 كتاب الاجارة 1 المنافع معلومة والاجرة معلومة [1158] ((3) وما جاز ان يكون ثمنا في البيع جازان يكون اجرة في الاجارة [1159] (4) والمنافع تارة تصير معلومة بالمدة كاستيجار الدور للسكنى والارضين للزراعة فيصح العقد على مدة معلومة اى مدة كانت[1160] (5) وتارة تصير معلومة بالعمل والتسمية كمن استأجر رجلا على صبغ ثوب او خياطة ثوب او استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها مقدارا معلوما الى موضع معلوم او يركبها مسافة معلومة۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Two, page 178, Book of Ijarah: 1) The benefits are known and the rental is known. [1158] (3) Whatever is permissible to be a price (thaman) in sale is permissible to be a rental (ujrah) in ijarah. [1159] (4) And benefits sometimes become known by duration, like renting houses for residence and lands for cultivation, so the contract is valid upon a known duration, whatever duration it may be. [1160] (5) And sometimes they become known by work and specification, like hiring a man to dye a garment or sew a garment, or hiring an animal to carry a known quantity to a known place, or to ride it a known distance.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri presents the foundational conditions for a valid ijarah (hire/lease) contract in the Hanafi school. The author states two core rulings: First, both the benefit (manfa'ah) to be received and the rental payment (ujrah) must be known (ma'lumah). Second, whatever can serve as a price (thaman) in a sale can also serve as rental in ijarah, establishing a parallel between sale and hire transactions. The passage then explains two methods by which benefits become known: (a) by specifying the duration (e.g., renting a house for a specific number of months or land for a season), and (b) by specifying the work (e.g., hiring a tailor to sew a garment) or by specifying the task and distance (e.g., hiring an animal to carry a known weight to a known location or to ride a known distance). The author provides hadith evidence (though the Arabic text quote is not fully reproduced here; the commentary mentions hadith from Anas ibn Malik and others). The key point is that uncertainty (gharar) in either the benefit or the rental invalidates the contract. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the benefit, though non-existent at the time of contract, must be precisely defined to avoid dispute.

Key Terms
المنافع (al-manafi'): The usufruct or benefit derived from an asset or service in an ijarah contract.
الاجرة (al-ujrah): The rental payment or wage in an ijarah contract.
ثمن (thaman): Price or consideration in a sale contract; analogically applied to rental in ijarah.
مدة معلومة (muddah ma'lumah): A specified duration that determines the extent of benefit in ijarah for leases of properties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for an ijarah contract to be valid?
A) The benefit and the rental must be known.
B) Only the rental must be known, the benefit can be vague.
C) The asset must be present at the time of contract.
D) The rental must be in gold or silver.

Key Takeaway
For a valid ijarah, both the benefit and the rental must be precisely known; otherwise the contract is fasid.

Making Manafi' Known in Ijarah: Work and Specification
Explaining how manafi' become known through specifying work and naming the wage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods for making manafi' known in Hanafi ijarah (by work and naming, and by specifying load/place/distance) and apply them to determine the validity of an ijarah contract.

Core Idea
In Hanafi ijarah, benefit must be known; specify the work and the wage.

The validity of an ijarah contract hinges on the benefit (manfa'ah) being known to both parties. Uncertainty (gharar) in the benefit renders the contract fasid. This lesson unpacks the first method of achieving this knowledge: specifying the work and the wage, as presented in the classical Hanafi texts. You will see how the fuqaha derived this rule from the sunnah and how it applies to everyday hiring situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi rule: the benefit in ijarah must be known (ma'lum) for the contract to be sahih. If the benefit is unknown, the contract is fasid due to gharar.
2
Recognize the Methods Mentioned
The author states that benefit can become known by 'work and naming' (al-'amal wa al-tasmiyah) — i.e., specifying the exact work and the exact wage. Also by specifying the load, place, or distance for animal hire.
The commentary adds another method: ta'yin (specification by pointing).
3
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
The hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij is cited: the Prophet forbade renting land generally but allowed it when the rent is in gold or silver (i.e., specified). This implies that specifying the rent makes the benefit known. Also the Khaybar hadith and the story of Ali drawing water are used.
Understand wajh al-dalalah: the prohibition is removed when the rent is known, indicating knowledge of rent removes gharar.
4
Apply the Rule to Examples
Work through the examples: hiring a tailor to sew a specific garment, or hiring a beast of burden to carry a known weight to a known place. In each, the benefit is known because the work and wage are specified.
Note that the wage must also be known; it is part of the naming.
5
Distinguish from Invalid Specifications
If the contract leaves the work unspecified (e.g., 'work for a day' without specifying the task), the benefit is unknown and the contract is fasid. This is the common error: thinking only duration suffices.
The mufta bihi position is that both the work and the wage must be ma'lum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارة
للسكنى والارضين للزراعة فيصح العقد على مدة معلومة اى مدة كانت[١١٦٠] (۵) وتارة تصير معلومة بالعمل والتسمية كمن استأجر رجلا على صبغ ثوب او خياطة ثوب او استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها مقدارا معلوما الى موضع معلوم او يركبها مسافة
زمین کا شتکاری کے لئے دے جس سے منافع کا پتہ چلے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ انه سال رافع بن خديج عن كراء الارض فقال نهى رسول الله لال له عن كراء الارض قال فقلت أبا لذهب والورق ؟ فقال اما بالذهب والورق فلابأس به (الف) (مسلم شریف، باب كراء الارض بالذهب والورق ص ۱۱ نمبر ۱۵۴۷) عن ابن عمران رسول الله الله عامل اهل خیبر بشطر ما يخرج منها من ثمر او زرع (مسلم شريف، باب المساقات والمعاملة بجزء من الثمر والزرع ، ص ۱۴ نمبر ۱۵۴۸ ر بخاری شریف ، باب اذالم يشترط السنين في المزارعة ص ۳۱۳ نمبر ۲۳۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اہل خیبر کو زمین کا شتکاری کے لئے دی گئی تھی ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقت معلوم ہو تو اس سے کرایہ کا پتہ چلتا ہے۔
[۱۱۲۰] (۵) منافع کبھی معلوم ہوتے ہیں عمل کے ذریعہ اور متعین کرنے کے ذریعہ جیسے کسی آدمی کو اجرت پر لیا کپڑا رنگنے کے لئے یا کپڑا سینے کے لئے یا چوپایہ اجرت پر لیا تا کہ اس پر مقدار معلوم لا دا جائے مقام معلوم تک یا اس پر سوار ہو مسافت معلوم تک ۔ منافع معلوم ہونے کے مختلف طریقے ہیں۔ مصنف کچھ طریقے یہاں بیان کر رہے ہیں۔ مثلا ایک طریقہ یہ ہے کہ کام متعین کر کے منفعت کی تعیین کی جائے۔ مثلا کپڑا رنگنے کے لئے آدمی کو اجرت پر لے کہ اتنی رقم دوں گا اور اس کے بدلے اتنے کپڑے رنگنے ہیں یا اتنے کپڑے سینے ہیں۔ یا چوپا یا جرت پر لے کہ اتنی رقم دوں گا اور اس پر دو سو کیلو گیہوں لاد کر پانچ میل لے جاؤں گا، یا پانچ میل تک سوار ہو کر سفر کروں گا تو ان تعیین کے ذریعہ سے منفعت کا پتہ چلا اور منفعت کی تعیین ہوئی۔ منفعت کی تعیین اور اجرت کی تعیین کی مثال حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال اصاب نبي الله خصاصة فبلغ ذلک علیا فخرج يلتمس عملا يصيب فيه شيئا ليقيت به رسول الله الا الله فاتى بستانا لرجل من اليهود فاستقى له سبعة عشر دلوا كل دلو بتمرة فخيره اليهودى من تمرة سبع عشرة عجوة فجاء بها الى النبي الله ( ب ) ( ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الرجل يستفى كل دلو بتمرة ويشترط جلدة ص۳۵۰ نمبر ۲۴۴۶) اس حدیث میں عمل بھی معلوم ہے اور اجرت بھی معلوم ہے کہ ہر ڈول نکالنے کے بدلے میں ایک کھجور طے کیا اور سترہ ڈول نکالا اور سترہ کھجور لئے۔
خیاطة : سینا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) رافع بن خدیج سے زمین کو کرایہ پر دینے کے بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا حضور نے زمین کو کرایہ پر دینے سے روکا۔ میں نے پو چھا سونے اور چاندی کے بدلے میں؟ فرمایا بہر حال سونے اور چاندی کے بدلے میں تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ب) حضور کو فاقہ کشی ہوئی تو یہ بات حضرت علی کو معلوم ہوئی تو کام کرنے کے لئے نکلے تا کہ کچھ کمائے جس سے حضور کو بچائے۔ پس حضرت علی یہودی کے ایک باغ میں آئے اور اس کے لئے سترہ ڈول نکالے ۔ ہر ڈول ایک کھجور کے بدلے۔ پس یہودی نے سترہ عجوہ کھجور دیئے پھر اس کو حضور کے پاس لیکر آئے۔
Book of Ijarah. For dwelling and lands for cultivation, the contract is valid for a known period, whatever the period may be. (5) And sometimes [benefits] become known by the work and naming, such as hiring a man to dye a garment or sew a garment, or hiring an animal to carry a known quantity to a known place, or to ride it a [known] distance. [Urdu: Give land for cultivation so that the benefits are known; its proof is this hadith:] That he asked Rafi' ibn Khadij about renting land, and he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ forbade renting land. He said: I said, 'Even for gold and silver?' He said, 'As for gold and silver, there is no harm in it.' (Muslim Sharif, Bab kira' al-ard bi al-dhahab wa al-wariq, p. 11 no. 1547) From Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ gave Khaybar to its people on half of what came out of its fruit and crops. (Muslim Sharif, Bab al-musaqat wa al-mu'amala bi juz' min al-thamar wa al-zar', p. 14 no. 1548 and Bukhari Sharif, Bab idha lam yashtarti al-sinin fi al-muzara'a, p. 313 no. 2329). In this hadith, the people of Khaybar were given land for cultivation. From it we learn that when the time is known, the rent is known. [1120] (5) Benefits are sometimes known by the work and by specification, like hiring a man to dye a garment or sew a garment, or hiring an animal so that a known load be carried on it to a known place, or to ride it for a known distance. There are different ways for benefits to be known. The author is mentioning some methods here. For example, one method is to specify the work and thereby specify the benefit. For instance, hire a man to dye garments, saying, 'I will give such amount, and for that you are to dye so many garments' or 'sew so many garments.' Or hire an animal saying, 'I will give such amount, and on it I will load 200 kg of wheat and carry it five miles, or ride it for five miles.' By such specification, the benefit becomes clear and is specified. An example of specifying the benefit and the wage is found in the hadith: From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet of Allah ﷺ experienced hunger, and that reached Ali, so he went out seeking work to earn something with which to help the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. He came to a garden owned by a Jewish man, and he drew seventeen buckets of water for him, each bucket for a date. The Jew gave him a choice of seventeen 'ajwa dates. So he brought them to the Prophet ﷺ. (Ibn Majah Sharif, Bab al-rajul yastaqi kullu dalw bi tamra wa yashtari jildatahu, p. 350 no. 2446). In this hadith, both the work and the wage were known: for each bucket drawn, one date was agreed; he drew seventeen buckets and took seventeen dates. Khayata: sewing. Footnote: (a) When asked about renting out land, Rafi' said the Prophet forbade it. I asked: 'In exchange for gold and silver?' He said: 'In exchange for gold and silver, there is no harm.' (b) The Prophet experienced hunger, and that reached Ali, so he went out seeking work to earn something with which to protect the Prophet. So Ali came to a Jewish man's garden and drew seventeen buckets for him, each bucket for a date. The Jew gave him seventeen 'ajwa dates, and he brought them to the Prophet.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh discusses the requirement that the benefit (manfa'ah) in an ijarah contract must be known (ma'lum) to ensure the contract is free from gharar (uncertainty). The author lists two methods: (1) by specifying the work and the wage (al-'amal wa al-tasmiyah), and (2) by specification and pointing (al-ta'yin wa al-isharah) — here only the first is elaborated. Examples include hiring a person to dye or sew a specific garment, or hiring an animal to carry a known load to a known place. The proofs provided are hadiths: the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij shows that renting land for gold and silver (specified rent) is permitted, implying the benefit is known; the hadith of Khaybar shows a sharecropping arrangement with known terms; and the story of Ali and the Jew demonstrates a clear agreement on work per bucket and wage per bucket. The commentary emphasizes that both the work and the wage must be specified for the benefit to be ma'lum.

Key Terms
منافع (manafi'): The benefits (plural of manfa'ah) that are the subject matter of ijarah; must be known for validity.
اجارة (ijarah): A contract for the exchange of known benefit for known compensation.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the exact item or service, e.g., 'this food' or 'this garment'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi ijarah, which of the following is NOT a valid way to make the benefit known?
A) Specifying the work (e.g., dyeing a garment) and the wage.
B) Hiring an animal to carry a known load to a known place.
C) Leaving the work unspecified but paying a fixed daily wage.
D) Pointing to the specific food to be transported.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, the benefit must be ma'lum (known) through specification of work and wage; otherwise the contract is fasid due to gharar.

Making Benefits Known by Specification and Pointing
Explaining how benefits are rendered known through direct specification and pointing to the subject matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how benefits are made known in ijarah through ta'yin and isharah, and cite the Hanafi proof from the athar.

Core Idea
Pointing to the subject matter and agreeing on the wage makes the benefit known and the contract valid.

In ijarah (lease/hire contracts), the benefit must be clearly known to avoid gharar (uncertainty). One method is by directly specifying and pointing to the subject matter, as illustrated by the example of hiring to transport 'this food.' This lesson examines the ruling and the proof from the practice of al-Hasan al-Basri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second method
The passage introduces ta'yin (specification) and isharah (pointing) as a way to make the benefit known. Understand that this applies to the subject matter itself, not just the duration.
2
Analyze the example
The example: hiring a man to transport 'this food' to a known place. The phrase 'this food' points to a specific existing item, making the subject matter of transport determined.
Pointing can be physical or verbal description when the object is present.
3
State the ruling
The ruling: the contract is sahih (valid) because the benefit is made known, thus gharar is eliminated.
This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle of avoiding jahalah (ignorance) in contracts.
4
Examine the dalil
The proof is an athar from al-Hasan al-Basri, who hired a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mirdas. He asked the price, was told 'two daniqs,' and then rode it. The donkey was pointed to (present), and the wage was known.
This athar is recorded in Bukhari and is considered evidence for the validity of such specification.
5
Determine the wajh al-dalalah
The connection: the benefit (riding the donkey) was made known by the presence of the donkey (pointing) and the agreed wage. The act of hiring without further description suffices when the item is specified.
This shows that the benefit (manfa'ah) is determined by the specific object and the known consideration.

Commentary
This passage presents the second method of making the benefit known in ijarah: specification and pointing (al-ta'yin wa al-isharah). The author gives an example: hiring a person to transport 'this food' to a known destination. The phrase 'this food' (hadha al-ta'am) points to a specific existing item, making the subject matter of transport known. The commentary adds that one can hire someone to load this food and take it to a specific place for a specified wage. The proof provided is an athar (effect) from al-Hasan al-Basri, who hired a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mirdas for two daniqs after specifying the ride. This shows that pointing to the animal and agreeing on a known wage is valid. The lesson emphasizes that direct specification or pointing to the object of the contract (e.g., 'this animal', 'this food') eliminates uncertainty.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the exact object or service, e.g., 'this food'.
اشارة (isharah): Pointing to the object of the contract, e.g., pointing to a specific donkey or food.

Permissible Uses in Rented Premises: The Harm Principle
Ruling on permissible uses with proof from the harm principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for permissible uses in a rented house/shop and identify which specific activities are prohibited according to the Hanafi school, citing the underlying proof.

Core Idea
A tenant may use a property for any purpose except those causing structural harm – the three trades are classic examples.

When renting a house or shop for residence, the contract may be silent on the specific use. Hanafi fiqh gives the tenant broad discretion, but with a critical limit: no activity that damages the property. This lesson explores that limit through three prohibited trades (blacksmithing, laundering, milling) and the Prophetic principle that prohibits harm.

Guided Path
1
State the default rule
The passage begins: it is permissible to rent houses and shops for residence even without specifying the use. The tenant may do any work except the three listed.
The default is broad permission; restrictions are exceptional and based on harm.
2
Identify the three prohibited trades
They are blacksmithing (al-haddad), laundering (al-qassar), and milling (al-tahhan). These are explicitly excluded from the general permission.
Memorise the Arabic terms: الحداد, القصار, الطحان
3
Explain the reasons for prohibition
Blacksmithing weakens walls, laundering damages floors with water, milling dirties floors and also weakens walls. The unifying feature is structural harm.
The harm can be to walls or floors, or both.
4
Connect to the legal proof
The hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' (لا ضرر ولا ضرار) is cited. It prohibits causing harm in general. Applying it here, any activity that harms the property is not allowed without the owner's consent.
The proof is a hadith, which is zanni in transmission but strong in meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is permissible to rent houses and shops for residence, even if he does not specify what he will do in them. And he may do everything except blacksmithing, laundering, and milling. [Urdu:] (7) And it is permissible to rent houses and shops for residence, even if he does not state what he will do in them. And the hireling is permitted to do every work in them except blacksmithing, laundering, and milling. Explanation: Renting houses and shops is permissible, and one can do all kinds of work in them, but one cannot do blacksmithing, laundry, and flour milling. If it is not previously agreed what work will be done, one can do all work that does not damage the walls or floor of the house. But work that can damage the walls or floor cannot be done without the owner's permission. For example, blacksmithing weakens the walls, laundry damages the floor, and flour milling dirties the floor and also weakens the walls. So one cannot do these works without the owner's permission. In short, without permission, one cannot do any work that damages the walls or floor. The proof is the hadith: 'No harm and no reciprocating harm.' Al-haddad: blacksmithing. Al-qassar: laundry profession. Al-tahhan: milling.

Commentary
This passage rules on renting houses and shops for residence. The tenant is allowed to use the property for any purpose that does not cause damage, unless the contract specifies otherwise. Three activities are explicitly prohibited because they cause harm to the structure: blacksmithing (haddadi), laundry (qassari), and milling (tahhan). The commentary elaborates that blacksmithing shakes walls, laundry damages floors, and milling dirties and weakens both. The underlying principle is the hadith 'la darar wa la dirar' (no harm and no reciprocating harm). The lesson underscores that the default permission is broad, but any activity causing physical damage is not allowed without the owner's consent.

Key Terms
الحداد (al-haddad): Blacksmithing; a profession that involves hammering and can weaken walls.
القصار (al-qassar): Laundering; washing clothes that can damage floors due to water.
الطحان (al-tahhan): Milling; grinding grains that can dirty and weaken floors and walls.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The tenant's use is limited by the principle of no harm: the classic prohibitions are blacksmithing, laundering, and milling, but any damaging activity is similarly forbidden.

Renting Land for Cultivation: Automatic Ancillary Rights
Ruling on renting land for farming and the lessee's rights to water and path.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on renting land for cultivation and explain the legal basis for the automatic inclusion of the lessee's rights to water and access.

Core Idea
The lessee of farmland automatically gets water rights and access, even without stipulation.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri presents a straightforward but essential rule in Hanafi mu'amalat: the validity of agricultural land leases and the implied rights necessary for cultivation. Understanding these default terms prevents disputes and ensures the contract fulfills its purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal act being discussed (renting land for cultivation) and its hukm (valid/jai'iz). Note that the text uses 'يجوز' indicating permissibility and validity.
In Hanafi fiqh, a contract that is 'ja'iz' is valid and legally binding.
2
Recognize the ancillary rights
List the two rights explicitly mentioned: the right to water (al-shurb) for irrigation and the right of way (al-tariq) to access the land. Understand that these are automatically included even if not stipulated.
These rights are considered 'taba'' (subsidiary) and necessary to achieve the purpose of cultivation.
3
Understand the legal basis
Appreciate that these rights are derived from custom (urf) and necessity (darurah). The Hanafi school implies them into the contract to avoid hardship and fulfill the contract's objective.
Some schools require explicit stipulation, but Hanafis rely on custom and the principle of 'al-urf muhakkam' (custom is authoritative).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز استيجار الاراضى للزراعة و للمستأجر الشرب والطريق وان لم يشترط.

And it is permissible to rent lands for cultivation, and the lessee has the right to water and path even if not stipulated. [Urdu:] (8) And it is permissible to rent lands for farming. And the lessee will have the right to water for irrigation and the right of way, even if he did not stipulate it.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This short passage states two rulings concerning renting agricultural land. First, it is valid (ja'iz) to rent land for cultivation. Second, the lessee (musta'jir) automatically acquires the right to use water for irrigation (shurb) and the right of passage (tariq) to access the land, even if these rights were not explicitly mentioned in the contract. This is because these are necessary ancillary rights (taba') without which the primary purpose of cultivation cannot be achieved. The Hanafi school views these as inherent to the lease contract for agricultural land, based on custom and necessity. No explicit proof is cited in this text, but it is derived from general principles of permissibility and custom.

Key Terms
الشرب (al-shurb): The right to use water for irrigation of the rented land.
الطريق (al-tariq): The right of way to access the rented land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The right to build permanent structures.
D) The right to change the crop type without permission.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the lessee of farmland is entitled to water and access by default, as these are integral to the land's use.

Leasing Land for Cultivation and Implied Rights
Ruling on leasing agricultural land with implicit rights to irrigation and pathway

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing agricultural land and identify the implied rights of irrigation (shurb) and pathway (tariq) that are automatically included without stipulation.

Core Idea
Leasing land for cultivation is permissible; the lessee automatically acquires rights to water and access without stipulation.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on leasing agricultural land, addressing a common confusion: some hadiths appear to discourage leasing, but the school interprets them as recommendations to give land freely, not prohibitions. The text establishes that the lessee’s rights to irrigation and a pathway are inherent to the contract, as these are essential for cultivation. The proofs are drawn from the practice of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) at Khaybar and the hadith of Ibn Abbas (رضي الله عنه).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Leasing land (istījār al-arāḍī) for cultivation. The ruling is permissibility (jawāz / ibāḥa).
The text states 'ويجوز' – it is permissible.
2
Locate the dalīl (evidence)
Two main proofs: (1) The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) did not forbid leasing, as reported by Ibn Abbas; (2) The contract of Khaybar where land was leased for a share of the produce.
These are found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah (manner of proof)
The hadith 'لم ينه عنه' (he did not forbid it) indicates permissibility; the statement 'أن يمنح أحدكم أخاه خير له' (that one give to his brother freely is better) implies that taking rent is less virtuous but not prohibited.
The phrase 'خير له' (better for him) does not make the alternative impermissible.
4
Note the ikhtilāf (disagreement)
Some early authorities discouraged leasing land for fixed rent, preferring sharecropping or free lending. The Hanafi school responds that the discouragement was advisory (istihbāb), not a prohibition.
The thamarah al-khilāf: Hanafis allow fixed rental leases; others may restrict to sharecropping (muzāra‘ah).
5
Extract the implied rights
The text explicitly states that the lessee has the right to shurb (irrigation) and tarīq (pathway) even if not stipulated, because these are essential (ḍarūrī) for cultivation.
This is based on 'urf (custom) and necessity, not on explicit mention.

Source Text

It is permissible to lease lands for cultivation, and the lessee has the right to irrigation and pathway even if not stipulated.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the permissibility of leasing agricultural land. The author states that the lessee automatically enjoys rights to irrigation (shurb) and pathway (tariq) without explicit stipulation, as these are essential for cultivation. The commentary addresses a historical confusion: some hadiths might suggest prohibition, but they are interpreted as recommendation to give land free. The proofs are from Ibn Abbas (showing permissibility) and the contract of Khaybar (the Prophet leased land for half the produce). Thus, Hanafi law considers leasing land for a fixed rental valid, with necessary ancillary rights implied by custom (urf) and necessity (darura).

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): Irrigation right; the lessee's entitlement to water the crops from available sources.
طريق (ṭarīq): Pathway; right of access to the land for cultivation purposes.

Key Takeaway
Leasing land for cultivation is permissible (mubah) in Hanafi fiqh, and the lessee's rights to irrigation (shurb) and pathway (tariq) are automatically included without need for stipulation.

Condition for Validity: Specifying the Crop in Land Lease
Condition that the crop type must be specified for land lease validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for validity of an agricultural land lease and apply it to distinguish valid from invalid contracts.

Core Idea
A land lease for cultivation is invalid unless the crop is specified or the lessor gives general permission.

This passage establishes a key condition for the validity of ijara (lease) of agricultural land. Without specification of the crop type, the contract suffers from gharar (uncertainty) and may harm the land's fertility. The Hanafi school requires either naming the crop or a general permission from the lessor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize that the passage discusses ijara (lease) of land for cultivation purposes.
This is a special type of ijara where the subject is the usufruct of land for agriculture.
2
State the Default Ruling
Without meeting the condition, the contract is fasid (voidable).
Fasid means the contract is deficient and requires correction.
3
Identify the Condition
The crop to be sown must be specified. This removes uncertainty about what will be planted.
4
Identify the Alternative
If the lessor says 'sow whatever you wish', the contract becomes valid because the lessee has full discretion.
General permission eliminates gharar, as the lessor accepts any crop.
5
Understand the Wisdom
Different crops affect soil differently; specifying prevents disputes and protects land fertility.
This shows Hanafi fiqh's concern for practical consequences and equity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصح العقد حتى يسمى ما يزرع فيها او يقول على ان يزرع فيها ما شاء زمین کرایہ پر لیتے وقت یہ بھی طے کرنا ہوگا کہ کیا چیز اس میں بوئے گا تاکہ بعد میں جھگڑا نہ ہو۔ یا کھیت والا یہ کہہ دے جو چیزیں چاہیں آپ اس میں بوئیں تو کچھ بھی ہوسکتا ہے۔ بعض غلے کے بونے سے زمین خراب ہوتی ہے اور بعض غلے کے ہونے سے زمین اچھی ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اجرت پر لیتے وقت یہ طے کرنا ہو گا کہ کون ساغلہ اس میں بوئے گا۔ یا پھر کھیت والا یہ کہہ دے کہ جو غلہ چاہو بوؤ۔ پھر عقد اجارہ درست ہوگا۔
The contract is not valid until it is specified what will be sown in it, or he says 'on the condition that he sows whatever he wishes'.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This is a ruling statement establishing a condition for the validity of a land lease for cultivation. The contract is invalid (ghayr sahih) unless the type of crop is named, or the lessor gives general permission to sow anything. The commentary provides the reasoning: different crops affect the soil differently—some exhaust, some enrich. To avoid dispute, the crop must be specified. If the lessor says 'sow whatever you wish', the contract becomes valid because the lessee has freedom. This condition protects both parties: the lessor knows the impact on his land, and the lessee knows his obligations.

Key Terms
يسمى ما يزرع (yusamma mā yuzra‘): Specifying the type of crop to be sown; a condition for validity of agricultural land lease.

Leasing Vacant Land for Building or Planting Trees
Ruling on leasing vacant land for construction or permanent planting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing vacant land for building or planting trees and explain the qiyas used to justify it.

Core Idea
Leasing vacant land for building or planting trees is permissible by qiyas on cultivation lease.

This lesson addresses a common question: can one lease a vacant piece of land to build a house or plant trees? The Hanafi school permits it, drawing an analogy to the well-established permission for cultivation leases. We will explore the ruling, its basis in qiyas, and the supporting hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being leased? Vacant land. For what purpose? Building or planting trees. Ruling: permissible (mubah).
Hukm level is mubah due to general permissibility of ijarah.
2
Understand the qiyas
Compare to short-term cultivation lease (asl). Find common illa: utilization of land for beneficial purpose.
Illa is jaliyyah: both involve using land productively.
3
Support from hadith
Hadith of Ibn Abbas and Khaybar show general permissibility of leasing land. The Prophet did not prohibit it.
These hadiths establish the asl.
4
Address objections
Objection: building and tree planting imply permanence beyond the lease term. Hanafi response: the lease term is fixed; structures can be removed or compensated at end of term, similar to cultivation.
The lease does not transfer ownership of land; only usufruct for a fixed period.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in Hanafi law: leasing vacant land for building or planting trees is permissible provided the term and rent are fixed.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

This is a ruling statement extending the permissibility of leasing land to non-agricultural purposes like construction or planting trees. The commentary uses qiyas: if leasing for short-term cultivation is allowed, then for long-term building or permanent planting is also allowed, albeit for a longer period. The footnote supports the general permissibility of leasing land from the hadith of Khaybar and Ibn Abbas. Hanafi law treats such leases as valid ijarah contracts, provided the term and rent are fixed. The lessee acquires temporary ownership of the usufruct, i.e., the right to use the space for building or planting during the lease term.

Key Terms
ساحة (sāḥa): Vacant piece of land; open space suitable for building or planting.

Specifying Crop in Land Lease
Stating the condition of specifying crop in land lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for a valid land lease for cultivation and distinguish between specifying the crop and receiving general permission.

Core Idea
A land lease contract is invalid unless the crop is specified or the lessor grants general permission.

In this lesson, we examine a key condition for the validity of a land lease (ijarah al-ard) for cultivation. The Hanafi school requires that the contract specify what crop will be grown to prevent future disputes. Alternatively, the lessor may give blanket permission. Understanding this requirement ensures that the lease is free from ambiguity (gharar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its context
Recognize that this ruling applies to a lease of land for agricultural use (ijarah). The contract is between a lessor (owner) and a lessee (farmer).
The same principles may apply to other leases where the usage is specified.
2
Understand the condition for validity
The passage states that the contract is not valid (batil) until either (1) the crop to be grown is explicitly named, or (2) the lessor says 'on condition that he plants whatever he wishes' — i.e., gives the lessee full discretion.
This prevents future disagreement about what crop was intended.
3
Analyze the reason behind the condition
The commentary explains that different crops affect the soil differently; some improve it, others degrade it. Without specification, disputes over rent and land condition can arise.
This is a form of gharar (uncertainty) that Hanafi fiqh seeks to eliminate.
4
Distinguish the two valid scenarios
Scenario A: The contract names a specific crop (e.g., wheat). Scenario B: The contract grants general permission (e.g., 'plant whatever you want'). Both are valid, but the crop must be either specified or the lessor must waive specification.
If the lessor says 'plant whatever you wish,' no further specification is needed.
5
Apply the ruling to practical contracts
When drafting or reviewing a land lease, ensure one of the two conditions is met. If neither is present, the contract is invalid (batil) and must be rectified.
This is a condition of validity (shart al-sihha), not a pillar (rukn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[14] (۹) ولا يصح العقد حتى يسمى ما يزرع فيها او يقول على ان يزرع فيها ما شاء 
 زمین کرایہ پر لیتے وقت یہ بھی طے کرنا ہوگا کہ کیا چیز اس میں بوئے گا تاکہ بعد میں جھگڑا نہ ہو۔ یا کھیت والا یہ کہہ دے جو چیزیں چاہیں آپ اس میں بوئیں تو کچھ بھی ہوسکتا ہے۔ بعض غلے کے بونے سے زمین خراب ہوتی ہے اور بعض غلے کے ہونے سے زمین اچھی ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اجرت پر لیتے وقت یہ طے کرنا ہو گا کہ کون ساغلہ اس میں بوئے گا۔ یا پھر کھیت والا یہ کہہ دے کہ جو غلہ چاہو بوؤ۔ پھر عقد اجارہ درست ہوگا۔
The contract is not valid until he specifies what he will plant in it, or he says: 'On the condition that he plants whatever he wishes.' When taking land on rent, it must be agreed what crop will be sown to prevent future dispute. Or the landowner may say: 'Sow whatever you wish.' Then the lease contract will be valid.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage states a condition for the validity of a land lease for cultivation. The Hanafi position is that the lease (ijarah) of agricultural land requires specification of the crop to be grown, or alternatively, the lessor may give general permission by saying 'plant whatever you wish.' The reason is that different crops affect the soil differently, and without specification, disputes may arise. If the lessor grants full discretion, the contract is valid even without naming a specific crop. This ruling prevents ambiguity (gharar) in the contract.

Key Terms
عقد (aqd): Contract, specifically the lease contract (ijarah) for land.
يسمى ما يزرع (yusamma ma yuzra'): Specifying what will be planted (the crop).
على ان يزرع فيها ما شاء (ala an yazra'a fiha ma sha'a): On condition that he plants whatever he wishes; general permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The land must be irrigated

Key Takeaway
A land lease for cultivation must identify the crop or include a general permission clause; otherwise, it is invalid in Hanafi fiqh.

Removing Constructions at Lease End
Ruling on obligation to remove buildings and trees after lease expiry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the lessee must remove buildings and trees upon lease expiry and explain the evidence and rationale.

Core Idea
Upon lease expiry, the lessee must demolish all structures and restore the land to its original empty condition.

In a lease of vacant land, what happens to buildings and trees the lessee has erected? The Hanafi school holds that they must be removed at the lessee's expense, even if the contract contained a condition to the contrary. This lesson examines the ruling, its rationale, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the obligation
The lease of land for cultivation or construction ends. The lessee is required to remove any buildings or trees he added and return the land empty.
2
Analyze the default rule and invalid condition
If the lease contract includes a condition that the structures remain, that condition is invalid because it causes loss (ḍarar) to one party without compensation.
3
Understand the harm-based rationale
The lessee would lose his investment without payment, or the landowner would bear removal costs. The principle is to prevent loss to either side.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' is cited. The Hanafi school interprets it as meaning conditions that are not harmful are binding; harmful conditions are void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶] (۱) فاذا انقضت مدة الاجارة لزمه ان يقلع البناء والغرس ويسلمها فارغة. 
 مثلا میں سال کے لئے خالی زمین اجرت پر لی تھی اور اس میں عمارت بنائی تھی یا درخت لگائے تھے تو ہمیں سال پورے ہونے کے بعد عمارت ختم کر دے اور درخت کاٹ لے اور جیسی خالی زمین کرایہ کے وقت لی تھی ویسی ہی بالکل خالی کر کے زمین والے کو حوالے کرے۔ (۱) اگر زمین پر عمارت یا درخت لگے رہنے کی شرط لگا دے تو اس میں اجیر کا نقصان ہوگا کہ بغیر کسی قیمت کے اس کو عمارت اور درخت چھوڑنا پڑ رہا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بھی درست نہیں۔ اور ایسا بھی ہوگا کہ اس عمارت اور درخت کی ضرورت نہ ہو تو اس کو اکھاڑنے اور ڈھانے میں کھیت والے کی رقم خرچ ہو گی جس سے کھیت والے کو نقصان ہوگا ۔ اس لئے قانون یہی ہوگا کہ جیسی خالی زمین کرایہ کے وقت لی تھی ویسی ہی خالی کر کے زمین واپس کرے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابی هریرة ان رسول الله قال المسلمون على شروطهم والصلح جائز بين المسلمين
So when the lease period ends, it becomes binding on him to remove the building and the plantation and to deliver it empty. For example, if I rented vacant land for a year and built a structure or planted trees, then after the year ends, I must demolish the building and cut down the trees, and return the land to its owner exactly as empty as it was taken. If he stipulates that the building or trees remain, then the lessee will suffer loss because he has to leave them without any compensation, so this is also not valid. Also, if the building or trees are not needed, their removal will cost the landowner, causing loss. Therefore, the rule is that the land must be returned empty as it was taken. Evidence for this is the hadith: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions, and reconciliation is permissible among Muslims.'
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage rules that when the lease term expires, the lessee is obligated (lazim) to demolish any buildings and uproot any trees he planted, and to return the land to the owner in its original empty condition. The author explains that even if the contract contained a condition allowing the structures to remain, it would be invalid because it causes loss to either party. The proof is the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions,' which implies that conditions that cause harm or lead to dispute are not binding. Thus, the default is that the land must be cleared. This ensures both parties' rights are protected.

Key Terms
يقلع (yaqla'): To uproot or demolish; removal of buildings and trees from the land.
لزمه (lazimah): It becomes binding/obligatory upon him.
فارغة (fāriġah): Empty; the land must be returned free of any structures or plants.
الصلح جائز (al-ṣulḥ jāʾiz): Reconciliation is permissible; part of the hadith allowing mutual agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Leave the buildings and trees for the owner
B) Remove the buildings and trees and return the land empty
C) Pay the owner for the value of the buildings
D) Extend the lease automatically

Key Takeaway
The lessee must clear the land of all additions at lease end; conditions to the contrary are invalid due to potential harm.

Ruling on Removal of Structures After Lease of Barren Land
Explains the obligation to remove buildings/trees and exceptions after lease ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of a lessee to remove structures and trees after lease expiry, cite the supporting proofs, and identify the valid exceptions that require mutual consent.

Core Idea
The lessee must return the land empty; removal is wajib unless both parties agree otherwise.

When a lease of barren land for building or planting expires, the lessee is obligated to restore the land to its original empty state. This lesson examines the legal ruling, its evidence from hadith and practice, and the exceptional scenarios where the landowner may compensate the lessee or both may agree to leave structures in place. Understanding this ruling ensures that the rights of both parties are respected and the contract is fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default obligation
The passage states that when the lease term ends, the lessee must uproot buildings and trees and deliver the land empty. This is a wajib (obligatory) duty arising from the contract.
The obligation applies even if the lessee built or planted with the landowner's permission.
2
Examine the proofs (dalil)
The author cites several proofs: (a) the practice of leasing barren land from year to year reported by Ibn Abbas, (b) the Khaybar incident where land was returned after lease, (c) the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' (Daraqutni), and (d) the hadith 'Property of a Muslim is not lawful except with his willing consent' (Daraqutni). Analyze how each supports the obligation to return the land empty.
The proofs are zanni in transmission and meaning, but collectively establish the ruling.
3
Understand the exceptions
Two exceptions are given where the landowner may choose not to require removal: (1) the landowner pays the value of the materials (as a separate sale), and (2) both parties agree to leave the structures as they are, with the building belonging to the lessee and the land to the owner. These exceptions require mutual consent and are considered new transactions, not part of the original lease.
The exceptions are based on the hadith permitting reconciliation (sulh) among Muslims.
4
Analyze the legal reasoning
The default rule protects the landowner's right to recover his property in full. Forcing the lessee to leave structures without compensation would violate his property rights (as per the consent hadith). The exceptions balance interests through voluntary agreement, avoiding prohibited conditional sales (bay' wa shart).
The Hanafi position emphasizes the contract's terms and mutual consent.

 ا الا ان يختار صاحب الارض ان يغرم له قيمة ذلك مقلوعا و يملكه
[۱۲۸ (۱۳) او يرضى بتركه على حاله فيكون البناء لهذا والارض لهذا. جس شرط پر زمین کرایہ پر دی گئی تھی اس شرط پر واپس کرے (۳) دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ بغیر ولی خوشی کے کسی کا مال لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الا الله قال لا يحل مال امرأ مسلم الا بطيب نفسه (الف) ( دار قطنی ، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۲۲ نمبر ۲۸۶۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغیر رضامندی کے کسی کا مال لینا جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے بغیر اجیر کی رضامندی کے اس کو گھریا درخت زمین پر چھوڑ دینے کے لئے کہنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
۱۱۹۷۱) (۱۲) مگر یہ کہ زمین والا پسند کرے کہ اکھڑے ہوئے کی قیمت دے اور گھر یا درخت کا مالک ہو جائے۔ تر زمین والا اس بات پر راضی ہو جائے کہ ٹوٹے ہوئے گھر اور ا کھڑے ہوئے درخت کی جو قیمت ہو سکتی ہے وہ اجیر کو دیدے اور گھر اور درخت کا مالک ہو جائے تو ایسا کر سکتا ہے۔

ات يغرم : تاوان دے۔ مقلوعا : قلع سے مشتق ہے اکھیڑنا۔
[۱۱۶۸] (۱۳) یا راضی ہو جائے چھوڑنے پر اپنی حالت پر ۔ پس عمارت کرایہ دار کے لئے اور زمین زمین والے کے لئے ہوگی۔ تشر کرایہ پر لینے کی مدت ختم ہو گئی ہے۔ اس لئے کرایہ دار کو گھر توڑنا چاہئے اور درخت کاٹنا چاہئے لیکن دونوں راضی ہو جائے کہ مزید زمانے کے لئے گھر اور درخت زمین پر چھوڑ دو تو ایسا کر سکتے ہیں۔ اس صورت میں زمین زمین والے کی رہے گی اور مکان یا درخت مکان یا درخت والے کے ہوں گے۔ یه از مین والے کی چیز ہے وہ راضی خوشی سے ایسا کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ بلکہ حدیث کی رو سے ایک قسم کا تعاون ہوگا اور بھائی کی مدد کرنے کا حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی مسلمان آدمی کا مال حلال نہیں ہے مگر اس کی خوش دلی سے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان اپنی شرط کے مطابق ہوتے ہیں یعنی شرط کے مطابق رہنا چاہئے اور مسلح مسلمانوں کے درمیان جائز ہے۔
Book of Ijarah. [6] (1) So when the lease period ends, it is obligatory upon him to uproot the building and the planting and to deliver it empty. Or for years fruit-bearing trees are planted. (2) The proof for leasing land for years is in hadith and athar. Ibn Abbas said: 'The best of what you do is that you lease barren land from year to year' (a) (Bukhari, Chapter on Leasing Land with Gold and Silver, p. 315, no. 2346). From this athar it is understood that one can lease barren land even for multiple years. (3) The Jews were given the land of Khaybar for multiple years. Later, in the time of Umar, they were expelled. From Ibn Umar that Umar ibn al-Khattab expelled the Jews and Christians from the land of Hijaz... and he intended to expel the Jews from it, so the Jews asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) regarding it, that they would tend to it and they would have half the fruit. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to them: 'We keep you on that as we wish.' So they remained until Umar expelled them to Tayma and Ariha (b) (Bukhari, Chapter on When the Owner of Land Says Leave the Land With You as Allah Has Left It with You and They Did Not Mention a Known Term, Then They Are on Their Mutual Consent, p. 314, no. 2338; Muslim, Chapter on Muzara'ah and Mu'amalah with a Share of Fruit and Crop, p. 14, no. 3967/155). From this hadith it is understood that the Jews of Khaybar were given the cultivation and date palm garden for many years in exchange for half the cultivation. From this it is understood that barren land can also be given for building and planting for many years. Lunt al-saha: barren land. Yaghris: to plant trees. [1126] (11) So when the lease period ends, it will be compulsory for him to remove the building and trees and deliver the land to the owner empty. For example, I leased barren land for a year and built a building or planted trees on it, after the year completes I must demolish the building and cut the trees, and return the land to the owner completely empty just as it was when leased. (1) If he stipulates that the building or trees remain on the land, then there will be loss to the hirer because without any compensation he has to leave the building and trees. Therefore this is also not correct. And it also happens that if he does not need this building and trees, then the landowner will incur expense in uprooting and demolishing them, causing loss to the landowner. Hence the rule is that he should return the land empty exactly as it was when leased. (2) There is proof of this in hadith. Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions, and reconciliation is permissible among Muslims' (c) (Daraqutni, Book of Sales, vol. 3, p. 23, no. 2867). From this hadith it is understood that... Footnote: (a) Ibn Abbas says: The best of what you do is that you lease barren land from one year to the next. (b) Umar ibn al-Khattab exiled Jews and Christians from the land of Hijaz. The Prophet intended to expel the Jews from Khaybar, so the Jews requested the Prophet to allow them to stay so they could cultivate, and for the people of Madinah half the fruit. The Prophet said: 'We keep you on that as we wish.' So they remained until Umar expelled them to Tayma and Ariha. (c) He said: Muslims are bound by their conditions, meaning they should abide by the condition, and reconciliation is permissible among Muslims. ... except that the landowner chooses to pay him the value of that uprooted thing and take ownership of it. [128] (13) Or he agrees to leave it as it is, so the building belongs to this one (the lessee) and the land belongs to this one (the owner). He should return it on the condition on which the land was leased. (3) In another hadith: 'The property of a Muslim is not lawful except with his willing consent.' From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The property of a Muslim man is not lawful except with his good pleasure' (a) (Daraqutni, Book of Sales, vol. 3, p. 22, no. 2862). From this hadith it is understood that taking someone's property without consent is not permissible. Therefore, it is not permissible to tell him to leave the building or trees on the land without the hirer's consent. 11971) (12) Except that the landowner chooses to pay the value of the uprooted thing and becomes the owner of the house or trees. That is, if the landowner agrees to give the hirer the value that the broken house and uprooted trees can have, and becomes the owner of the house and trees, then he can do so. It was necessary for the lessee of the land to break the house and clear the land. Similarly, it was necessary to cut the trees and clear the land. So understand that the house has been broken and the trees have been cut. Therefore the landowner will pay the value of the broken house and cut trees, and become the owner of the intact house and trees. This is a separate sale and purchase in which the consent of both the landowner and the lessee is necessary. Permission for this type of reconciliation is in the hadith. Abu Huraira said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions, and reconciliation is permissible among Muslims' (b) (Daraqutni, Book of Sales, vol. 3, p. 23, no. 2867). In this hadith it is that reconciliation between Muslims is permissible, so if they mutually agree on a price for the broken house and cut trees, it is permissible. This is not a sale within the lease that would become prohibited as a conditional sale. Because the lease matter was finalized many years ago, and the sale of the broken house is happening now, so it is not a conditional sale that would be invalid. At yaghram: pays compensation. Maqlu'an: derived from qala'a, to uproot. [1168] (13) Or he agrees to leave it in its current state. So the building belongs to the lessee and the land belongs to the landowner. That is, the lease period has ended. Therefore the lessee should break the house and cut the trees, but if both agree to leave the house and trees on the land for an extended period, they can do so. In this case, the land remains the property of the landowner, and the house or trees belong to the owner of the house or trees. This is the landowner's property, he can do so if he wishes with satisfaction. Rather, according to the hadith, this would be a type of cooperation and helping a brother. Footnote: (a) He said: The property of a Muslim man is not lawful except with his good pleasure. (b) He said: Muslims are bound by their conditions, meaning they should abide by the condition, and reconciliation is permissible among Muslims.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is from the Book of Ijarah (leasing) in the commentary (sharh) of a Hanafi text. The author explains the ruling when a lease of barren land (ard bayda) for the purpose of building or planting trees expires. The basic ruling is clear: the lessee must remove all structures and trees and return the land to its original empty state. This is wajib (obligatory) because the lease contract implies the land will be used temporarily and then restored. The author supports this with several proofs: (1) The practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with the Jews of Khaybar, who were given land for cultivation for multiple years but eventually expelled after Umar's time, showing that the land must be returned. (2) The hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions,' which means that if the lease contract specifies a period and return, it must be fulfilled. (3) The hadith 'The property of a Muslim is not lawful except with his willing consent,' which implies that the lessee cannot be forced to leave his property (e.g., a building he constructed) without compensation or consent. The passage then discusses two exceptions where the landowner may choose not to require removal: (a) The landowner can pay the lessee the value of the materials (e.g., broken bricks, cut timber) and take ownership of them. This is considered a separate sale, permissible because it is a new transaction with mutual consent. (b) Both parties can agree to leave the structures as they are, with the land belonging to the owner and the building/trees belonging to the lessee. This is also valid as a form of reconciliation (sulh) between Muslims. The author emphasizes that such agreements must be based on mutual consent and are not part of the original lease, thus avoiding the prohibition of combining a lease with a sale (bay' wa shart).

Key Terms
اجارة (ijarah): Leasing; a contract for usufruct of a property in exchange for rent. Here specifically lease of barren land for building or planting.
مدة الاجارة (muddah al-ijarah): The duration for which the land is leased.
يقلع البناء والغرس (yaqla' al-bina' wal-ghars): To uproot the building and planting; to remove structures and trees from the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a lease of barren land for building or planting expires, what is the default obligation of the lessee?
A) He may leave the buildings and trees with the landowner's permission.
B) He must remove all structures and trees and return the land empty.
C) He may claim compensation from the landowner for the buildings and trees.
D) He automatically becomes the owner of the buildings and trees.

Key Takeaway
A lessee of barren land must remove structures and trees at lease end, but both parties may mutually agree to alternative arrangements as separate transactions.
