Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
Options for Landowner After Lease Expiry
Ruling on landowner's right to pay for or keep tenant's constructions after lease expiry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to the landowner and tenant after lease expiry, apply the hadith proofs, and distinguish between forced removal and consensual settlement.

Core Idea
After lease expiry, the landowner may pay for the structures or both parties may agree to leave them.

When a lease ends, the tenant is obliged to remove his structures. However, the Hanafi school provides flexible options to avoid hardship, based on principles of mutual consent and amicable settlement. This lesson explores the rulings and the supporting hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default obligation
Recognize that after lease expiry, the tenant is normally required to demolish buildings and uproot trees to return the land empty.
This is the baseline ruling before considering any options.
2
Understand the landowner’s option to pay and own
The landowner may choose to pay the tenant the value of the structures as if they were demolished/up uprooted, and thereby own them.
This is a separate sale requiring the tenant’s consent.
3
Understand the alternative of mutual agreement to leave
Both parties may agree to leave the structures in place, with the building belonging to the tenant and the land to the landowner.
This is a form of settlement (sulh) permissible by hadith.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The hadith 'لا يحل مال امرئ مسلم' prohibits taking property without consent; 'المسلمون على شروطهم' validates conditions and settlements; 'لأن يمنح الرجل أخاه أرضه' encourages gratuitous permission.
These proofs establish the legal basis for the options.
5
Distinguish this from a sale within a lease
The payment option is a new, independent sale, not a condition of the original lease, so it avoids the prohibition of combining a sale and a lease in one contract.
This is important to prevent confusion with invalid transactions.

[۱۲۸ (۱۳) او يرضى بتركه على حاله فيكون البناء لهذا والارض لهذا. جس شرط پر زمین کرایہ پر دی گئی تھی اس شرط پر واپس کرے (۳) دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ بغیر ولی خوشی کے کسی کا مال لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الا الله قال لا يحل مال امرأ مسلم الا بطيب نفسه (الف) ( دار قطنی ، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۲۲ نمبر ۲۸۶۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغیر رضامندی کے کسی کا مال لینا جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے بغیر اجیر کی رضامندی کے اس کو گھریا درخت زمین پر چھوڑ دینے کے لئے کہنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
۱۱۹۷۱) (۱۲) مگر یہ کہ زمین والا پسند کرے کہ اکھڑے ہوئے کی قیمت دے اور گھر یا درخت کا مالک ہو جائے۔ تر زمین والا اس بات پر راضی ہو جائے کہ ٹوٹے ہوئے گھر اور ا کھڑے ہوئے درخت کی جو قیمت ہو سکتی ہے وہ اجیر کو دیدے اور گھر اور درخت کا مالک ہو جائے تو ایسا کر سکتا ہے۔
کرایہ پر زمین لینے والے پر گھر توڑ کر زمین خالی کرنا ضروری تھا۔ اسی طرح درخت کاٹ کر زمین خالی کرنا ضروری تھا اس لئے یوں سمجھو کہ گھر ٹوٹ چکا اور درخت کٹ چکے۔ اس لئے ٹوٹے ہوئے گھر کی قیمت اور کٹے ہوئے درخت کی قیمت جو ہوسکتی ہے وہ قیمت زمین والا دے گا اور سالم گھر اور سالم درخت کا مالک بن جائے گا۔ یہ الگ سے بیع اور شراء ہے جس میں کھیت والا اور کرایہ پر لینے والے دونوں کی رضامندی ضروری ہے۔ اس قسم کے صلح کی گنجائش حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله المسلمون على شروطهم والصلح جائز بين المسلمين (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۲۳ نمبر ۲۸۶۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مسلمان کے درمیان صلح کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے ٹوٹے ہوئے گھر اور کٹے ہوئے درخت پر آپس میں صلح کی قیمت ہو جائے تو جائز ہے۔ یہ پہلے کرایہ کے اندر بیع نہیں ہے کہ بیع کے اندر بیج ہو کرنا جائز ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ کرایہ کی بات تو کئی سال پہلے ہو چکی تھی اور ٹوٹے ہوئے گھر کی بیع ابھی ہو رہی ہے اس لئے بیع و شرط نہیں ہوئی کہ نا جائز ہو جائے۔
ات يغرم : تاوان دے۔ مقلوعا : قلع سے مشتق ہے اکھیڑنا۔
[۱۱۶۸] (۱۳) یا راضی ہو جائے چھوڑنے پر اپنی حالت پر ۔ پس عمارت کرایہ دار کے لئے اور زمین زمین والے کے لئے ہوگی۔ تشر کرایہ پر لینے کی مدت ختم ہو گئی ہے۔ اس لئے کرایہ دار کو گھر توڑنا چاہئے اور درخت کاٹنا چاہئے لیکن دونوں راضی ہو جائے کہ مزید زمانے کے لئے گھر اور درخت زمین پر چھوڑ دو تو ایسا کر سکتے ہیں۔ اس صورت میں زمین زمین والے کی رہے گی اور مکان یا درخت مکان یا درخت والے کے ہوں گے۔ یه از مین والے کی چیز ہے وہ راضی خوشی سے ایسا کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ بلکہ حدیث کی رو سے ایک قسم کا تعاون ہوگا اور بھائی کی مدد کرنے کا
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی مسلمان آدمی کا مال حلال نہیں ہے مگر اس کی خوش دلی سے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان اپنی شرط کے مطابق ہوتے ہیں یعنی شرط کے مطابق رہنا چاہئے اور مسلح مسلمانوں کے درمیان جائز ہے۔
عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله الا الله قال لان يمنح الرجل اخاه ارضه خير له من ان يأخذ عليها خرجا معلوما (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب الارض شيخ ص ۱۴ نمبر ۱۵۵۰ر بخاری شریف، باب ما کان من اصحاب النبي الله يواسى معهم في الزراعة. والنمر ص ۳۱۵ نمبر ۲۳۴۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بغیر کرایہ کے زمین کسی بھائی کو دے تو بہت بہتر ہے۔ اس لئے اپنی زمین بغیر کرایہ کے گھر والے یا مکان والے کو دے سکتا ہے، ثواب ملے گا۔
Book of Ijarah. Except if the landowner chooses to pay the value of uprooted and own it, or he agrees to leave it as is, so the building is for this one and the land for that one. [Commentary: The land was rented on a condition; it must be returned on that condition. Another hadith: It is not permissible to take a Muslim's wealth without his consent. From Anas that the Prophet said: 'The wealth of a Muslim is not lawful except with his own pleasure.' This shows that without the consent of the hirer, it is not permissible to tell him to leave the house/trees on the land. Rather, if the landowner wishes, he may give the value of the uprooted and become owner of the house/trees. Or if he agrees to leave them, then the building is for the hirer and the land for the owner. The hirer was required to demolish the house and cut the trees, so it is as if the house is demolished and trees cut. The landowner will pay the value and become owner. This is a separate sale requiring both parties' consent. Permission for such settlement is in the hadith: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions, and settlement between Muslims is permissible.' So settlement on the value of demolished house and cut trees is permissible. This is not a sale within a lease. Then hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'For a man to give his land to his brother is better than taking a fixed rent.' So giving land without rent is better and earns reward.]
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samiri discusses the options available to the landowner and tenant after the lease of land expires, when the tenant has constructed buildings or planted trees on the land. The original ruling states that the landowner may either pay the tenant the value of the structures/trees as if they were uprooted/cut, and thereby own them, or both parties may agree to leave the structures/trees in place, with the building belonging to the tenant and the land to the owner. The commentator explains that since the lease is over, the tenant is obliged to remove his structures, but the law does not force him to do so without his consent, as per the hadith 'لا يحل مال امرئ مسلم إلا بطيب نفسه'. However, if the landowner compensates him for the value, it becomes a separate sale requiring mutual consent. The hadith 'المسلمون على شروطهم' supports the validity of a settlement (sulh) between them. Additionally, the hadith from Ibn Abbas encourages the landowner to give the land without rent as a virtuous act. Thus, the ruling provides practical solutions for ending the lease while respecting property rights and encouraging amicable agreements.

Key Terms
اجارة (ijarah): hiring or leasing of land or services for a known rent
صلح (sulh): amicable settlement between parties to avoid dispute
مقلوع (maqloo'): uprooted trees, valued for compensation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a tenant built a house on rented land and the lease expires, which of the following is permissible according to the text?
A) The landowner can force the tenant to leave the house for free.
B) The tenant must demolish the house without any compensation.
C) The landowner may pay the value of the house as if demolished and own it.
D) The tenant must leave the house and landowner can keep it for free.

Key Takeaway
After lease expiry, the landowner cannot forcibly take the tenant's structures without consent; he may either compensate the tenant at the 'as if removed' value or both may agree to leave the structures in place.

Hiring Animals and Clothes Without Specifying the User
Ruling on permissibility of absolute hire with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on absolute hire (itlaq) of animals and garments, apply the condition that usage must not cause harm, and cite the hadith proof from Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
Absolute hire allows flexible use by any person, provided no excessive harm results.

When you hire an animal for riding or a garment for wearing, must you specify the rider or wearer? The Hanafi school holds that if the contract is absolute (itlaq), the hirer may allow any person to use the item. This lesson examines the ruling, its rationale, and the textual proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage states that hiring animals for riding or loading, and clothes for wearing, is permissible. If the contract is absolute (no specific user or item stipulated), the hirer has broad discretion.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) in principle.
2
Identify the conditions
The permissibility of flexible use is conditional upon the usage not causing destruction or severe harm to the hired item. For example, loading an animal with an excessively heavy load is not allowed.
Harm is defined by custom and likelihood (ghalabat al-zann).
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of Hasan al-Basri, who hired a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mirdas for two daniqs, rode it, and later rode it again without a new stipulation, paying half a dirham.
This is cited as an example of custom being authoritative in contracts.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that when no specific rider is designated, any person may ride. The payment was based on custom (urf), indicating that absolute hire is valid and the customary fee is owed.
The Hanafi school relies on the principle that custom (urf) governs ambiguous terms.
5
Apply the ruling practically
If you hire a donkey for a day without naming a rider, you may let any employee ride it. If you hire a garment without saying who will wear it, any family member may wear it, as long as the usage is within normal limits.
Avoid using the hired item in a way that would violate the contract's implicit limits (e.g., using a riding animal for heavy load without agreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۱۶۹ (۱۴) جائز ہے چوپایوں کو اجرت پر لینا سوار ہونے کے لئے اور بوجھ لادنے کے لئے ، پس اگر مطلق رکھا سوار ہونے کو تو جائز ہے کہ اس پر سوار ہو جو چاہے۔ اور ایسے ہی اگر اجرت پر لیا کپڑے کو پہنے کے لئے اور مطلق رکھا۔ تر چوپائے کو سوار ہونے کے لئے اور بوجھ لادنے کے لئے اجرت پر لینا جائز ہے۔ اگر کسی سواری کو متعین نہیں کیا تو کوئی بھی آدمی اس پر سوار ہو سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح بو جھ لادنے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا اور کیا چیز لا دے گا اس کا تعین نہیں کیا تو کوئی چیز بھی چوپائے پر لا سکتا ہے۔ البتہ ایسی چیز نہیں لا سکتا جس سے چوپائے کی ہلاکت یا اس کے نقصان ہونے کا ظن غالب ہو۔ چوپایہ سواری کے لئے کرایہ پر لے اس کے ثبوت کے لئے پیار ہے۔ واکتری الحسن من عبد الله بن مرداس حمارا فقال بـكـم؟ قال بدانقين فركبه ثم جاء مرة اخرى فقال الحمار الحمار فركبه ولم يشارطه فبعث اليه بنصف درهم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من اجری امر المصار على ما يتعارفون بينهم في البيوع والاجارة الخ ص ۲۹۴ نمبر ۲۲۱۰) اس اثر میں گدھے کو سواری کے لئے دو دائق میں کرایہ پر لیا گیا ہے۔ اور کوئی آدمی اس لئے سوار ہوسکتا ہے کہ کسی خاص آدمی کا تعین نہیں کیا۔ اسی طرح کپڑا پہننے لئے اجرت پر لیا تو لے سکتا ہے۔ اور پہنے والے کا تعین نہیں کیا تو کوئی بھی آدمی اس کپڑے کو پہن سکتا ہے۔ وں مستعمل کے اختلاف سے فرق نہ پڑتا ہو اور کسی خاص آدمی کی شرط نہ لگائی ہو تو کوئی بھی استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔ اطلق : مطلق چھوڑا ہو، کسی کو متعین نہ کیا ہو۔
It is permissible to hire animals for riding and loading. If the hiring for riding is absolute, it is permissible for him to ride whomever he wishes. Similarly, if he hires a garment for wearing and it is absolute. [Commentary: It is permissible to hire animals for riding and loading. If no specific rider is determined, any person may ride. Similarly, if hired for loading without specifying what to load, he may load anything except something likely to cause the animal's destruction or damage. For the proof, it is narrated that Hasan hired a donkey from Abdullah bin Mirdas for two daniqs, rode it, then came again and rode without stipulating, and sent half a dirham. This shows that when no specific person is designated, anyone may ride.]
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of hiring animals for riding or carrying goods, and garments for wearing, without specifying the particular person who will use them. The ruling is that if the hire is absolute (i.e., no specific user or item is stipulated), the hirer may allow any person to ride or wear the garment, and may load any goods onto the animal, except those that would likely cause harm or destruction. The commentator cites the practice of Hasan al-Basri who hired a donkey for a specific journey but later rode it again without a new agreement, paying the usual fee. This indicates that in absolute hire, usage is not restricted to one person. The key condition is that the usage should not vary significantly in terms of the burden on the animal or the wear on the garment, and no specific person is stipulated by contract.

Key Terms
اطلاق (itlaq): absolute hire without specifying user or item
دواب (dawabb): four-legged animals used for riding or carrying loads

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if someone hires a donkey for riding without specifying the rider, who can ride it?
A) Only the hirer himself.
B) Only a family member of the hirer.
C) Any person the hirer allows.
D) No one except those named in the contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, absolute hire (itlaq) grants the hirer broad discretion over who uses the hired item, limited only by avoiding harm.

Liability When Specified User is Changed
Ruling on liability when specified user is changed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the hirer becomes liable for loss if he changes the specified user of a hired item, and explain the legal rationale of ta'addi.

Core Idea
Changing the specified user of a hired item without permission makes the hirer liable for loss, even if the loss is not due to negligence.

This lesson examines a specific case in ijarah: when a hirer stipulates a particular person to use the hired animal or garment, but then allows someone else. The key question is: if the item is lost or destroyed, who bears the loss? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the hirer becomes liable (damin) for the full value. We will explore why this is the case, focusing on the concept of ta'addi (transgression) against the terms of the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contractual term
The hirer explicitly stated that a specific person (e.g., Zaid) will use the hired item. This condition is part of the contract.
The specification must be made at the time of hire.
2
Determine the hirer's action
The hirer allowed a different person (e.g., Umar) to use the item instead of the specified user.
This is a clear deviation from the contract.
3
Recognize the legal consequence
If the item is lost, destroyed, or damaged while used by the unauthorized person, the hirer is liable (damin) for the loss.
Liability applies regardless of negligence; the breach alone triggers it.
4
Understand the legal rationale
By changing the user, the hirer commits ta'addi (transgression) against the terms of the trust (amanah). He is no longer a mere trustee but a transgressor, hence liable.
The same principle applies to hired animals and garments.
5
Compare with cases without specification
If no specific user is named, the hirer may use it himself or allow others without liability, unless he exceeds normal usage.
The specification restricts the hirer's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۱۷۰ (۱۵) پس اگر کہا چوپائے والے کو یہ کہ اس پر سوار ہو گا فلاں یا کپڑا پہنے گا فلاں ۔ پس سوار کیا اس کے علاوہ کو یا پہنایا اس کے علاوہ کو تو ضامن ہو گا اگر ہلاک ہوا چو پایہ یا بر باد ہوا کپڑا ۔ ر چوپایہ کرایہ پر لیا اور اس پر خاص آدمی کے سوار ہونے کو کرایہ پر لیتے وقت متعین کیا۔ بعد میں اس کے خلاف کیا اور دوسرے آدمی کو سوار کیا۔ پس اگر جانور ہلاک ہو گیا یا کپڑا برباد ہو گیا تو اجیر جانور اور کپڑے کا ضامن ہوگا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی اپنے بھائی کو زمین عطا کرے یہ بہتر ہے اس کے لئے اس سے کہ اس پر کوئی معلوم اجرت لے (ب) حضرت حسن نے عبد اللہ بن مرد اس سے گدھا کرایہ پر لیا تو پوچھا کتنے میں ہے؟ عبداللہ نے کہا دو دانق میں۔ پس اس پر سوار ہوئے پھر دوسری مرتبہ آئے اور کہا گدھا چاہئے ۔ پس اس پر سوار ہوئے اور کرایہ کی شرط نہیں کی ۔ پھر اس کو آدھا اور ہم بھیجا۔
If he says to the owner of the animal: 'So-and-so will ride it' or 'So-and-so will wear the garment', and then he makes someone else ride or wear it, then he is liable if the animal perishes or the garment is ruined. [Commentary: If a specific person is designated at the time of hire, and the hirer later changes to another, and the animal dies or garment is destroyed, the hirer is liable.]
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This lesson addresses a specific scenario in ijarah: when the hirer stipulates a particular person to use the hired animal or garment, but then allows someone else to use it instead. The ruling is that if the animal dies or the garment is ruined while being used by the unauthorized person, the hirer becomes liable (daman) for the loss. This is because the hirer committed a breach of contract (taghayyur al-'ayn) by allowing a different user, thereby exceeding the scope of the hire. The hirer is considered a guarantor (amin) for the property, but when he violates the terms, he becomes a muta'addi (transgressor) and must compensate. The commentary also includes a marginal note repeating the hadith about giving land for free and the story of Hasan al-Basri, likely as additional context or a reminder.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): liable to pay compensation for the value of the hired item
تعدي (ta'addi): transgression beyond the agreed terms, causing liability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hirer stipulates that Zaid will ride the donkey, but then allows Umar to ride instead, and the donkey dies, who is liable?
A) The owner of the donkey.
B) The hirer (ajir).
C) Umar who rode it.
D) No one, as it was an accident.

Key Takeaway
The hirer is liable for loss when he changes the specified user, because he exceeds the contract's trust and becomes a transgressor.

Permissibility of Hiring Animals and Absolute Use
States ruling on hiring animals and absolute use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring animals for riding and carrying, apply the rule of absolute use where the specific rider or load is not stipulated, and identify the evidence from the practice of al-Hasan.

Core Idea
Hiring an animal for riding is permissible even without naming the rider—custom determines the permissible use.

This lesson presents a foundational rule of Islamic hire (ijara): the permissibility of hiring animals for transportation without specifying the exact user or load. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of al-Hasan al-Basri, holds that absolute hire is valid and the hirer may use the animal for any customary purpose, so long as no excessive harm is caused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognise that the passage deals with hiring animals (dawābb) for riding or carrying loads. The core ruling is that this is permissible (jā’iz) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalīl
Find the proof (dalīl): the athar where al-Hasan al-Basri hired a donkey without specifying a rider, and on another occasion rode without fixing the rent, then paid the customary fee.
This is a sunnah ahad with zanni thubut and dalala, but sufficient for permissibility.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
Understand how this action proves the ruling: al-Hasan's practice shows that hiring for riding is permissible, and that it is valid without specifying the rider or even the exact rent (custom suffices).
4
Note the scope and exception
The ruling applies to both riding and carrying, and to garments as well. However, the hirer is prohibited from loading the animal with something that would likely destroy or harm it.
This exception protects the animal from abuse.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Think of hiring a taxi or rickshaw: if the hirer does not specify who will ride, he may allow others to ride as long as the vehicle is not overloaded or damaged.
Custom and safety determine the limits.

كتاب الاجارة [۱۱۶۹ (۱۴) ويجوز استيجار الدواب للركوب والحمل فان اطلق الركوب جازله ان يركبها من شاء وكذلك ان استأجر ثوبا للبس واطلق فان قال له على ان بعضي ثواب ملے گا۔ عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله الا الله قال لان يمنح الرجل اخاه ارضه خير له من ان يأخذ عليها خرجا معلوما (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب الارض شیخ ص ۱۴ نمبر ۱۵۵۰ر بخاری شریف، باب ما کان من اصحاب النبي الله يواسى معهم في الزراعة. والنمر ص ۳۱۵ نمبر ۲۳۴۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بغیر کرایہ کے زمین کسی بھائی کو دے تو بہت بہتر ہے۔ اس لئے اپنی زمین بغیر کرایہ کے گھر والے یا مکان والے کو دے سکتا ہے، ثواب ملے گا۔ [۱۱۶۹ (۱۴) جائز ہے چوپایوں کو اجرت پر لینا سوار ہونے کے لئے اور بوجھ لادنے کے لئے ، پس اگر مطلق رکھا سوار ہونے کو تو جائز ہے کہ اس پر سوار ہو جو چاہے۔ اور ایسے ہی اگر اجرت پر لیا کپڑے کو پہنے کے لئے اور مطلق رکھا۔ تر چوپائے کو سوار ہونے کے لئے اور بوجھ لادنے کے لئے اجرت پر لینا جائز ہے۔ اگر کسی سواری کو متعین نہیں کیا تو کوئی بھی آدمی اس پر سوار ہو سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح بو جھ لادنے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا اور کیا چیز لا دے گا اس کا تعین نہیں کیا تو کوئی چیز بھی چوپائے پر لا سکتا ہے۔ البتہ ایسی چیز نہیں لا سکتا جس سے چوپائے کی ہلاکت یا اس کے نقصان ہونے کا ظن غالب ہو۔ چوپایہ سواری کے لئے کرایہ پر لے اس کے ثبوت کے لئے پیار ہے۔ واکتری الحسن من عبد الله بن مرداس حمارا فقال بـكـم؟ قال بدانقين فركبه ثم جاء مرة اخرى فقال الحمار الحمار فركبه ولم يشارطه فبعث اليه بنصف درهم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من اجری امر المصار على ما يتعارفون بينهم في البيوع والاجارة الخ ص ۲۹۴ نمبر ۲۲۱۰) اس اثر میں گدھے کو سواری کے لئے دو دائق میں کرایہ پر لیا گیا ہے۔ اور کوئی آدمی اس لئے سوار ہوسکتا ہے کہ کسی خاص آدمی کا تعین نہیں کیا۔ اسی طرح کپڑا پہننے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا تو لے سکتا ہے۔ اور پہنے والے کا تعین نہیں کیا تو کوئی بھی آدمی اس کپڑے کو پہن سکتا ہے۔ وں مستعمل کے اختلاف سے فرق نہ پڑتا ہو اور کسی خاص آدمی کی شرط نہ لگائی ہو تو کوئی بھی استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔ اطلق : مطلق چھوڑا ہو، کسی کو متعین نہ کیا ہو۔
Book of Hire: It is permissible to hire animals for riding and carrying. If riding is left absolute, it is permissible for him to ride whomever he wishes. Similarly, if he hired a garment for wearing and left it absolute... [Urdu commentary: It is permissible to hire animals for riding and carrying. If he did not specify a rider, any person may ride. Similarly, if he hired for carrying and did not specify what to carry, he may carry anything, except that which would likely destroy or harm the animal. Evidence: Al-Hasan hired a donkey from Abdullah bin Mirdas; he asked the price, was told two daniqs, then rode. Another time he came and said 'the donkey, the donkey' and rode without negotiating, then sent half a dirham.]
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof. The text opens 'Kitab al-Ijarah' (Book of Hire) and states the general permissibility of hiring animals for riding and carrying loads. The ruling is from the Hanafi school. It then clarifies that if the hiring contract does not specify a particular rider or carrier, the hirer may use any person. Similarly for a garment, if the specific wearer is not stipulated, any person may wear it. The commentary provides the proof: a narration (athar) where al-Hasan al-Basri hired a donkey without specifying a particular rider, and in one instance even without fixing the rent, paying the customary fee. This establishes the permissibility. The commentary also warns that the hirer cannot carry something that would likely destroy or harm the animal, as that would constitute a violation of the trust. The footnote includes a hadith about lending land without rent being better, which is a separate issue but reinforces the general permissibility of voluntary use.

Key Terms
استيجار (istījār): To hire or lease something for a specified benefit in exchange for compensation.
دواب (dawābb): Beasts of burden, i.e., riding or pack animals such as horses, donkeys, mules.

B) Only the person named in a separate agreement.
C) Any person the hirer chooses.
D) The animal cannot be used unless a rider is specified.

Key Takeaway
Hiring animals for riding or carrying is permissible, and absolute hire (without specifying rider or load) is valid, subject to the condition that the animal is not harmed.

Exception for Immovable Property: No Liability for User Change
Ruling statement with reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for damage to immovable property when a specific user is stipulated, and explain why the hirer is not liable.

Core Idea
Land and buildings do not vary with the user, so no liability for damage from user change.

In the previous lesson, we learned that stipulating a specific user for a movable item (e.g., a garment) makes the hirer liable if another uses it and damage occurs. However, there is an important exception: immovable property (ʿiqār) such as land or buildings. This lesson explains why this exception exists and how it applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
Recognize that this passage states an exception to the general rule of liability for stipulated user. The exception covers immovable property like land and buildings.
2
Understand the 'illa (legal cause)
The key reason is that immovable property does not vary with the user. The text says it 'does not differ with the change of user' – its value and condition remain stable regardless of who uses it.
This contrasts with movables like animals or clothes, which wear differently based on user.
3
Apply to a scenario
Consider land hired for cultivation with a stipulation that a specific person (e.g., Zaid) will cultivate. If another person (Umar) cultivates and damage occurs (e.g., erosion), who is liable?
4
State the ruling
The hirer is not liable for the damage because land does not vary with the user. The stipulation does not create liability.
The owner bears the loss unless the substitute user is negligent (then that user may be liable separately).
5
Note the basis
The legal basis is the nature of ʿiqār: it is resilient and uniform in use. The 'illa for liability in the previous rule (user-specific wear and tear) is absent here.
This is a settled Hanafi ruling; no major ikhtilaf among the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۱۷۲) (۱۷) بہر حال زمین اور ہر وہ چیز جو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے مختلف نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس اگر شرط لگائی کسی خاص آدمی کی رہائش کی تب بھی اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ دوسرے کو ٹھہرائے۔ زمین ہے یا مکان ہے جو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے کوئی زیادہ فرق نہیں پڑتا یا استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے کوئی زیادہ نقصان نہیں ہوتا ۔ جیسے زمین میں کوئی آدمی بھی کا شتکاری کرے زمین پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ اس لئے زمین کو کاشتکاری کے لئے کرایہ پر لے اور خاص آدمی کو متعین کرے پھر دوسرے آدمی اس کو کاشتکاری کرنے لگ جائے اور نقصان ہو جائے تو کرایہ دار پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ زمین کو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے کچھ فرق نہیں پڑتا ہے۔ ول استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے فرق نہ پڑتا ہو تو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدل جانے پر نقصان ہونے سے تاوان لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اس صورت میں کوئی بھی آدمی استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔ النت العقار : زمین۔
As for real estate and anything that does not vary with the change of user, if he stipulates residence of a specific person, it is permissible for him to house another. Land or house does not change with the change of user; whoever cultivates the land, it makes no difference. So if land is hired for cultivation and a specific person is stipulated but another cultivates and damage occurs, the hirer is not liable because the land does not vary with the user.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. The text clarifies an exception to the previous rule about liability. For immovable property (ʿiqār) like land or a house, the user does not significantly affect the property. Therefore, even if the hire contract stipulates a specific person to use it (e.g., a specific tenant or cultivator), it is permissible to allow another person to use it. If damage occurs, the hirer is not liable. The reason is that the property does not vary with the user, unlike animals or clothes where the user matters. This is based on the Hanafi principle that the 'illa (cause) for liability is the change that could potentially harm the item, which does not apply to land.

Key Terms
عقار (ʿiqār): Immovable property such as land, buildings, and real estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires land for cultivation and stipulates that Zaid will cultivate, but then Umar cultivates and the land is damaged (e.g., erosion), who is liable?
A) The hirer is liable for the damage.
B) Zaid is liable.
C) The hirer is not liable because land does not vary with the user.
D) The owner bears the loss.

Key Takeaway
For immovable property, stipulating a specific user does not impose liability for damage because the property does not vary with the user.

Specification of Load in Animal Hire Contracts
Ruling on binding nature of specified load type and quantity in animal hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a hirer specifies the type and quantity of load in an animal hire contract and apply the rule to determine the validity of loading different goods.

Core Idea
Specified load type and quantity in an animal hire contract are binding — any deviation violates the contract.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh on ijara presents a clear ruling: when a person hires an animal and specifies both the type and quantity of the load, he must load exactly that. The ruling underscores the importance of precision in contractual terms and the liability for non-compliance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that this is a contract of hire (ijara) for an animal to carry a load.
The animal is the object of hire, and the load is the subject matter of the service.
2
Identify the specification
Note that the hirer has explicitly stated both the type (e.g., wheat) and the quantity (e.g., five qafiz).
This specification eliminates uncertainty (gharar) in the contract.
3
State the ruling
The text rules that it is permissible (ja'iz) for the hirer to load that specified item.
The permissibility is conditional upon adherence to the specification.
4
Recognize the restriction
Understand that the hirer is restricted to loading exactly that type and quantity; he cannot substitute a different type or exceed the quantity.
Loading a different type (e.g., barley instead of wheat) or more quantity violates the contract.
5
Note the consequence of deviation
If the hirer deviates, he becomes liable for any damage to the animal or breach of contract.
The animal owner may seek compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۱۷۳) (۱۸) اگر متعین کیا ایک نوع یا مقدار جو لا دے گا چوپائے پر مثل یہ کہے کہ پانچ قفلیز گیہوں تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ لادے جو گیہوں
If he specifies a type and quantity that he will load on the animal, such as saying 'five qafiz of wheat', then it is permissible for him to load that wheat.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This is a ruling statement about hiring an animal for carrying loads. If the hirer specifies the type of load (e.g., wheat) and the quantity (e.g., five qafiz), then he is restricted to loading exactly that specified type and amount. He cannot load a different type (like barley) or more than the specified quantity because it would violate the contract and could harm the animal. This ruling aligns with the principle that the contract must be adhered to; exceeding the specification makes the hirer liable for any damage.

Key Terms
قفلیز (qafiz): A classical unit of volume used for measuring grain, approximately 50-60 liters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a donkey to carry exactly five qafiz of wheat, can he instead load five qafiz of barley?
A) Yes, because the quantity is the same.
B) Yes, if the donkey can carry it without harm.
C) No, because the type is specified as wheat.
D) No, because he must load wheat only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijara, once the type and quantity of load are specified, the hirer is contractually bound to load exactly that; any deviation is a breach.

Liability When Specified User Is Changed in Ijarah
Ruling on liability when specified user is changed in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when the specified user in an ijarah contract is changed, and apply the principle that items varying with user are subject to daman.

Core Idea
Changing the specified user in a hire contract turns the item from amanah to daman—the hirer is liable if it perishes.

Hiring an animal or garment for a specific person creates a trust (amanah) condition. If the hirer allows a different user to use it, the item becomes a guarantee (daman). This lesson explains the ruling and the reasoning behind the change of liability, focusing on the Hanafi position that the condition violation triggers compensation if the item is destroyed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that if a person hires an animal or garment for a specific user and then allows another user, and the item perishes, the hirer is liable for compensation (daman). Determine the act (violating the condition) and the legal consequence (liability).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is a qiyas based on the illa that usage varies with the user (ikhtilaf bi-ikhtilaf al-mustamal). The asl is the case of the animal rider; the far' is the garment wearer. Both share the same effective cause.
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that different users affect the item differently (e.g., a heavy rider vs a light rider, an experienced rider vs an inexperienced one). This variation justifies the rule that changing the user breaks the trust and imposes liability upon destruction.
4
Note the generalization
The text extends the ruling: 'and likewise everything that varies with the variation of the user.' This means any hired item sensitive to user characteristics (e.g., cars, tools) gets the same ruling.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school imposes strict liability upon condition violation leading to loss, while other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require negligence. Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) in court or dispute resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يركبها فلان او يلبس الثوب فلان فاركبها غيره او البسه غيره كان ضامنا ان عطبت الدابة او تلف الثوب (۱) وكذلك كل ما يختلف باختلاف المستعمل  
قاعدہ ہے کہ استعمال کرنے والے کے الگ الگ ہونے سے استعمال کرنے میں فرق پڑتا ہے جیسے کہ سوار سوار میں فرق ہوتا ہے۔ کوئی بھاری سوار ہوتا ہے کوئی ہلکا سوار ہوتا ہے۔ گدھا بھاری سوار کو مشکل سے لے جائے گا جبکہ ہلکے سوار کو آسانی سے منزل مقصود تک پہنچا دے گا۔ اسی طرح ماہر سوار جانور کو آرام سے لے جاتا ہے جبکہ اجڑ سوار جانور کو تنگ کر دیتا ہے۔ یہی حال کپڑے پہننے والے کا ہے۔ اس لئے جب ایک خاص آدمی سواری کے لئے متعین ہوا اور بعد میں اس کے خلاف کیا تو چونکہ شرط کے خلاف کیا اس لئے وہ چیز اس کے ہاتھ میں امانت کی نہیں رہی بلکہ ضمانت کی ہو گئی۔ اس لئے ہلاک ہونے پر جانور کا تاوان دینا ہو گا ۔ یا جو نقصان ہوا ہے وہ بھرنا ہوگا۔
شرط کے خلاف کرنے سے ہلاکت پر تاوان ادا کرنا پڑے گا۔
عطب : ہلاک ہوا، تھک گیا۔ تلف : برباد ہوا، ضائع ہو گیا۔
[۱۱۷۱) (۱۶) ایسا ہی حال ہے ہر اس چیز کا جو مختلف ہوتی ہے استعمال کرنے والے کے اختلاف سے۔
He rides it such-and-such or wears the garment such-and-such. If another rides it or he wears another, he is liable if the animal perishes or the garment is destroyed. And likewise everything that varies with the variation of the user. Explanation: The rule is that with different users, the usage differs, e.g., rider differs - some heavy, some light; ass will carry heavy with difficulty but light easily; experienced rider takes animal smoothly while inexperienced rider troubles it. Same with garment wearer. Therefore when a specific person was designated for riding, and later contrary to that, because he acted contrary to the condition, the item is no longer a trust in his hand but becomes guaranteed. Thus if it perishes, he must compensate its value or whatever loss occurred. By acting contrary to condition, compensation is due upon loss. 'Atab: perished, exhausted. Talaf: ruined, lost. [1171] (16) The same applies to everything that varies with the variation of the user.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from 'Al-Sharh al-Thamiri' presents a Hanafi ruling on the liability of a hirer when the specific user designated in a hire contract is changed. The ruling: if a person hires an animal or garment for a specific individual (e.g., 'Zaid rides it') and then allows another person to use it, and the item is destroyed, the hirer becomes liable for compensation (daman). The reason is that the item is no longer held as an amanah (trust) because the condition was violated, so it becomes a guaranteed item (madhmun). The commentary explains the underlying principle: items that vary in their usage depending on the user, such as animals (different riders affect the animal) and clothes (different wearers affect the garment), are subject to this ruling. If the user differs, the potential for harm increases, so the hirer is responsible. The text then generalizes: 'and likewise everything that varies with the variation of the user' means any item that is affected by who uses it. This is a key principle in Hanafi ijarah law: the specific condition is binding for movable items that are sensitive to the user's characteristics. The proof is based on the maxim that violating a valid condition in a contract leads to liability.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): Liable for compensation; the hirer becomes a guarantor of the item's value if it is destroyed after violating the condition.
عطب (atab): Perished or became exhausted (of an animal).
تلف (talaf): Destroyed or wasted (of goods).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a donkey to be ridden by Zaid, but then allows Amr to ride it and the donkey perishes, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The hirer is not liable because the donkey was an amanah.
B) The hirer is liable because the condition was violated and the donkey perished.
C) The owner is responsible because he should have checked who rides.
D) The hirer is liable only if he was negligent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, violating the specified user condition turns the hired item from amanah to daman, making the hirer liable for compensation if the item perishes.

6 min
Exception for Immovables: User Specification Not Binding
Explains that for immovables like land, specifying a particular user does not restrict the hirer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi exception for immovables in ijarah to determine whether a user specification is binding and whether liability arises from substituting users.

Core Idea
For immovables, user does not matter; specifying a specific user in a hire contract is not binding.

This lesson examines a key nuance in Hanafi ijarah (hire/lease) law: the distinction between movables and immovables regarding user specification. While for movables, restricting the user is binding and any deviation can incur liability, for immovables such as land and buildings, the user's identity is legally irrelevant. The passage explains the reasoning behind this exception and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type
Determine whether the leased property is movable (such as animals, vehicles) or immovable (such as land, buildings). The ruling hinges on this classification.
2
Check the user specification
If the contract stipulates a specific user (e.g., 'only Zaid may reside' or 'only Bakr may farm'), note that this condition is present.
3
Apply the exception
For immovables, the condition is not binding. The hirer may substitute the user without breaching the contract.
4
Determine liability
If damage occurs due to the substituted user, the hirer is not liable for compensation because the property does not vary with user identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاما العقار وما لا يختلف باختلاف المستعمل فلا يعتبر تقييده فان شرط سكنى واحد بعينه فله ان يسكن غيره  
[1172) (17) بہر حال زمین اور ہر وہ چیز جو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے مختلف نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس اگر شرط لگائی کسی خاص آدمی کی رہائش کی تب بھی اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ دوسرے کو ٹھہرائے۔ زمین ہے یا مکان ہے جو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے کوئی زیادہ فرق نہیں پڑتا یا استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے کوئی زیادہ نقصان نہیں ہوتا ۔ جیسے زمین میں کوئی آدمی بھی کاشتکاری کرے زمین پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ اس لئے زمین کو کاشتکاری کے لئے کرایہ پر لے اور خاص آدمی کو متعین کرے پھر دوسرے آدمی اس کو کاشتکاری کرنے لگ جائے اور نقصان ہو جائے تو کرایہ دار پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ زمین کو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے کچھ فرق نہیں پڑتا ہے۔ ول استعمال کرنے والے کے بدلنے سے فرق نہ پڑتا ہو تو استعمال کرنے والے کے بدل جانے پر نقصان ہونے سے تاوان لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اس صورت میں کوئی بھی آدمی استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔
النت العقار : زمین۔
As for immovables and that which does not vary with the variation of the user, its specification is not considered. If he stipulates the residence of a specific person, he may lodge someone else. [1172) (17) Anyway, land and everything that does not vary when the user changes: if he stipulates the residence of a specific person, it is still permissible for him to put another. Land or house does not change much with the change of user, or no significant harm. For example, in land, anyone can farm it; no effect on the land. So if he rents land for farming and stipulates a specific person, then another person starts farming and harm occurs, the tenant is not liable for compensation. Because land does not differ with change of user. And when user change does not make a difference, then if a loss occurs due to change of user, compensation is not obligatory. In this case, anyone can use it. Al-khattaar: land.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage provides the exception to the previous ruling. The author distinguishes between movables (which vary by user) and immovables (which do not). For immovables like land (العقار) or houses, specifying a particular user is not legally significant. Thus, if a hire contract for land or a house stipulates a specific person (e.g., 'Zaid shall reside'), the hirer may still allow another person to use it without incurring liability if the property is harmed. The reasoning is that land and buildings are not affected by who uses them in the same way as animals or clothes. For example, farming land by any farmer does not damage the land inherently. Therefore, the condition of specifying a particular user is not binding. The Hanafi school emphasizes that liability (daman) only arises when the condition violation leads to potential increased harm. Since immovables are not sensitive to user identity, the hirer is free to substitute users.

Key Terms
عقار (aqar): Immovable property, such as land and buildings.
تقييد (taqyid): Specification or restriction of the user in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person rents a house for himself to live in, but later allows his friend to stay instead, and the house is damaged, what is the ruling?
A) The tenant is liable for the damage because he changed the user.
B) The tenant is not liable because houses are immovables and do not vary by user.
C) The friend is liable because he occupied the house.
D) The owner is liable because he allowed the change.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, user specifications for immovables are not binding because the use does not vary with the user's identity.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
6 min
Loading Type and Weight: Permissible Substitutions and Liability
Rules on permissible substitutions when load type and weight are specified in animal hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a hirer may load similar or less harmful items than stipulated, and state when compensation (daman) becomes wajib.

Core Idea
In animal hire, the hirer may load similar or less harmful items; more harmful items incur liability.

In a contract of animal hire, the parties often specify the type and quantity of load. What happens if the hirer loads a different type? This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling: the key factor is the degree of harm to the animal. If the substituted load is similar or less harmful, it is permissible. If it is more harmful, the hirer violates the condition and becomes liable for compensation if the animal perishes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract terms
Determine the stipulated load type and quantity in the animal hire contract. For example, 'five qafiz of wheat' or '100 kg of cotton'.
The exact quantity matters only when comparing harm levels; the ruling does not depend on quantity as long as it matches.
2
Assess the harm level of the substitute
Compare the harm (darar) of the substituted load to the stipulated load. Is it similar, less harmful, or more harmful? The passage gives examples: wheat vs. barley/sesame (similar or less), wheat vs. salt/iron/lead (more harmful).
Harm is determined by the load's density, texture, and effect on the animal's back and stamina.
3
Apply the permissibility rule
If the substitute is similar or less harmful, loading it is permissible. If it is more harmful, loading it is not permissible (haram) and constitutes a breach of contract.
The principle: 'He may load similar or less harmful items; not more harmful.'
4
Determine liability (daman)
If the hirer loads a permissible substitute and the animal perishes, no liability. If he loads a more harmful load and the animal perishes, he must pay compensation (daman) because he transgressed the contract.
The evidence from Shuraih: transgression (ta'addi) triggers liability even if the harm is not directly caused.
5
Review the proof (dalil)
The ruling is supported by narrations from Ma'mar and Shuraih. Ma'mar states that loading according to the condition incurs no liability. Shuraih adds that exceeding the condition (e.g., by time or load) makes both the hire fee and compensation due.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh for such rulings.

وان سمی نوعا وقدرا يحمله على الدابة مثل ان يقول خمسة اقفزة حنطة فله ان يحمل ما هو مثل الحنطة في الضرر او اقل كالشعير والسمسم وليس له ان يحمل ما هو اضر من الحنطة كالملح والحديد والرصاص 114 (19) فان استأجرها ليحمل عليها قطنا سماه فليس له ان يحمل مثل وزنه حديدا .
کے مثل ہو ضرر میں یا کم ہو، جیسے جو اور تل ۔ اور اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ لادے جو زیادہ نقصان دہ ہو گیہوں سے، جیسے نمک، لوہا اور سیسہ چوپایہ کرایہ پر لیا اور خاص قسم کی چیز لادنے کی شرط کی تو قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ اس جیسی چیز یا اس سے کم نقصان دہ چیز اس پر لا د سکتا ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ نقصان دہ چیز نہیں لا د سکتا۔ اگر لا دے تو خلاف مشروط ہو گا اور ہلاک ہونے پر تاوان ادا کرنا ہوگا۔ مثلا شروط کی پانچ قفیز گیہوں لا دوں گا تو پانچ قیز جواورتل لا سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ نقصان دہ میں گیہوں کے برابر ہیں۔ لیکن پانچ فیز نمک، لوہا اور سیسہ نہیں لا سکتا۔ کیونکہ نمک اور لوہا جانور کو زیادہ نقصان دیتے ہیں۔ اصول جس قسم کی چیز طے ہوئی اس کی مثل یا اس سے کم نقصان دہ چیز لا سکتا ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ ضرر رساں چیز نہیں لا دسکتا۔ دلیل یہ اثر ہے
عبد الرزاق قال قال معمر اذا دفعها الى رجل فحمل عليها مثل شرطه قال لا شيء عليه ولا ضمان (الف)(مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الکری بعدی به ج ثامن ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۴۹۳۰)
اقفزة : قفیر کی جمع، ایک خاص وزن السمسم : تل۔ ارصاص : سیسہ۔
[۱۷] (۱۹) پس اگر چوپائے کو اجرت پر لیا تا کہ اس پر معین مقدار روئی لا دے تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ اس کی وزن کے مقدار لوہا لا دے.
چوپایہ کرایہ پر لیا تا کہ اس پر مثلا سو کیلور وکئی لا دے گا تو اس پر سو کیلولو ہا نہیں لا دسکتا۔
روئی نرم ہوتی ہے اس سے جانور کی پیٹھ زخمی نہیں ہوگی اور ہلکی محسوس ہوگی۔ اس لئے روئی کے بدلے اسی کے وزن کے مثل لو ہا نہیں لاد سکتا۔ اگر لادا اور جانور ہلاک ہوا تو ضمان لازم ہوگا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن شریح انه قال ليس على مستكرى ضمان فان تعدى فجاوز عليها الوقت فعطبت قال شريح يجتمع عليه الكراء والضمان (ب) (سنن ) س اللبیھقی ، باب لاضمان علی المکتری فیما اکتری الا ان یتعدی ج سادس ص ۲۰۳ نمبر ۱۱۶۷۱۔ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الكرى يتعدى به، ج ثامن ، ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۹۲۵) حضرت شریح کے اس فیصلے میں ہے کہ شرط سے تجاوز کرے اور جانور ہلاک ہو جائے تو اجیر پر ضمان اور کرا یہ دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔
حاشیہ (الف) حضرت معمر نے فرمایا جب کرایہ کا جانور دے کسی آدمی کو اور اس پر سوار ہو اس کی شرط کے مشکل تو فرمایا اس پر نہ کوئی الزام ہے اور نہ ضمان ہے ( ب ) حضرت شریح نے فرمایا کرایہ دار پر کوئی ضمان نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر تعدی کرے اور شرط سے تجاوز کرے اور جانور ہلاک ہو جائے تو حضرت شریح نے فرمایا اس پر جمع ہوگا کرا یہ بھی اور ضمان بھی۔
And if he specifies a type and measure he will load on the animal, e.g., he says 'five qafiz of wheat', then he may load what is similar to wheat in harm or less, like barley and sesame. And he may not load what is more harmful than wheat, like salt, iron, and lead. 114 (19) And if he hires it to load cotton which he specified, he may not load iron of the same weight. Commentary: Similar in harm or less, like barley and sesame. And it is not permissible for him to load what is more harmful than wheat, like salt, iron, and lead. If he hires an animal and stipulates a specific type of load, the rule is: he may load similar or less harmful items, not more harmful. If he loads, it is against the condition, and if the animal perishes, he must pay compensation. For example, if he stipulated he will load five qafiz of wheat, he may load five qafiz of barley or sesame because they are equal in harm. But he may not load five qafiz of salt, iron, or lead because salt and iron cause more harm to the animal. The principle: he may load similar or less harmful items, not more harmful. The proof is the narration from Abdurrazzaq who said Ma'mar said: when he gives it to a man and he loads on it similar to his condition, he said 'nothing is upon him and no daman.' (Mussanaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab al-kariy bi...). Aqfiza: plural of qafiz, a specific weight; al-simsim: sesame; arasas: lead. [17] (19) Then if he hires an animal to load on it a specified quantity of cotton, then it is not permissible for him to load iron of the same weight. He hires the animal to load e.g., 100 kg cotton, so he cannot load 100 kg iron. Cotton is soft, it does not wound the animal's back and feels light. Therefore, he cannot load iron of the same weight instead of cotton. If he loads and the animal perishes, daman is obligatory. The evidence is from Shuraih: he said, 'The hirer is not liable, but if he transgresses and exceeds the time for it and it perishes, Shuraih said: both the hire and the daman are due on him.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). Hazrat Shuraih's judgment: if he violates the condition and the animal perishes, both the hire and daman are due. Footnote (a): Ma'mar said: when he gives the hired animal to a man and he rides it according to his condition, he said: no liability and no daman. (b) Shuraih said: no daman on the hirer. Then if he transgresses and violates the condition and the animal perishes, Shuraih said: both hire and daman are due.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage deals with cases where the hire contract specifies both the type of load (e.g., wheat) and the quantity (e.g., five qafiz). The ruling: It is permissible to load a similar type (i.e., equivalent in harm) or a less harmful type. For example, if wheat is specified, one may load barley or sesame. It is not permissible to load a more harmful type like salt, iron, or lead. If the hirer does so and the animal perishes, he is liable for compensation. The principle is that the degree of harm to the animal is the criterion. The text also provides a specific case: if cotton is specified, one cannot load iron even of the same weight because iron is denser and more harmful. The commentary provides hadith evidence: the narration from Ma'mar indicates that if the hirer loads according to the condition, he is not liable; but if he violates, he becomes liable. The ruling from Shuraih adds that in case of violation, both the hire fee (payment) and compensation (daman) are due. The hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi supports this.

Key Terms
قفیز (qafiz): A measure of weight or volume, here used for grain loads.
ضرر (darar): Harm or damage, specifically to the animal from the load.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person hires a donkey to carry five qafiz of wheat. Instead, he loads five qafiz of salt. The donkey perishes. What is the ruling?
A) He is not liable because the weight is the same.
B) He is liable because salt is more harmful than wheat.
C) He is liable only if the salt causes visible injury.
D) He is not liable because he loaded the same quantity.

Key Takeaway
In animal hire, the hirer may substitute only loads that are similar or less harmful; more harmful loads constitute a breach that triggers compensation liability.

Carrying Goods Similar or Less Harmful Than Agreed: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on permissible and impermissible loads in hire contracts, with prophetic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on loading goods similar or less harmful than the agreed type and identify the evidence (athar) used to support it.

Core Idea
The hirer may load goods similar or less harmful; loading more harmful goods constitutes transgression and incurs liability.

When hiring an animal to carry goods, the contract typically specifies the type and quantity. The Hanafi school establishes a clear principle: the hirer may load goods of similar or less harm compared to the agreed type, but not more harmful. This rule protects the animal from undue strain and ensures the contract terms are respected. The passage provides illustrative examples and cites early authorities to support the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is loading goods on a hired animal. The ruling: permissible to load similar or less harmful goods; prohibitive disliked (makruh tahrimi) to load more harmful; if animal perishes due to transgression, daman is due.
The ruling balances contractual fidelity and animal welfare.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from Ma'mar in Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq: when the hirer loads as per condition, no liability; if he deviates, liability applies.
The proof is a qawl sahabi, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The implication (mafhum al-mukhalafah) from the athar: compliance = no liability; deviation = liability. This establishes the boundary of permissible loading.
The athar does not specify harm; the commentator derives the harm criterion through legal reasoning (qiyas).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no internal Hanafi dispute on this ruling; it is part of Zahir al-Riwayah and unanimously upheld.
Cross-madhhab, other schools generally agree on the principle, though specifics may differ.
5
Evaluate the practical application
The thamarah: if the hirer loads more harmful goods and the animal perishes, the hirer must pay the animal's value (daman) and still owes the hire fee.
This ruling applies in everyday hire contracts for transport of goods.

Source Text

The beast: for example if he says 'five qafiz of wheat', then he may carry what is like wheat in harm or less, like barley and sesame, and he may not carry what is more harmful than wheat, like salt, iron, and lead. 114 (19) And if he hires it to carry specified cotton on it, then he may not carry its weight of iron. Similar in harm or less, like barley and sesame. And it is not permissible for him to load what is more harmful than wheat, like salt, iron and lead. He hired an animal and specified a particular type of thing to load; the rule is that he may load something similar or less harmful. He cannot load something more harmful. If he does, it is contrary to the condition and if it perishes, he must pay compensation. For example, he stipulated 'I will load five qafiz of wheat', then he may load five qafiz of barley or sesame because they are equal in harm to wheat. But he may not load five qafiz of salt, iron, or lead because salt and iron harm the animal more. The principle: he may load something similar to the type agreed upon or less harmful, but not a more harmful thing. The proof is this athar: 'Abd al-Razzaq said: Ma'mar said: When he gives it (the animal) to a man and he loads on it like his condition, he said: There is nothing on him, no guarantee.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Kira bi dhaylihi, vol. 8, p. 212, no. 14930) aqfiza: plural of qafiz, a specific weight. al-simsim: sesame. al-arsas: lead. [17] (19) So if he hires an animal to carry a specified amount of cotton on it, then it is not permissible for him to carry its weight of iron. He hired an animal to carry, for example, one hundred weight of cotton, then he cannot carry one hundred weight of iron on it. Cotton is soft; it will not injure the animal's back and feels light. Therefore he cannot load iron equal to its weight. If he loads and the animal perishes, guarantee (daman) is obligatory. There is proof for this in an athar: From Shuraih, he said: There is no guarantee on the hirer. And if he transgresses and exceeds the time on it and it becomes lame, Shuraih said: Both the hire and the guarantee are collected on him. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab la daman 'ala al-mukhtari fima ikhtari illa an yata'adda, vol. 6, p. 203, no. 11671; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Kira yata'adda bihi, vol. 8, p. 211, no. 14925) In the judgment of Hadrat Shuraih: if he exceeds the condition and the animal perishes, then on the hired person both guarantee and hire are obligatory. Footnote (a): Hadrat Ma'mar said: When he gives the hired animal to a man and he rides on it according to his condition, he said: On him is no liability nor guarantee. (b) Hadrat Shuraih said: On the hirer is no guarantee. Then if he transgresses and exceeds the condition and the animal perishes, Hadrat Shuraih said: On him both the hire and the guarantee are collected.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the book of Ijarah expounds the ruling regarding the liability of a hirer when he loads goods on a hired animal. The author establishes a clear principle: the hirer must adhere to the type of goods agreed upon. He may load goods of similar or lesser harm, but not more harmful. The example given: if the agreement is to carry wheat, barley or sesame (similar harm) are permissible, but salt, iron, or lead (greater harm) are not. The proof is an athar from Ma'mar reported in the Musannaf of 'Abd al-Razzaq, indicating that if one loads what was agreed, no guarantee is due; conversely, transgression (ta'addi) leads to liability. A specific sub-case is then mentioned: if hired to carry cotton, one cannot substitute iron of the same weight because iron is more harmful. Another athar from Shuraih confirms that transgression results in both the hire being due and the guarantee. This ruling is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah of the Hanafi school and is consistently upheld.

Key Terms
أقفزة (aqfizah): Plural of qafiz, a unit of weight used for grains, approximately equivalent to a specific measure (e.g., 60 lbs depending on region).
ضرر (darar): Harm, specifically to the animal being hired; the degree of harm determines what goods may be carried.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability to pay compensation for loss or damage; in this context, the hirer must pay the value of the animal if it perishes due to his transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a donkey to carry 100 kg of wheat, what can he load instead?
A) 100 kg of iron because it is the same weight.
B) 100 kg of barley because it is similar in harm.
C) 100 kg of cotton because it is lighter.
D) He cannot load anything except wheat.

Key Takeaway
The hirer must load goods of similar or less harm; loading more harmful goods is transgression and incurs daman.

Riding and Allowing Another: Liability for Animal's Death
Ruling on hired animal with additional rider

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when an additional rider is allowed on a hired animal and differentiate the liability based on the animal's capacity.

Core Idea
For a hired animal, liability for an unauthorized additional rider is proportional to the degree of transgression.

In rental contracts (ijara), the permitted use is clearly defined. When the hirer adds an extra rider without permission, this act is a transgression (ta'addi) that may affect the animal's safety. The Hanafi school holds that the hirer's liability depends on the animal's capacity to bear the extra load. This lesson examines the ruling from the matn and its evidentiary basis from the practices of the Companion Shuraih and the tabi'i Hammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The hirer makes an additional person ride behind him on a hired animal. The ruling states that if the animal becomes lame, the hirer guarantees half its value if the animal could carry both riders; otherwise, full value.
The act is the unauthorized addition of a rider, which is a transgression.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario 1: Animal could bear both riders. Scenario 2: Animal could not bear both. In scenario 1, liability is half; in scenario 2, full.
The capacity is based on the animal's strength, not the riders' weight.
3
Trace the principle of proportional liability
The transgression is the additional rider. In scenario 1, half the usage was authorized, half unauthorized, so half liability. In scenario 2, the entire act is transgressive, leading to full liability.
This follows the principle that liability is proportional to the excess over the permitted use.
4
Examine the proofs from the Athar
The passage cites two athar: (a) From Ibn Sirin that Shuraih made a hirer pay compensation proportional to the excess load. (b) From Hammad that transgression results in both hire and guarantee.
These show that transgression (ta'addi) leads to guarantee proportionate to the excess.
5
Note the operative factor
The key factor is the number of riders, not their weight. Custom (urf) assumes one rider as the standard.
Weight is not considered because the contract specifies a rider, not a weight limit.

But the excess is calculated proportionally, and guarantee is required. If the animal was such that it could not bear the load of two men, yet two men rode, then he is guarantor for the full value of the animal. Because he acted against the norm and it will be considered that he intended to destroy the animal, so he pays the full price. Transgression necessitates guarantee. 'Ataba: he became tired, perished.

Commentary
This passage presents ruling (20) regarding the rental of an animal for riding. The hirer makes an additional person ride behind him, causing the animal's death. The ruling differentiates based on the animal's capacity: if the animal could carry both men (i.e., had sufficient strength) yet still perished, the hirer guarantees half the animal's value. This is because the transgression is in the second rider, who was not authorized, so liability is shared. If the animal could not even carry both, then the hirer is liable for the full value, as his act is tantamount to deliberate destruction. The commentator emphasizes that the key factor is the number of riders, not their weight, as per custom. Proof is provided from the practice of Shuraih, who made a hirer pay compensation proportional to the excess load, and from Hammad who stated that transgression results in both hire and guarantee. This ruling is part of the standard Hanafi position in the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
أردف (ardafa): To make someone ride behind; in this context, the additional rider beyond the agreed one.
عطب (ataba): The animal becomes lame or perishes due to overexertion.
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression; exceeding the permitted limits of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Liability for transgression in a hire contract is proportional to the degree of unauthorized use, measured by the number of riders (or proportional excess in goods).

Exceeding Agreed Load: Proportional Liability in Ijarah
Ruling on hiring animal to carry a specified load and exceeding it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exceeding an agreed load in a hire contract and calculate proportional compensation when the animal perishes.

Core Idea
Exceeding the agreed load is transgression; liability is proportional to the excess, not the full value.

In Hanafi fiqh, the hire contract (ijarah) requires strict adherence to the agreed terms. Any deviation, such as loading more than specified, is considered transgression (ta'addi). If the animal perishes due to this excess, the hirer must compensate the owner, but only in proportion to the extra load. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidentiary basis from the practice of the early jurists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is exceeding the agreed load in a hire contract for an animal. The Hanafi ruling is that this is a transgression, and the hirer becomes liable for compensation if the animal perishes.
The compensation is proportional, not the full value.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The Ḥanafī school relies on the practice of the Companion Shuraih, who judged that the hirer must pay compensation equal to the proportion of the excess load. This is a qawl ṣaḥābī (statement of a Companion) and is considered a valid proof.
The athar is narrated by Ibn Sīrīn and recorded by ‘Abd al-Razzāq.
3
Understand the proportionality principle
The compensation is calculated by dividing the excess load by the total load actually carried. For example, if the agreed load was 100 kg and the hirer loaded 150 kg (excess 50 kg), the excess fraction is 1/3. The hirer pays 1/3 of the animal's value.
The same principle applies whether the animal dies or is injured.
4
Apply to a similar scenario
Consider hiring a donkey to carry 200 bricks; if you load 250 bricks and it collapses, you calculate the excess fraction (50/250 = 1/5) and pay that proportion of the donkey's value.
Ensure the excess was the direct cause of harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۱۷۶) (۲۱) اگر اجرت پر لیا چوپائے کوتا کہ اس پر لا دے گیہوں کی ایک مقدار، پس لادا اس سے زیادہ ، پس چوپایہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضامن ہوگا
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن سیرین سے منقول ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے ایک آدمی کو اجرت پر لیا تا کہ مقام معلوم تک اس کی پیٹھ پر کچھ لا دا جائے۔ پس اس پر زیادہ لادا تو حضرت شریح اس کو تاوان دلواتے تھے اس کی مقدار جو زیادہ ہوا اس کے حساب سے (ب) حضرت حماد سے منقول ہے کہ جس نے کرایہ پر لیا پس زیادتی کی جس کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کے لئے کرایہ اول ہے اور اس پر منمان ہے۔
[1176] (21) If he hires an animal to carry a quantity of wheat on it, then he loads more than that, then the animal perishes, he will be liable. Footnote: (a) It is narrated from Ibn Sirin that a man hired a man to carry something on his back to a known place, then he loaded extra on him, so Shuraih used to make him pay compensation according to the amount of extra he loaded. (b) It is narrated from Hammad that whoever hires and then makes an excess causing it to perish, then for him is the first hire and guarantee is upon him.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This is ruling (21) which deals with the case of hiring an animal to carry a specific quantity (e.g., wheat) and then the hirer loads more than agreed, causing the animal's death. The ruling states that the hirer becomes liable for compensation (daman). The footnotes provide supporting precedents from Ibn Sirin and Shuraih, indicating that the liability is proportional to the excess load, and from Hammad that in such transgression, both the hire fee and guarantee are due. This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that transgression (ta'addi) in a hire contract results in liability, and the measure is the extent of the excess.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyādah): Excess load beyond the agreed quantity; triggers liability if the animal perishes.
ضامن (ḍāmin): Liable; the hirer becomes responsible for compensation.
تاوان (tāwān): Compensation, indemnity paid for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, exceeding the specified load is ta'addi; compensation is proportional to the excess, not the full value.

Liability for Riding Double on a Hired Animal
Ruling on liability when a hired animal is made to carry an extra rider

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a hired animal is made to carry an extra person, and apply the principle of ta'addi to determine the amount of daman.

Core Idea
Adding an unauthorized rider to a hired animal creates proportional liability—half value if capable, full if not.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on liability (daman) when a hirer exceeds the stipulated use of a hired animal by adding an extra rider. The passage uses proof from the practice of the Companion Shuraih to establish that transgression (ta'addi) triggers proportional liability. The key distinction is whether the animal could carry the extra load; if yes, liability is halved; if no, full liability applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
Clearly state the act: hiring an animal for one rider, then adding a second rider, causing the animal to perish. The ruling is that the hirer is liable for half the value if the animal could carry both, and full value if not.
The ruling distinguishes based on the animal's capacity, not the actual weight of the riders.
2
Trace the Legal Basis (Ta'addi)
Understand that the ruling is founded on the concept of ta'addi (transgression). The hirer had permission for one rider only; adding a second is a transgression against the contract, making him liable for the damage.
3
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
The passage cites the athar from Ibn Sirin that Shuraih imposed liability only for the extra load proportionally. This establishes the principle of proportional liability in cases of transgression.
The dalil is a Qawl Sahabi, which is a valid but zanni (speculative) proof in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the Principle to the Given Case
Apply the proportional liability rule: if the animal could carry both, the transgression is only for the second rider, so liability is for half the value. If not, the hirer is considered to have intentionally destroyed the animal, hence full liability.
The number of riders is the measure, not their weight, as per custom (urf).
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some other schools may hold that if the animal could bear the extra weight, there is no liability because the damage was not caused by the transgression. The Hanafi school, however, holds that ta'addi itself creates liability regardless of actual capacity.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in Hanafi, the hirer must pay even if the animal was strong enough, whereas in other schools he may not.

Source Text

وان استأجرها ليركبها فاردف معه رجلا آخر فعطبت ضمن نصف قيمتها ان كانت الدابة يطيقهما ولا يعتبر بالثقل (۱۱۶ (۲۱) وان استأجرها ليحمل اصول شرط سے تجاوز کرنے سے ہلاک ہوا تو ضمان لازم ہوگا۔ ۱۱۷۵ (۲۰) اگر چوپائے کو اجرت پر لیا تا کہ اس پر سوار ہو۔ پس اپنے پیچھے دوسرے کو بھی سوار کر لیا اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کی آدھی قیمت کا ضمان ہو گا اگر چوپا یہ دونوں کو اٹھانے کی طاقت رکھتا ہو اور بوجھ کا اعتبار نہیں ہوگا۔
چوپایہ اجرت پر لیا تا کہ اس پر ایک آدمی سوار ہو ۔ اب اپنے پیچھے ایک اور آدمی کو سوار کر لیا جس کی وجہ سے جانور ہلاک ہو گیا۔ پس اگر جانور ایسا تھا کہ دونوں آدمیوں کو اٹھانے کی طاقت رکھتا تھا تا ہم وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو اجیر جانور کی آدھی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اور اگر جانور ایسا تھا جو دو آدمیوں کے اٹھانے کی طاقت نہیں رکھتا تھا تو پوری قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔
(۱) عام عرف کے اعتبار سے ایک آدمی سوار ہونا چاہئے لیکن دو آدمی سوار ہو گئے جس کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک آدمی کی اجازت تھی دوسرے آدمی کی اجازت نہیں تھی اس لئے آدھی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا (۲) عن ابن سيـريـن اسـتـاجـر اجيرا ليحمل على ظهره شيئا الى مكان معلوم فزاد عليه فغرمه شريح بقدر ما زاد عليه بحساب ذلك (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الكرى يتعدى به ج ثامن ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۴۹۲۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جتنا طے ہوا تھا اتنا لا دنے سے ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن جو زیادہ لادا اس کا فیصد نکال کر حساب کر کے ضمان لازم ہوگا۔
اگر جانور ایسا تھا کہ دو آدمیوں کا بوجھ نہیں اٹھا سکتا تھا پھر بھی دو آدمی سوار ہو گئے تو پورے جانور کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اس نے معروف کے خلاف کیا اور ایسا سمجھا جائے گا کہ جانور کو جان بوجھ کر ہلاک کرنے کی نیت سے دو آدمی سوار ہوئے اس لئے پوری قیمت ادا کرے۔ اثر میں ہے عن حماد قال من اکتری فتعدی فهلک فله الكرى الاول والضمان عليه (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الکری بعدی به ج نامن ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۴۹۲۵ار سفن صحیح البیهقی ، باب لا ضمان علی المکتری فیما اکتری الا ان بعدی، ج سادس، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۱۶۷۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ تعدی کا ضمان لازم ہوگا۔
آدمی سوار ہونے میں آدمی کی تعداد کا اعتبار ہے خود آدمی کے وزن کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔
تعدی کا ضمان لازم ہوگا۔ عطب : تھک گیا، ہلاک ہو گیا۔
And if he hires it to ride it, and then makes another man ride with him, and it perishes, he is liable for half its value if the animal can carry both, and weight is not considered. (116 (21) And if he hires it to carry loads... If it perishes due to exceeding the stipulated condition, liability is necessary. 1175 (20) If he hired an animal to ride, then he made another ride behind him, and it perished, then he is liable for half its value if the animal had the capacity to carry both, and weight is not considered. He hired the animal so that one man would ride it. Now he made another man ride behind him, causing the animal to perish. So if the animal was such that it had the capacity to carry both men but still perished, then the hirer is liable for half the value. And if the animal was such that it could not carry two men, then he is liable for the full value. (1) According to general custom, one man should ride, but two men rode, causing perishing. Thus, permission was for one man, not for the second, so he is liable for half the value. (2) From Ibn Sirin: He hired a man to carry something on his back to a known place, and he increased [the load], so Shuraih made him liable for the amount he increased by proportion. (Mussanaf Abdur Razzaq, Bab al-Kura yata'adda bihi, vol. 8, p. 212, no. 14926) In this athar, it is that no liability is necessary for what was agreed upon, but for what was loaded extra, by calculating the percentage, liability is necessary. If the animal was such that it could not bear the load of two men, yet two men rode, then he is liable for the full value of the animal. This is because he acted against the known custom, and it will be considered that he intentionally rode two men with the intention of destroying the animal, so he pays the full value. In an athar: From Hammad, he said: Whoever hires and then transgresses, and it perishes, then for him is the first hire, and liability is upon him. (Mussanaf Abdur Razzaq, Bab al-Kura yata'adda bihi, vol. 8, p. 211, no. 14925, and Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab la daman 'ala al-mukhtari fina ikhtara illa an yata'adda, vol. 6, p. 203, no. 11671) From this athar we learn that transgression incurs liability. In riding a man, it is the count of men that is considered, not their weight. Transgression incurs liability. 'Atab: became tired, perished.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh discusses the ruling on liability when a hired riding animal is made to carry an additional person beyond what was stipulated. It is a ruling with proof from athar. The author first states the matn: if a man hires an animal to ride and then lets another person ride with him, and the animal perishes, he is liable for half the value if the animal was capable of carrying both, regardless of actual weight. The weight of the riders is not considered; only the number matters. If the animal was not capable of carrying both, he is liable for the full value. The commentary explains the reasoning: the hirer had permission for one rider, but by adding a second he transgressed. For the first rider, the hire is valid; for the second, it is a transgression. The liability is divided proportionally. Proof is given from the practice of Shuraih, who assessed liability proportionally for extra load. Also from Hammad, who states that one who transgresses owes the hire for the first but is liable for damage. Thus, the basis is that transgression (ta'addi) triggers liability. The commentary clarifies that the measure is the count of persons, not their weight, and that the hirer's act is considered intentional if he overloads beyond capacity.

Key Terms
تعدی (ta'addi): Exceeding the permitted use or stipulated condition in a contract of hire.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for damage or loss caused by transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a horse to ride alone. He invites a friend to ride with him, and the horse, though strong enough for two, stumbles and dies. How much is the hirer liable for?
A) Full value because he added an unauthorized rider.
B) Half value because the horse could carry both.
C) Nothing because the horse was strong enough.
D) Only the friend's share of the hire.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, adding an unauthorized rider to a hired animal creates proportional liability: half value if capable, full if not, based on the principle that ta'addi triggers daman.
