Liability for Overloading a Hired Animal
Ruling on liability when hired animal is overloaded

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a hired animal is overloaded and apply the proportional liability principle to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Only the excess load is compensable; the original hire remains valid.

In contracts of hire (ijara), the agreed terms define the scope of permission. When a hirer exceeds the agreed load and the animal perishes, Hanafi law distinguishes between the permitted use and the transgression. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidential basis from the practice of the early jurists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is loading an animal with more than the stipulated amount. The ruling: the hirer is liable (damān) for the excess weight proportionally.
2
Locate the dalīl
The primary proof is the athar of Ibn Sīrīn that Qāḍī Shurayḥ imposed proportional liability. A second athar from Ḥammād confirms the principle.
The dalīl is qawl ṣaḥābī (a Companion's or early jurist's ruling).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The athar shows that liability is limited to 'the amount he increased upon him, calculated accordingly.' This indicates apportionment by percentage of excess weight.
The Ḥanafī school uses this as a basis for proportional liability.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Some schools may hold that the transgression invalidates the entire contract, making the hirer liable for the full value. The Ḥanafī position retains the original hire and only charges for the excess.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fīh.
5
Evaluate the Ḥanafī tarjīḥ
The relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is proportional liability. No internal Ḥanafī ikhtilāf exists; the three imāms agree.
This ruling is from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.

Source Text

عليها مقداراً من الحنطة فحمل عيلها اكثر منه فعطبت ضمن مازاد من الثقل (۱۱۷۷] (۲۲) وان كبح الدابة بلجامها او ضربها فعطبت ضمن عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى و جتنا بوجھ زیادہ ہو۔

مسئلہ نمبر ۲۰ میں قاضی شریح کا فتوی گزر گیا ہے اور اصول بھی۔
(1176) (21) If he hired an animal to carry a certain amount of wheat, then he loaded more than that, and the animal perished, he is liable. Footnote: (a) From Ibn Sirin: A man hired a man to carry something on his back to a known place, then he loaded more, so Shuraih made him pay compensation according to the amount of the excess. (b) From Hammad: He who hired and then transgressed, and it perished, then for him is the first hire and upon him is liability. 
[Page 193] 
... upon it a quantity of wheat, then he loaded more than that, and it perished, he is liable for the excess weight. (1177) (22) And if he pulled the animal by its bridle or struck it, and it perished, he is liable according to Abu Hanifa... and as for the excess weight. For example, he hired the animal to load 100 kg of wheat, then contrary to the condition he loaded 125 kg, then he is liable for the 25 kg excess proportionally. For example, if the animal's value was 125 pounds, then the hirer is liable for 25 pounds, and the remaining 100 pounds are lost to the owner. Because loading 100 kg was permitted, so he is not liable for that; only the excess is liable. In mas'ala no. 20, the fatwa of Qadi Shuraih and the principle have already passed.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This lesson covers the ruling on hiring an animal to carry a specific quantity of grain, then overloading it, causing its death. The matn states: if the hirer loads more than agreed, and the animal perishes, he is liable for the excess weight. The commentary explains with an example: if agreed for 100 kg and he loads 125 kg, the liability is proportional to the excess. If the animal's value is equally divided, he pays for the extra fraction. The proof is from the athar of Ibn Sirin and Shuraih, who made the hirer liable only for the excess. Another athar from Hammad states that the hire for the permitted load stands, but liability attaches to the transgression. This establishes that the original contract remains valid for the agreed amount, and the hirer is only responsible for the additional damage caused by his transgression. The principle is that the hirer is not liable for the original permitted use, even if the animal perishes due to that use, provided no negligence. But when he exceeds, he becomes guarantor for the extra portion.

Key Terms
زيادہ لادنا (ziyada ladna): Loading more than the stipulated amount in a hire contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling from the athar of Shuraih, if a hired animal is overloaded by 20% above the agreed weight and dies, what is the hirer's liability?
A) Full value of the animal
B) 20% of the animal's value
C) No liability because the contract is valid
D) The full hire fee plus the full value

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that overloading a hired animal does not void the entire contract; the hirer is liable only for the proportion of the damage caused by the excess load.

Liability for Customary Actions on a Hired Animal: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for customary actions causing animal's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability for customary actions causing harm to a hired animal, identify the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and evaluate the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Liability arises even from customary actions if they cause harm—Abu Hanifa's conditional right view.

In a valid ijara contract, the hirer has the right to use the animal in the customary manner. But what if that very action causes the animal's death? The Hanafi school is divided: Imam Abu Hanifa holds the hirer liable, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not. This dispute turns on whether the right to use is conditional upon the animal's safety. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to analyse legal rights and their limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The scenario: a hirer pulls the bridle or strikes the hired animal, and the animal dies. The question: is the hirer liable (daman) for the value? Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says liable; Sahibayn say not liable.
The act is customary—pulling the rein to control the animal is normal use.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa rules that even customary actions are conditional on safety. He cites the athar of al-Sha'bi: 'He is liable for what his hand causes.' He analogises to artisans (dyer, washerman) who must compensate for damage even when acting within their trade.
The proof combines a textual athar with qiyas jali (clear analogy).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The Sahibayn argue that customary actions are not transgression. They cite the practice of Shuraih: liability only for actual transgression. Pulling the rein is an inherent right; if the animal dies despite proper handling, it is an accident.
They emphasise that the hirer did not exceed the custom: no ta'addi.
4
Determine the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, the hirer pays compensation; under Sahibayn, he does not. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view because it is more precautionary and supported by clear athar. However, both views are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
In fatwa, the stronger position is the one that protects the owner's property.

Source Text

امام محمد نے ضامن نہیں ہوگا۔
ان کو پایہ کرایہ پر لیا اور اس کو لگام سے کھینچ کر کھڑا کرنا چاہا جس سے چوپایہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ضامن ہوگا۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ لگام کھینچنے کا حق ہے لیکن بشرط سلامت حق ہے۔ اس طرح لنگام کھینچنے کا حق نہیں ہے کہ چو پایہ ہلاک ہو جائے ۔ اس کو احتیاط سے کام لینا چاہئے۔ لیکن احتیاط سے کام نہیں لیا اس لئے ضامن ہو گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے وقــال مطرف عن الشعبي يضمن مــا اعـنـت بیده (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ضمان الاجير الذى يعمل بیدہ نمبر ۱۴۹۴۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ہاتھ سے جو نقصان ہو وہ اجیر کو ادا کرنا ہوگا۔ یہاں ہاتھ سے لگام کھینچا ہے اور جانور ہلاک ہوا ہے اس لئے تاوان ہو گا۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ نگام کھینچنا اس کا ذاتی حق ہے اس کے بغیر تو جانور کو کھڑا ہی نہیں رکھ سکتا تھا اس لئے اس کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہوا ہے تو یہ تعدی نہیں ہے اس لئے کرایہ دار پر تا وان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
ے اثر میں ہے عن ابن سيرين قال جعل شريح على رجل تعدى بقدر ما تعدى (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الکری متعدی به ج ثامن ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۴۹۲۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تعدی اور زیادتی کے مطابق کرایہ دار پر ضمان ہوگا اور کرایہ دار نے لگام کھینچ کر کوئی تعدی نہیں کی اس لئے اس پر کوئی ضمان لازم نہیں ہے۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس قاعدہ پر متفرع ہے کہ معروف طریقے پر جو حقوق ہیں ان کو استعمال کرنے کے لئے سلامت کی شرط ہے یا نہیں۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کا قاعدہ یہ ہے جانور کو کھینچنے اور چلانے کا جو حق حاصل ہے وہ اس شرط پر ہے کہ جانور سالم رہے ہلاک نہ ہو۔ اگر جانور ہلاک ہوا تو حق استعمال کرنے کے باوجود ضامن ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ معروف طریقے سے حقوق استعمال کئے تو جاہے جانور ہلاک ہو جائے اس حاشیه : (الف) حضرت شعمی فرماتے ہیں ضامن ہوگا جو کچھ اپنے ہاتھ سے کام کیا۔ یعنی ہاتھ سے کام کرنے کی وجہ سے اگر ہلاک ہوا ہو تو اس پر ضمان ہوگا ۔ جیسے رنگریز اور دھوبی (ب) حضرت ابن سیرین فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت شریح وہ آدمی جس نے زیادتی کی ہو تو زیادتی کی مقدار ضمان لازم کرتے تھے۔
And as for the excess weight. For example, he hired the animal to load 100 kg of wheat, then contrary to the condition he loaded 125 kg, then he is liable for the 25 kg excess proportionally... In mas'ala no. 20, the fatwa of Qadi Shuraih and the principle have already passed. [1177] (22) If he pulled the animal by its bridle or struck it, and it perished, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa he is liable, and Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: he is not liable. They hired the animal and pulled it by the bridle to make it stand, causing it to perish. According to Abu Hanifa, he is liable. He said: the right to pull the bridle is conditional upon safety. He does not have the right to pull in a way that kills the animal. He must be careful, but he was not careful, so he is liable. (2) There is an athar supporting this: Mutarrif from al-Sha'bi said: He is liable for what his hand has caused. (Mussanaf Abdur Razzaq, Bab daman al-ajir alladhi ya'malu biyadihi, no. 14946) This athar indicates that the hirer must compensate for damage caused by his hand. Here he pulled the bridle with his hand and the animal died, so he must pay. The Sahibayn say: pulling the bridle is his inherent right; without it he could not make the animal stand. Therefore, if the animal dies, it is not transgression, so no liability on the hirer. Another athar: from Ibn Sirin: Shuraih made a man liable according to the amount of his transgression. (Mussanaf Abdur Razzaq, Bab al-Kura yata'adda bihi, vol. 8, p. 212, no. 14927) This athar states that liability is according to transgression, and the hirer did not transgress by pulling the bridle, so no liability. The principle of this issue is based on the rule: whether the use of rights in the customary manner is conditional upon safety or not. Abu Hanifa's rule is: the right to pull and drive the animal is conditional upon the animal remaining safe. If the animal perishes, even though he used his right, he is liable. The Sahibayn say: if he used the right in the customary manner, even if the animal dies, he is not liable. Footnote: (a) H. Sha'bi says: he is liable for what he did with his hand, i.e., if death occurs due to handiwork, he is liable, like a dyer or washerman. (b) Ibn Sirin says: Shuraih made the one who transgressed liable for the amount of transgression.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This lesson presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding liability when a hired animal dies due to a common action like pulling the rein or striking. The matn states that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the hirer is liable; according to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn), he is not. The dispute centers on whether the right to use the animal in the customary manner (e.g., pulling the rein to stop or guide) is conditional upon the animal's safety. Abu Hanifa holds that any action that causes death, even if normally permissible, becomes a transgression because the right is granted only on condition of safety. The Sahibayn argue that using the animal in the usual way is a legitimate right; if the animal dies despite proper handling, it is an accident and not a transgression. Proofs: Abu Hanifa cites the athar of al-Sha'bi that one is liable for what his hand causes, analogizing to artisans like dyers who must compensate for damage. The Sahibayn cite the practice of Shuraih, who only imposed liability for actual transgression, and pulling the rein is not transgression. The underlying principle (qawida) is whether the exercise of a right is conditioned on safety. Abu Hanifa's view is that it is conditional, so if harm results, the right is forfeited and liability arises. The Sahibayn view is that the right is absolute as long as it is exercised customarily. The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa in this issue, as the text implies preference through the order and supporting athar. However, the Sahibayn's view is also recorded.

Key Terms
كبح الدابة بلجامها (kabh al-dabbah bil-lijamiha): Pulling the bridle to check or control the animal.
شرط سلامت (shart al-salamat): Condition of safety; the right to use an object is valid only if it remains safe.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression; exceeding the proper limits of permissible action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a hirer pulls the bridle of a hired horse to stop it and the horse dies, is he liable?
A) Yes, because the right to pull is conditional on safety.
B) No, because pulling the rein is a customary right.
C) Yes, only if he pulled violently.
D) No, because the owner assumed the risk.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, even a customary action like pulling a rein can trigger liability if it causes harm, because the right to use is conditional on safety (shart al-salamat) according to Abu Hanifa, the mufta bihi view.

Liability for Excess Weight on Hired Animal
Ruling on liability for overloading hired animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on liability when a hired animal is overloaded and identify that liability is only for the excess weight.

Core Idea
Liability falls only on the excess weight — the agreed portion is at the owner's risk.

When you hire an animal or vehicle, you must adhere to the agreed load. If you exceed it and the animal is destroyed, you are not liable for the entire loss, only for what you added without permission. This lesson clarifies the precise extent of liability in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The person hired the animal to carry a specified weight (e.g., an agreed amount of wheat). This creates a condition: the hirer must not exceed that weight.
2
Determine the transgression
If the hirer loads more than the agreed amount, that extra loading is unauthorized (ta'addi). The animal perishes as a result.
The agreed weight was permitted, so no transgression for that part.
3
State the liability
The hirer is liable only for the excess weight because the damage to the agreed portion was not caused by his transgression. The owner bears the loss for the agreed weight.
Liability is proportionate to the unauthorized portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليها مقداراً من الحنطة فحمل عليها اكثر منه فعطبت ضمن ما زاد من الثقل
He loaded an agreed amount of wheat on it, then he loaded more than that and it was destroyed, so he is liable for the excess weight.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the chapter of ijarah. It establishes that when a person hires an animal to carry a specified weight, he must adhere to the condition. If he loads more than the agreed amount and the animal perishes as a result, he is liable only for the excess portion. The reasoning is that he was authorized to load the agreed amount, so no liability for that part; liability falls on the excess because it constitutes transgression (ta'addi). The animal's owner bears the loss for the agreed portion. This ruling is clear and requires no additional proof in this passage.

Key Terms
ثقل (thiqal): Weight or load being carried
عطبت (atbat): It was destroyed (the animal perished)
ضمن (damin): He is liable, responsible for compensation
ما زاد (ma zad): The excess, what is additional

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a camel to carry 100 kg of wheat, but loads 130 kg and the camel dies, for how much is the hirer liable?
A) The full value of the camel
B) The value of 30 kg of wheat
C) The value of 100 kg of wheat
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, liability for overloading a hired animal is limited to the value of the excess weight, not the entire animal.

intermediate
6 min
Pulling Reins or Striking Hired Animal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for customary actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hirer liability for customary actions causing death, explain the Sahibayn's opposing view, and evaluate the evidence each side uses.

Core Idea
Even a customary action like pulling reins can trigger liability if it causes harm—Abu Hanifa conditions the right on safety.

In ijarah (hiring) contracts, questions often arise about the extent of a hirer's permissible use. This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when a hirer uses customary methods to control a hired animal, but the animal dies? Two distinct views emerge from the founding imams, grounded in different prophetic traditions (athar).

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: the hirer is liable (damān) for the animal's death. His reasoning: the right to use customary actions is conditional on safety; causing death violates this condition and constitutes transgression (ta'addī).
He relies on the athar of al-Sha'bī: 'He is liable for what his hand caused.'
2
State the Sahibayn's position
Identify the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: no liability. Their reasoning: these actions are customary and necessary; without them, the hirer cannot manage the animal, so no transgression is committed.
They cite the athar of Ibn Sīrīn that Shuraih only imposed liability proportional to transgression, and here there is no transgression.
3
Compare the proofs (athar)
Note that both sides use traditions from early authorities. al-Sha'bī's statement is general; Ibn Sīrīn's is more specific about proportionality.
Abu Hanifa treats the right as conditional; the Sahibayn treat it as absolute within custom.
4
Analyze the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilāf: under Abu Hanifa, the hirer compensates the owner; under the Sahibayn, the owner bears the loss.
In later Hanafi fatwa, the view of the Sahibayn is often preferred for ijarah contracts, but both positions are valid.
5
Reflect on the underlying principle
The dispute hinges on whether customary permission implies absolute immunity or is limited by the condition of safety. This reflects a broader Hanafi method of balancing established custom (urf) against the general principle of liability for harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كبح الدابة بلجامها او ضربها فعطبت ضمن عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله لا يضمن. فيه اثر عن مطرف عن الشعبي يضمن ما اعنت بيده. وعن ابن سيرين قال جعل شريح على رجل تعدى بقدر ما تعدى.
And if he pulled the animal by its reins or struck it and it died, he is liable according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: he is not liable. There is an athar from Mutarrif from al-Sha'bi: he is liable for what his hand caused. And from Ibn Sirin: Shuraih held liable a man who transgressed to the extent of his transgression.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability of a hirer who uses customary methods (pulling reins or striking) to control the animal, but the animal dies. Abu Hanifa holds that even though the hirer has the right to use these methods, it is conditional on the animal's safety; if the animal dies, he is liable because he failed to exercise due care. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that these actions are his right; without them he could not manage the animal, so no transgression is committed and no liability follows. Abu Hanifa supports his position with an athar from al-Sha'bi that one is liable for what his hand does. The Sahibayn cite an athar from Ibn Sirin that Shuraih only imposed liability proportional to the transgression, and here there is no transgression because the action was customary. The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, the hirer must compensate for the animal; according to the Sahibayn, he does not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but often the view of the Sahibayn is preferred in ijarah matters.

Key Terms
ضمن (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage incurred by the hirer's action.
تعدى (ta'addi): Transgression beyond the permissible bounds of use, triggering liability.
كبح (kabh): To pull the reins to check or slow an animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the basis for holding the hirer liable when pulling reins causes the animal's death?
A) The reins are the property of the owner and cannot be touched
B) The athar of al-Sha'bi: 'He is liable for what his hand caused'
C) The athar of Ibn Sirin: 'Shuraih imposed liability proportional to transgression'
D) The contract of ijarah prohibits any interference with the animal

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, even customary actions can incur liability if harm results, because the right to use is conditional on safety—though the Sahibayn differ, and their view often prevails in practice.

Two Types of Hirelings: Ajir Mushtarak and Ajir Khas
Definition of two types of hirelings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ajir mushtarak and ajir khas, and apply the rule of wage entitlement to classify a given hireling scenario.

Core Idea
Wage is due upon completion for a common hireling; wage is due by time passage for an exclusive hireling.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi classification of hirelings (ujara') into two fundamental types. Understanding this distinction is essential because it determines when the hireling becomes entitled to payment and also influences liability rules in contracts of ijarah. The passage from the matn gives a crisp definition that we will unpack step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Read the opening statement: 'والاجراء على ضربين: اجير مشترك و اجير خاص.' Note the two categories: ajir mushtarak and ajir khas.
The passage uses 'اجير' for hireling; 'مشترك' means shared/common; 'خاص' means exclusive/private.
2
Analyze the criterion for ajir mushtarak
The text says: 'المشترك من لا يستحق الاجرة حتى يعمل' – the common hireling does not deserve the wage until he works. The key is that wage is tied to the performance of work.
Examples given: الصباغ (dyer) and القصار (fuller/launderer) – they work for multiple customers and are paid per job.
3
Analyze the criterion for ajir khas
The text says: 'الخاص من يستحق الاجرة بمضي الزمان و ان لم يعمل' – the exclusive hireling deserves the wage by the passage of time even if he does not work. Wage is tied to the duration of hire.
Passage does not give an example here; common example is a domestic servant hired for a day or month.
4
Apply the criterion to examples
Test your understanding: Given a scenario, determine which type of ajir it is. If the hireling is hired to perform a specific task for multiple principals, it is mushtarak. If hired for a fixed period exclusively, it is khas.
The critical legal implication: for ajir mushtarak, the wage is a debt payable only after work; for ajir khas, the wage accrues over time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاجراء على ضربين: اجير مشترك و اجير خاص. فالمشترك من لا يستحق الاجرة حتى يعمل كالصباغ و القصار. و الخاص من يستحق الاجرة بمضي الزمان و ان لم يعمل.
And hirelings are of two types: common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and exclusive hireling (ajir khas). The common hireling is one who does not deserve the wage until he works, like the dyer and the fuller. And the exclusive hireling is one who deserves the wage by the passage of time even if he does not work.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This is a definition and classification ruling from the chapter of ijarah. The Hanafi school divides hirelings (ujara') into two categories. The ajir mushtarak (common hireling) is someone who works for multiple people simultaneously, such as a dyer or laundry worker. He is not entitled to payment until he actually performs the work; his wage is tied to the output. The ajir khas (exclusive hireling) is someone hired exclusively for a period of time, e.g., a domestic servant from morning to evening. He becomes entitled to his wage simply by the passage of time, regardless of how much work he does. This distinction has implications for liability: the ajir mushtarak holds property as a trustee (amanah) and is not liable for loss without transgression, while the ajir khas is considered a guarantor in some cases. The passage does not discuss those details here; it only provides the basic definition.

Key Terms
اجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hireling who works for multiple principals and only earns wage upon completion of work.
اجير خاص (ajir khas): A hireling hired exclusively for a time period and earns wage by its passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A dyer takes cloth from multiple customers. He is not paid until he dyes the cloth. What type of ajir is he?
A) Ajir khas
B) Ajir mushtarak
C) Neither
D) Both

Key Takeaway
Ajir mushtarak earns wage upon completion; ajir khas earns wage by passage of time.

Amanah or Daman? – Liability of the Common Hireling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ajir mushtarak liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the ajir mushtarak's liability and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The ajir mushtarak's hand is amanah, not daman – he is not liable for loss without transgression.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over the legal status of goods in the possession of a common hireling (ajir mushtarak). While Abu Hanifa considers his hand a trust (amanah), the Sahibayn argue it is a guarantee (daman). Understanding the basis of each view is critical for correctly determining liability in hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the possession of goods by an ajir mushtarak. The core question: is his possession a yad amanah (trust) or yad daman (guarantee)?
The ajir mushtarak works for multiple principals, unlike ajir khas.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa says the goods are amanah in his hand; if they perish without transgression, he is not liable. His proof: the practice of Ali (RA) who did not impose liability, and analogy to a depositary (wadi’).
The owner voluntarily gave the goods, so custody is a trust.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the hand is daman; the hireling is liable even without transgression. Their proof: because he takes wages, his hand is akin to a guarantor's hand (qiyas on other wage-based contracts).
They argue that benefit (wages) implies liability.
4
Determine the thamarah and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, no compensation; under Sahibayn, full compensation. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it aligns with the practice of the Companions.
This is the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمتاع امانة في يده ان هلك لم يضمن شيئا عند ابي حنيفة. وقال ابو يوسف و محمد يضمن. حجة ابي حنيفة: انه امين كالمودع. و حجتهما: انه يده يد ضمان لانه يأخذ الاجرة.
And the goods are a trust in his hand; if they perish, he is not liable for anything according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: he is liable. Abu Hanifa's proof: he is a trustee like a depositary. Their proof: his hand is a hand of guarantee because he takes wages.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of the ajir mushtarak (common hireling) for goods in his possession. According to Abu Hanifa, the goods are held as a trust (amanah), similar to a depositary (wadi'). Therefore, if the goods are destroyed without his transgression, he is not liable. He supports this by citing the practice of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who did not hold the ajir mushtarak liable, and also the principle that the owner voluntarily gave the goods to him. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that because the ajir mushtarak receives wages for his work, his possession is akin to that of a guarantor (yad daman); hence, he is liable for loss even without transgression. They analogize to other wage-earners. The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, if a dyer loses a cloth without fault, he owes nothing; under the Sahibayn's view, he must compensate. The mufta bihi position in later Hanafi works is often the view of Abu Hanifa, as it aligns with the majority of the Companions' practice.

Key Terms
امانة (amanah): A trust; property held without liability for loss unless due to transgression.
اجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hireling who works for multiple principals; his hand is disputed as amanah or daman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, the ajir mushtarak is not liable for loss because his possession is classified as:
A) Daman
B) Amanah
C) Rahn
D) Ariyah

Key Takeaway
For the ajir mushtarak, the mufta bihi Hanafi position is that his hand is amanah, not daman, so he is not liable for accidental loss.

The Common vs Specific Hire and the Liability Dispute
Defines two types of hired workers and presents the Hanafi dispute on liability for loss.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ajir mushtarak and ajir khas, and state the Hanafi positions on liability for loss of amanah goods.

Core Idea
A common worker holds goods as amanah; Abu Hanifa says no liability, Sahibayn say yes – a key intra-Hanafi dispute.

In this passage we learn about two fundamental categories of hired workers in Hanafi fiqh: the common worker (ajir mushtarak) who is paid for output, and the specific worker (ajir khas) who is paid for availability. The text then presents a dispute among the early Hanafi authorities regarding the liability of the common worker when the entrusted property is lost without negligence. This is a classic intra-madhhab ikhtilaf with practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the first part of the passage which defines two types of hired workers. Note the key distinction: the common worker earns wage only upon completing the work, while the specific worker earns wage simply by being available.
2
Understand the amanah status
The passage states that goods held by a common worker are an amanah (trust). This means he is not liable for their loss unless he is negligent or transgresses. This is the default Hanafi principle.
3
Compare Hanafi positions
Note that Imam Abu Hanifa holds the worker is not liable, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he is liable. Identify the practical difference: compensation is required in the latter case even without negligence.
The Sahibayn’s view is often relied upon for craftsmen in later fatawa.
4
Connect to the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is whether the worker must compensate for accidental loss. This affects insurance and business practices for artisans today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاجراء على ضربين اجیر مشترک و اجیر خاص فالمشترك من لا يستحق الاجرة حتى يعمل كالصباغ و القصار والمتاع امانة في يده ان هلك لم يضمن شيئا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا رحمهما الله تعالى يضمنه
Hired workers are of two types: common worker and specific worker. The common worker does not deserve the wage until he works, like the dyer and the washer. The goods are an amanah in his hand; if they perish, he does not guarantee anything according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He guarantees it.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage defines the two categories of hired workers: the common worker (ajir mushtarak) who works for multiple people and earns wage upon completion, and the specific worker (ajir khas) hired exclusively for a period. The ruling states that goods handed to a common worker are a trust (amanah). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the goods are destroyed without negligence, the worker is not liable. However, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that he is liable. The text cites an athar from Ali (RA) who did not impose liability, and another athar from Ali and Umar (RA) who did. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view in cases of negligence, but the text does not explicitly resolve it here.

Key Terms
اجیر مشترک (ajir mushtarak): A worker hired by multiple people simultaneously, who earns wage only upon completing the work, like a dyer or washer.
اجیر خاص (ajir khas): A worker hired exclusively for a specific period, who earns wage just by making himself available, even if he does little work.
امانت (amanah): A trust; the worker holds the item without liability for loss unless caused by his own negligence or transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The goods are a trust (amanah) and the worker is not liable for loss without negligence.
B) The goods are a guarantee (damān) and the worker is always liable.
C) The goods become the worker's property.
D) The goods are considered a loan.

Key Takeaway
The common worker holds goods as a trust, but liability is disputed between Abu Hanifa (no) and Sahibayn (yes), with later practice favoring the Sahibayn.

Liability for Damage Caused by the Worker's Action
States ruling with examples and companion precedent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on worker liability for damage caused by his action and apply it to concrete examples.

Core Idea
A worker is liable for damage resulting from his own action, not from external causes.

This passage from the matn addresses a critical question in ijarah (hire) contracts: when must a common worker compensate for loss or damage to the entrusted item? The text provides clear examples: the washer who tears cloth by beating, the porter who drops a load, the carrier whose rope breaks from over-tightening, the boatman whose pulling sinks the boat. The ruling is that such damage, arising directly from the worker's act, requires compensation. The Hanafi school supports this with precedents from the companions Ali and Umar (RA).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the damage
For each of the four examples in the text, identify the worker's specific action and the resulting damage (e.g., beating causes tearing, slipping causes falling, pulling causes sinking).
2
Determine causation: action vs. fate
Analyze whether the damage is directly caused by the worker's physical action or by an external event (like theft or natural disaster). The ruling only applies to the former.
If the damage is from a third party or act of God, the worker is not liable.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
State that compensation (damān) is wajib because the worker's action constitutes ta'di (transgression) against the implied condition of safe handling.
This is the position of the Sahibayn, relied upon in practice.
4
Recall the companion proof
The athar from Ali (RA) and Umar (RA) imposing liability on craftsmen like dyers and goldsmiths serves as the primary evidence for this ruling.
The text quotes Ali: 'People cannot be set right except by that.'
5
Distinguish non-action losses
Contrast these cases with scenarios where the item is stolen, lost without worker action, or damaged by natural causes. In such cases, the worker is generally not liable.
This boundary is crucial for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما تلف بعمله كتخريق الثوب من دقه وزلق الحمال وانقطاع الحبل الذى يشد به المكارى الحمل وغرق السفينة من مدها
And what is ruined by his action, like the tearing of the cloth from its beating, the slipping of the porter, the breaking of the rope with which the carrier ties the load, and the sinking of the boat from its pulling (too much).
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage specifies that if the common worker causes damage through his own physical action, he is liable. Examples include a washer beating cloth so hard it tears, a porter slipping and dropping the load, a rope breaking due to over-tightening by a camel carrier, and a boat sinking because it was pulled excessively. The ruling is based on the principle that the item was given with the condition of safe return; any damage resulting from the worker's act (ta'di or negligence) obligates compensation. The text cites athar from Ali and Umar (RA) who imposed liability on craftsmen. This is the position of Sahibayn, which is relied upon in practice.

Key Terms
ما تلف بعمله (ma talifa bi'amalihi): Damages that result directly from the worker's own action, such as tearing, dropping, or breaking due to how he performed the work.
تخریق (takhriq): Tearing of cloth, specifically from beating or pressing during cleaning.
زلق (zalaq): Slipping of a porter causing the load to fall and break.
مد (madd): Pulling too hard, e.g., pulling a boat to the point of sinking or pulling a rope too tight causing it to break.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Cloth was stolen from the dyer's shop.
B) The washer's beating caused the cloth to tear.
C) The dyer's shop caught fire by accident.
D) The cloth faded naturally in the sun.

Key Takeaway
A common worker is liable for compensation when damage results directly from his action, as established by the Hanafi school based on companion practice.

Liability of the Common Hired Worker
Establishes liability of ajir mushtarak for damage caused by his work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the liability of the ajir mushtarak and identify the proof from the practice of the Companions (qawl sahabi).

Core Idea
A common hired worker is liable for damage caused by his work, even without negligence — safeguarding people's property.

In this lesson, we examine the liability of a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) for property damage during the course of his work. The Hanafi school, following Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, holds him liable for any damage resulting from his actions, unlike the exclusive worker who is a trustee. This ruling is supported by the established practice of the Companions Ali and Umar, who imposed liability on dyers and artisans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the common hired worker performing work on another's property. The ruling is that any damage caused by his work must be compensated (daman).
This is the default liability for ajir mushtarak, unlike ajir khas.
2
Understand the condition of safety
The property was entrusted with the implied condition of safe return. If the worker's action causes harm, he breaches that condition, triggering liability.
The condition is implicit in the contract.
3
Connect the proof (qawl sahabi)
The text cites athar from Ali and Umar imposing liability on dyers and goldsmiths. This is a valid proof in Hanafi usul, indicating obligation.
The specific wording from Ali: 'لا يصلح للناس الا ذاك' (people cannot do without that).
4
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa held the worker as an amin (trustee) and not liable unless negligent. The Sahibayn's view is the mufta bihi due to public interest.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

Book of Hiring. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said, may Allah have mercy on them both: He guarantees it. [1180] (25) And whatever is destroyed by his action, such as the tearing of cloth from beating it, the slipping of a porter, the breaking of the rope with which the carrier binds the load, and the sinking of a ship from its pulling, is guaranteed. It has been handed over to him for work with the condition of safety, and he destroyed it, so he will be liable. There is an athar that many Companions and Successors used to hold the common hired worker liable. From Ali, that he used to hold the dyer and the goldsmith liable, and he said: 'People cannot do without that.' (Reference) This athar proves that when an item is destroyed in the hands of a common hired worker, he will be liable. Because the item in the hands of a common hired worker is on the basis of guarantee. [1180] (25) And whatever is destroyed due to the worker's action, such as the tearing of cloth from beating, the worker's slipping, the breaking of the rope by which the hirer ties the load, and the sinking of the ship from pulling—all are guaranteed. For work done by hand, if damage occurs, the worker must guarantee it. For example, cloth given for washing: the washer beat it so much that it tore, so the washer must guarantee it. Or the worker slipped, causing the load on his head to fall and break goods, so the worker must guarantee it. Or the rope that ties the load broke, causing the load to fall and break, so he must guarantee it. Or the ship was suddenly pulled, causing it to sink and goods to be damaged, so the boatman must guarantee the goods. The worker had the right to do all this, but with the condition that the goods remain safe. But he worked in a manner that caused damage, so he must compensate. This issue is according to the school of the two Imams (Sahibayn). There is also the athar that passed that Ali used to impose liability on the common hired worker. And that Umar ibn al-Khattab used to hold liable the dyer who works with his hand. (Reference) This athar indicates that Umar also used to impose liability for damage on the dyer who works with his hand. Therefore, they will be liable. The common hired worker will be liable for damage. Glossary: takhriq: tearing; daqq: beating; zalaq: slipping; al-Hammal: porter; al-Mukari: hirer; madd: pulling. Footnote: (a) Ali used to impose liability on the dyer and the blacksmith, saying it is not good for people except this. (b) Umar used to hold liable the dyer who works with his hand.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The ruling (hukm) is that a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) is liable (daman) for damage to property that occurs as a direct result of his work. The matn lists examples: a cloth tearing due to the fulling process, a porter's load falling due to his slipping, the rope breaking, or a ship sinking from being pulled. All such losses are guaranteed by the worker. The reasoning is that the property was entrusted to him on condition of safe return, and his working style caused harm, so he must compensate. The text then provides proofs from the practices of the Companions: Ali ibn Abi Talib and Umar ibn al-Khattab used to hold dyers and other artisans liable for damages. This establishes the ruling as an accepted practice. The commentary notes that this opinion is from Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn), while Imam Abu Hanifa differed, holding the worker not liable unless guilty of negligence (ta'addi). However, the relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn, as it safeguards people's wealth.

Key Terms
اجير مشترك (ajīr mushtarak): A hired worker whose services are available to the public, not exclusively to one employer, and who works for a fee on specific tasks (e.g., a porter, dyer, washer).
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage, typically by paying the value of the damaged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) is liable for damage caused by his work as per the Sahibayn, a ruling based on the practice of the Companions and adopted for public benefit.

No Liability for Human Life in Hiring (and Cupping)
Exceptions human life from liability of ajir mushtarak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the ajir is not liable for human life in ijarah, explain the reasoning, and identify the conditions that trigger liability for medical procedures.

Core Idea
Human life is excluded from contractual liability; permissible work causing death does not obligate the ajir.

In the previous lesson, we established that the ajir mushtarak is liable for damage to property. This lesson introduces a critical exception: human life (bani Adam) is not included in that liability. Even if the ajir's actions directly cause a person's death—for example, by sinking a ship or causing a fall from an animal—he is not personally required to pay blood-money. The passage also extends this principle to medical practitioners like cuppers and cauterizers, provided they do not exceed the customary limits. This ruling is rooted in athar (reports from the Companions) and a careful distinction between contractual liability and liability for manslaughter (qatl khata).

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
The text states 'لا يضمن به بني آدم' – he is not liable for human life. Specifically, if a person drowns due to the ship sinking or falls from an animal while being transported, the ajir is not liable for that death.
This is an exception to the earlier rule that the ajir mushtarak is liable for lost or damaged property.
2
Understand the reasoning
The commentary explains that liability for human life is 'very great' and only arises from direct causation (mubashara) or accidental killing (qatl khata) – not from a contract. In qatl khata, the diya is on the aqila (clan), but here the death is due to the hiring contract, not a transgression (jinaya), so even the aqila does not pay. Thus, the ajir has no personal liability.
If the death were due to the ajir's negligence exceeding the scope of work, it might be different; but the text presumes the work is permissible.
3
Examine the proofs
Two athar are cited: (1) 'Amir al-Sha'bi was asked about a camel owner who carried people and they drowned; he said 'ليس عليه شيء' (nothing upon him). (2) Ibn Sirin reported that Shuraih did not hold the boatman liable for drowning or burning. These show the precedent of non-liability.
These reports are from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, and are zanni al-thubut (probable transmission) but qati al-dalala (clear meaning) in the Hanafi view.
4
Apply the principle to cupping/cauterization
The passage extends the same logic: if a cupper (fassad) or cauterizer (bazzagh) performs the procedure within the usual place (lam yatajawaz al-mawdi' al-mu'tad), he is not liable for any resulting death. He has permission (idhn) to do that act, and death is considered an unintended consequence.
If he exceeds the usual place, he transgresses the bounds of permission and becomes liable – the ruling changes.
5
Synthesize the condition for non-liability
The common thread: the ajir or practitioner must be acting within the scope of the permissible work as defined by custom and the contract. If he deviates or exceeds, liability may attach. Otherwise, human life is not subject to contractual damages.
This is a manifestation of the Hanafi principle that liability for human life follows rules of jinayat (criminal law), not mu'amalat (contracts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا انه لا يضمن به بنی آدم فمن غرق في السفينة او سقط من الدابة لم يضمنه [١١٨١) (٢٦) واذا فصد الفصاد او بزغ البزاغ ولم يتجاوز الموضع المعتاد فلا ضمان عليه [١١٨٢) (٢٧)
مگر یہ نہیں ضامن ہوگا بنی آدم کا پس جو غرق ہو گیا کشتی ڈوبنے کی وجہ سے یا گر گیا چوپائے سے تو اس کا ضامن نہیں ہو گا۔ البتہ اجرت کے موقع پر انسان ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کا ضمان اجیر پر نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ کسی کھینچنے کی وجہ سے کشتی ڈوب گئی اور اس کی وجہ سے آدمی مر گیا تو آدمی کا ضمان اجیر پر نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی طرح بوجھ کھینچنے کی وجہ سے آدمی چوپائے سے گر گیا اور مر گیا تو اجیر پر آدمی کا ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
کیونکہ انسان کا ضمان بہت عظیم ہے، اس لئے صرف قتل خطا یا مباشرت سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ عقد اجارت سے۔ اور یہاں اجیر کی غلطی کی وجہ سے اگر آدمی کی جان گئی تو یہ قتل خطا ہے اور قتل خطا کا تاوان اجیر کے خاندان والے (عاقلہ) دیں گے نہ کہ اجیر خود۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ اجیر کے عاقلہ جنایت کی وجہ سے جو قتل خطا ہوا ہو اس کا تاوان دیتے ہیں۔ اور یہ قتل خطا جنایت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوا ہے بلکہ عقد اجرت کی وجہ سے ہوا ہے اس لئے اجیر کے عاقلہ یعنی خاندان والے اس کا تاوان ادا نہیں کریں گے۔ اس لئے خود اجیر پر بھی انسانی ہلاکتوں کا ضمان لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) انسان کا ضمان بہت بڑا ہے، اگر اس کا ضمان لازم کریں تو اجیر تباہ ہو جائے گا اس لئے انسان کا ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا (۳) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ سئل عامر عن صاحب بعیر حمل قوما فغرقوا قال ليس عليه شيء (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ضمان الاجير الذى يعمل بیده، ج ثامن،ص ۲۲۱، نمبر ۱۴۹۶۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اونٹ والے نے کچھ لوگوں کو سوار کیا پھر وہ سب غرق ہو گئے تو اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں کیا (۳) عن ابن سيرين عن شريح انه كان لا يضمن الملاح غرقا ولا حرقا (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۴ ۵ فی الاجیر یضمن ام لا؟ ج رابع میں ۳۱۵ نمبر ۲۰۴۸۸) اس اثر میں حضرت شریح نے ملاح پر ڈوبنے اور جلنے کی وجہ سے کچھ لازم نہیں کیا۔
اجرت کی وجہ سے انسانی ہلاکت پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہے۔
غرق: ڈوب گیا۔ الدابة: چوپایہ۔
But he is not liable for human life. So whoever drowns in the ship or falls from the beast, he is not liable for him. [1181] (26) And when the cupper cups or the cauterizer cauterizes and does not exceed the usual place, then there is no liability upon him. [1182] (27) But he will not be liable for human life. So if a person drowns due to the ship sinking, or falls from an animal, he will not be liable. Rather, if a human perishes at the workplace, the ajir is not liable for him. For example, if the ship sinks due to pulling and a person dies, the ajir is not liable for the person. Similarly, if due to pulling the load a person falls from the animal and dies, the ajir is not liable for the person. Because liability for a human being is very great; it only occurs from accidental killing (qatl khata) or direct causation, not from the hiring contract. And here, if a person dies due to the ajir's mistake, it is qatl khata, and the blood-money (diya) for qatl khata is to be paid by the ajir's clan (aqila), not by the ajir himself. The rule is that the aqila pays diya for qatl khata that results from a transgression (jinaya). But this qatl khata is not due to transgression; it is due to the hiring contract, so the aqila will not pay. Therefore, the ajir himself is not liable for human deaths. (2) The liability for a human is very great; if we impose it, the ajir would be ruined, so he is not liable. (3) There is proof in the athar. 'Amir was asked about the owner of a camel who carried some people and they drowned; he said: Nothing is upon him.' (Reference) In this athar, the camel owner carried some people, then they all drowned; he did not impose anything. (3) From Ibn Sirin from Shuraih that he used not to hold the boatman liable for drowning or burning. (Reference) In this athar, Shuraih did not impose anything on the boatman for drowning or burning. There is no liability for human death due to hiring. Glossary: gharaq: drowned; al-dabbah: beast.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage states two rulings. The first is an exception to the previous general rule: the ajir mushtarak is not liable for loss of human life (bani Adam). Even if his action (e.g., pulling a ship or carrying a load) directly causes a person's death, he is not liable to pay compensation. The commentary explains the reasoning: human life is too valuable to be subject to ordinary contractual liability; such death would be either qatl khata (accidental killing) with diya on the aqila, or it falls under a different category. Here, since the death arises from the hiring contract and not from a transgression, the ajir is not liable. This is supported by athar from Amir and Shuraih. The second ruling concerns cupping (fasd) and cauterization (bigh): if the practitioner performs the procedure without exceeding the usual place, he is not liable for any resulting death. This is because he has permission (idhn) to do that much, and any harm is considered from an act permitted by custom. However, if he exceeds the usual spot, he becomes liable for transgressing the bounds of permission.

Key Terms
بنی آدم (banī Ādam): Human beings, as distinct from property. In this ruling, it means that liability does not apply to loss of human life.
عاقلہ (ʿāqila): The clan or male relatives who pay diya on behalf of a person who commits accidental manslaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a boatman's pulling causes a ship to sink and a passenger dies, what is the boatman's liability for the death according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must pay diya from his own wealth
B) His aqila pays diya
C) He is not liable for the death
D) He is liable but only half of the diya

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the ajir is not liable for human life lost due to his actions within the scope of the hire, based on athar and the principle that blood-money is not a contractual obligation.

Liability of Cupper and Cauterizer in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on liability for cupper and cauterizer who stick to usual spot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for a cupper or cauterizer and identify the condition that triggers liability.

Core Idea
No liability for harm if the practitioner stays within customary limits; transgression triggers liability.

Islamic law regulates medical liability by distinguishing between permitted and forbidden acts. This lesson examines the case of a cupper (fassad) and cauterizer (bazzagh) in Hanafi fiqh. The key principle: a professional who acts with permission is not liable for unforeseen harm as long as he respects the usual practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and acts
The passage refers to two practitioners: the cupper (fassad) who opens a vein, and the cauterizer (bazzagh) who applies a hot iron. Both are performing therapeutic procedures.
2
Identify the default ruling
If they do not exceed the usual place (al-mawdiʿ al-muʿtād), they are not liable for any resulting death.
The ruling applies to both uniformly.
3
Identify the exception
If they exceed the usual spot, they become liable (daman). This is because they have transgressed (taʿaddā) the bounds of permission.
Transgression removes the protection of permission.
4
Extract the underlying principle
The ruling is based on the concept of idhn (permission). A person who acts with permission is not liable for normal consequences, but liability arises when he exceeds what is permitted.
This is a standard Hanafi principle in tort law.
5
Apply the principle to a scenario
Imagine a cupper makes a standard cut but the patient dies from a rare reaction. The cupper is not liable because he stayed within the customary limits. If he cuts more than needed, he is liable for any harm.
Custom (ʿurf) defines the usual practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا فصد الفصاد او بزغ البزاغ ولم يتجاوز الموضع المعتاد فلا ضمان عليه [١١٨٢) (٢٧)
اگر فصد کھولنے والے نے فصد کھولی یا داغ لگانے والے نے داغ لگایا اور معتاد جگہ سے آگے نہیں بڑھا تو ان دونوں پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس کا جو ان سے ہلاک ہوا۔ اور اگر اس سے بڑھ گیا تو ضمان ہوگا۔
فصد لگانے والے کو جسم چیرنا پڑتا ہے۔ پس اگر اتنا ہی چیرا جتنا چیرنا چاہئے پھر بھی آدمی ہلاک ہو گیا تو فصد کھولنے والے پر کچھ ضمان نہیں ہو گا۔ اسی طرح داغ لگانے والے نے جسم پر اتنا ہی داغ لگایا جتنا لگانا چاہئے پھر بھی ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا۔ اور زیادہ لگا دیا جس کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہوا تو ضمان لازم ہوگا۔
مناسب مقام تک فصد لگانے اور اس کو چیرنے کی اس کو اجازت ہے اس لئے اتنا چیر نے یا داغ لگانے سے ہلاک ہو جائے تو ضامن نہیں۔
And when the cupper cups or the cauterizer cauterizes and does not exceed the usual place, then there is no liability upon him. [1182] (27) If the cupper opens a vein or the cauterizer applies a brand, and they do not go beyond the customary place, then there is no liability on both for anyone who dies from it. And if he goes beyond that, then there is liability. The cupper has to cut the body. So if he cuts only as much as needed, and yet the person dies, there is no liability on the cupper. Similarly, the cauterizer applied exactly the necessary spot, and yet the person died, he is not liable. If he applies more and causes death, then liability is necessary. He has permission to cup and cut up to the appropriate place; therefore, if he dies from that much cutting or branding, he is not liable.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It concerns medical practitioners: a cupper (fasād) who draws blood or a cauterizer (bazzāgh) who burns the skin. The ruling says they are not liable for any death that occurs as a result of the procedure, provided they do not exceed the usual site (al-mawdiʿ al-muʿtād). The permission to perform the procedure is limited to the standard area; if they exceed it, they have transgressed (taʿaddā) and become liable. This is based on the principle that a person who acts with permission (idhn) is not liable for harm that normally results from that permitted act, as long as they stay within the bounds of custom. The commentary emphasizes the distinction: the practitioner is entrusted to act only to the necessary extent; any deviation makes him a transgressor (mutʿaddī) and thus liable for the ensuing harm.

Key Terms
فصاد (faṣṣād): A cupper, one who performs phlebotomy (venesection) by cutting a vein to draw blood.
بزاغ (bazzāgh): A cauterizer, one who applies a hot iron to burn a wound for therapeutic purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a cupper (fassad) liable for a patient's death?
A) Always, because he directly causes harm
B) Never, because he is a professional
C) Only if he cuts beyond the usual place
D) Only if he was not paid

Key Takeaway
A cupper or cauterizer is not liable for harm if he remains within the customary limits of procedure; exceeding those limits creates liability.

Non-Liability of a Hired Worker for Human Deaths
Ruling that a hired person is not liable for human death from accidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a hired worker is not liable for accidental human deaths occurring during the execution of the hire contract, identify the proofs from athar, and explain the rationale including the role of the 'aqila.

Core Idea
A hired worker is not liable for human death caused by the work—death is incidental to the contract, not a crime.

This passage addresses a critical question in Islamic contract law: if a hired person (ajir) accidentally causes the death of a human being while performing the hired work, is he liable for blood money? The Hanafi school holds that he is not, and this lesson unpacks the ruling, the reasoning, and the evidence from early authorities. You will see how the contract of hire shifts liability away from the worker, protecting him from ruin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the performance of hired work that accidentally causes a human death (e.g., drowning from a boat sinking, falling from an animal). The ruling is that the hired person (ajir) is NOT liable (la yadman) for the death.
The passage begins with 'But he is not liable for human beings.'
2
Understand the rationale
The commentary provides two reasons: (1) The death is due to the contract, not a crime, so the 'aqila (tribe) does not pay blood money. (2) If liability were imposed, the hired worker would be ruined. The death is qatl khata' but the cause is the hire, not a criminal act.
The 'aqila normally pays for accidental killing, but here they are exempt.
3
Examine the evidence from athar
The passage cites two narrations: (a) 'Amir al-Sha'bi was asked about a camel owner who carried people and they drowned; he ruled nothing is upon him. (b) Shuraih did not hold the boatman liable for drowning or burning.
These athar are from the early generation (tabi'un) and serve as precedent.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i reportedly holds a liable position in some cases. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the hired worker must pay diya or not.
This lesson focuses on the Hanafi position; the dispute is acknowledged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۶) الا انه لا يضمن به بنی آدم فمن غرق في السفينة او سقط من الدابة لم يضمنه 
مگر یہ نہیں ضامن ہوگا بنی آدم کا پس جو غرق ہو گیا کشتی ڈوبنے کی وجہ سے یا گر گیا، چوپائے سے تو اس کا ضامن نہیں ہو گا۔ البتہ اجرت کے موقع پر انسان ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کا ضمان اجیر پر نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ کسی کھینچنے کی وجہ سے کشتی ڈوب گئی اور اس کی وجہ سے آدمی مر گیا تو آدمی کا ضمان اجیر پر نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی طرح نگام کھنچنے کی وجہ سے آدمی چوپائے سے گر گیا اور مرگیا تو اجیر پر آدمی کا ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
یر کی غلطی کی وجہ س آئی کی ان گئی تو یقیل خا ہے اور قل لا کا تاوان اجیر کے خاندان کے لوگ دیں گے جو جبر کے عاقلہ میں ۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ اجیر کے عاقلہ جنانیت کی وجہ سے جو قتل خطا ہوا ہو اس کا تاوان دین گے۔ اور یہ قتل خطا جنایت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوا ہے بلکہ عقد اجرت کی وجہ سے ہوا ہے اس لئے اجیر کے عاقلہ یعنی خاندان والے اس کا تاوان ادا نہیں کریں گے۔ اس لئے خود اجیر پر بھی انسانی ہلاکتوں کا ضمان لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) انسان کا مضمان تو بہت ہوتا ہے۔ اگر اس کا ضمان لازم کریں تو اجیر تباہ ہو جائے گا اس لئے انسان کا ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا (۳) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ سئل عـامـر عـن صاحب به يو حمل قوما فغرقوا قال ليس عليه شيء (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ضمان الاجير الذى يعمل بیده ، ج ، امن ،ص ۲۲۱، نمبر ۱۴۹۶۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اونٹ والے نے کچھ لوگوں کو سوار کیا پھر وہ سب غرق ہو گئے تو اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں کیا (۳) عن ابن سيرين عن شريح انه كان لا يضمن الملاح غرقا ولا حرقا (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۴ ۵ فی الا جیر یضمن ام لا؟ ج رابع میں ۳۱۵ نمبر ۲۰۴۸۸) اس اثر میں حضرت شریح نے ملاح پر ڈوبنے اور جلنے کی وجہ سے کچھ لازم نہیں کیا۔
But he is not liable for human beings. So whoever is drowned in the ship or falls from the animal, he is not liable for him. ... The hired person is not liable for human deaths resulting from the drowning or falling. The blood money for accidental killing is paid by the 'aqila (tribe), but here the death is due to the contract of hire, not a crime, so the 'aqila does not pay, and the hired person himself is not liable. ... There are proofs from narrations: 'Amir was asked about a camel owner who carried people and they drowned; he said nothing is upon him. Also from Ibn Sirin from Shuraih that he did not hold the boatman liable for drowning or burning.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the author, explaining that a hired worker (ajir) is not liable for the death of a human being caused by the work itself, such as drowning from a sinking boat or falling from an animal. The commentary provides two reasons: first, the 'aqila (tribe) usually pays blood money for accidental killings, but here the death is not due to a crime but due to the contract, so they do not pay; second, if liability were imposed, the hired worker would be ruined. The author then cites two athar (narrations) as evidence: one from 'Amir al-Sha'bi about a camel owner who carried people and they drowned, and another from Shuraih who ruled that a boatman is not liable for drowning or burning. This establishes the Hanafi position that such liability is not incurred.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or responsibility to compensate for loss or damage.
عاقلہ (aqila): The tribe or group responsible for paying blood money (diya) for accidental killing by one of their members.
قتل خطا (qatl khata'): Accidental killing where there is no intent.
اجير (ajir): A hired worker, either specific (ajir khas) or general (ajir mushtarak).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, is a hired boatman liable if passengers drown due to the boat capsizing accidentally?
A) Yes, he is liable for the deaths.
B) No, he is not liable for the deaths.
C) Yes, but only if he was negligent.
D) No, because passengers are not human.

Key Takeaway
A hired worker is not liable for accidental human death caused during the performance of the hire contract, as the death is considered incidental to the contract, not a criminal act.

Liability of Phlebotomist and Cauterizer
Ruling on liability of medical practitioners if they cause death when staying within limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for non-liability of a medical practitioner and determine liability in given scenarios.

Core Idea
A medical practitioner is not liable if he stays within customary limits; exceeding them triggers liability.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text addresses the liability of medical practitioners who cause death while performing procedures. The distinction hinges on whether the practitioner acted within the customary boundaries (al-mawdi' al-mu'tad) or exceeded them. Understanding this ruling is crucial for applying the Hanafi principle of daman (liability) in cases of permissible but dangerous actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage discusses two acts: phlebotomy (fasad) and cauterization (bazgh). The ruling has two parts: no liability if within usual limits, and liability if exceeded.
2
Define 'usual limits'
The 'usual place' (al-mawdi' al-mu'tad) is determined by custom and medical practice. It refers to the standard, accepted extent of the procedure.
This is a matter of custom ('urf) which is a source of law in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the condition to examples
Consider scenarios: if the phlebotomist cuts only as much as needed and the patient dies, no liability. If he cuts deeper than usual and causes death, he is liable.
The harm must be a direct result of the transgression (ta'addi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۷) واذا فصد الفصاد او بزغ البزاغ ولم يتجاوز الموضع المعتاد فلا ضمان عليهما فيما عطب من ذلك وان تجاوزه ضمن 
اگر فصد کھولنے والے نے فصد کھولی یا داغ لگانے والے نے داغ لگایا اور معتاد جگہ سے آگے نہیں بڑھا تو ان دونوں پر ضمان نہیں ہے اس کا جوان سے ہلاک ہوا۔ اور اگر اس سے بڑگ گیا تو ضمان ہوگا۔
فصد لگانے والے کو جسم چیرنا پڑتا ہے۔ پس اگر اتناہی چیرا جتنا چیر نا چاہئے پھر بھی آدمی ہلاک ہو گیا تو فصد کھولنے والے پر کچھ ضمان نہیں ہو گا۔ اسی طرح داغ لگانے والے نے جسم پر اتنا ہی داغ لگایا جتنا لگانا چاہئے پھر بھی ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا۔ اور زیادہ لگا دیا جس کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہوا تو ضمان لازم ہوگا۔
مناسب مقام تک فصد لگانے اور اس کو چیرنے کی اس کو اجازت ہے اس لئے اتنا چیر نے یا داغ لگانے سے ہلاک ہو جائے تو ضامن نہیں حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شریح سے پوچھا گیا کہ اونٹ والے نے کچھ لوگوں کو اٹھایا۔ پس وہ لوگ ڈوب گئے۔ فرمایا اونٹ والے پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہے (ب) حضرت شریح سے منقول ہے کہ ملاح ڈوبنے اور جلنے کا ضامن نہیں ہے۔
حاشیۂ : حضرت شریح فرماتے ہیں کہ کرایہ دار پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر تعدی کی اور شرط سے تجاوز کیا اور ہلاک ہوا تو حضرت شریح نے فرمایا اس پر کرایہ اور ضمان دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔
And if the phlebotomist performs phlebotomy or the cauterizer cauterizes and does not exceed the usual place, then there is no liability upon them for what is damaged from that; and if he exceeds, he is liable. ... The phlebotomist has to cut the body. So if he cuts only as much as is necessary and the person dies, there is no liability; similarly for the cauterizer. If he applies more than necessary and causes death, he is liable. ... Footnote: Shuraih said: The lessee is not liable; if he transgresses and exceeds the condition and damage occurs, then both rent and liability are upon him.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for medical practitioners: a phlebotomist (fassad) and a cauterizer (bazzagh) are not liable for death if they perform the procedure within the usual and permissible limits (al-mawdi' al-mu'tad). The Arabic text states 'no liability upon them for what is damaged from that; and if he exceeds, he is liable.' The Urdu commentary clarifies that if the practitioner cuts only as much as is necessary or applies cautery only to the required extent, and the patient dies due to the procedure, the practitioner is not liable because he acted with permission. However, if he exceeds the limit and causes harm, he becomes liable. The footnote from Shuraih provides a parallel principle: a lessee is not liable as long as he stays within bounds; if he exceeds, both the rent and liability are due. This reflects the Hanafi principle that permission to act within limits exempts from liability for accidental harm, but exceeding limits constitutes transgression (ta'addi) triggering liability.

Key Terms
فصد (fasad): Phlebotomy or bloodletting by incision.
بزغ (bazgh): Cauterization or branding with a hot iron.
الموضع المعتاد (al-mawdi' al-mu'tad): The usual or customary place for the procedure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a phlebotomist cuts the patient in the usual spot but the patient dies due to an unknown allergy, is the phlebotomist liable?
A) Yes, because death occurred.
B) No, because he did not exceed the usual limit.
C) Yes, because he should have known about the allergy.
D) No, because the patient should have informed.

Key Takeaway
A medical practitioner is not liable for harm when acting within customary limits; exceeding those limits makes him liable.

Definition and Liability of a Special Employee (Ajir Khas)
Definition and ruling on non-liability of a special employee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the special employee (ajir khas) and state the Hanafi ruling on his liability for property damage in his custody.

Core Idea
A special employee is not liable for damage to property held as an amanah unless he transgresses.

This lesson defines the ajir khas (special employee) in Hanafi fiqh and explains his liability for property in his custody. The key distinction is that he is hired for a specific period and earns wages simply by making himself available, not necessarily by completing work. This affects the legal status of property in his hands: it is an amanah (trust), so he is not liable for loss or damage unless he exceeds the limits of his permission (ta'addi). Understanding this ruling is essential for properly applying the rules of hire (ijara) in Islamic commercial law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of ajir khas
From the Arabic and Urdu, extract the defining characteristics: hired for a specific period, exclusive service, wage earned by availability.
The Urdu commentary emphasizes that he cannot work for others during the period.
2
Contrast with ajir mushtarak
Note that the common worker is hired for a specific task and can work for others; the special employee is exclusive and his custody is an amanah.
This contrast clarifies the basis of non-liability.
3
State the ruling on liability
The passage clearly states la daman (no liability) on the ajir khas for what is damaged in his hand or by his action, unless he commits ta'addi.
The phrase 'in his hand' covers property in his custody.
4
Analyze the basis of non-liability
The reason given: the property is an amanah, and an amanah only imposes liability when there is transgression.
This is a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: custody without liability unless fault.
5
Apply to examples
The passage gives examples: a goat dying naturally or a kid dying; in both cases, no liability without transgression.
The footnote from Shuraih reinforces the rule.

Source Text

اجیر خاص اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ خاص مدت میں اسی کا مزدور ہو کسی اور کا نہ ہو۔ اور اس مدت میں اس کا کام کر سکتا ہوکسی اور کا نہ کر سکتا ہو ۔ جیسے صبح سے لیکر شام تک مزدور کو اجرت پر لیتے ہیں کہ اس کا کام کرے گا کسی اور کا نہیں یا مثلا ایک ماہ تک مالک کی خدمت کرے گا یا ایک ماہ تک مالک کی بکری چرائے گا۔ تو یہ اجیر مشترک نہیں اجیر خاص ہے۔ اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ کام کم کرے یا زیادہ کرے یا نہ کرے، صرف صبح سے شام تک مدت متعینہ میں مستأجر کو سپر د کر دے اسی سے وہ اجرت کا مستحق ہو جاتا ہے۔
(۲۹) ولا ضمان على الاجير الخاص فيما تلف في يده 
اور نہیں ضمان ہے اجیر خاص پر اس کا جو ضائع ہو جائے اس کے ہاتھ میں اور نہ جو ضائع ہو جائے اس کے عمل سے مگر یہ کہ زیادتی کرے۔
تشریح اجبیر خاص کے ہاتھ میں جا کر کوئی چیز ضائع ہو جائے یا جو منافع وجود میں آئے تھے ان میں سے کچھ نفع ضائع ہو گیا تو ان دونوں کے ضائع ہونے پر اجیر خاص پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ مثلا بکری چرانے کے لئے اجیر خاص کو دی اور بکری اس کے پاس سے بغیر اس کی تعدی کے ہلاک ہوگئی تو اجیر پر بکری کا تاوان نہیں ہے۔ یا بکری کو بچہ ہوا اور اجیر کے پاس مر گیا تو اس بچے کا تاوان اجبیر پر نہیں ہے۔
اجیر خاص کے ہاتھ میں جو کچھ ہے چاہے عین شی ہو یا اس کے منافع ہوں وہ مالک کی اجازت سے ہیں اور اس وقت کسی اور کا مال اجیر کے ہاتھ میں نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ مال امانت کے طور پر اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے اور بغیر تعدی کے امانت ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہوتا نہیں یہ کے پر اس کے ہاتھ اور تو پر لازم ہوتا حاشیہ : حضرت شریح فرماتے ہیں کہ کرایہ دار پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر تعدی کی اور شرط سے تجاوز کیا اور ہلاک ہوا تو حضرت شریح نے فرمایا اس پر کرایہ اور ضمان دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔
(28) And the special employee (ajir khas) is the one who deserves the wage by surrendering himself during the period, even if he does not work, like one who hires a man for a month for service or for shepherding sheep. ... (29) And there is no liability on the special employee for what is damaged in his hand or by his action, unless he exceeds (limits). ... Explanation: If property in the hand of the special employee is destroyed, or some of the benefits coming into existence are lost, there is no liability on the special employee for their loss. For example, if a goat is given to a special employee for shepherding and it dies without his transgression, he is not liable for the goat. Or if the goat gives birth and the kid dies in his custody, he is not liable. ... Footnote: Shuraih said: The lessee is not liable; if he transgresses and exceeds the condition and damage occurs, then both rent and liability are upon him.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage defines the special employee (ajir khas) and states his non-liability for property damage. The Arabic definition: the ajir khas is one who is hired for a specific period (e.g., a month for service or shepherding) and earns the wage simply by making himself available for that period, regardless of whether he works or not. The Urdu commentary clarifies that he is exclusively hired; he cannot work for others during that time. The ruling: there is no liability on the ajir khas for property that is damaged in his hand or by his action, unless he transgresses (ta'addi). The Urdu gives an example: if a goat given to him for shepherding dies without his transgression, he is not liable; similarly if a newborn kid dies. The reason: the property is in his hand as an amanah (trust), and an amanah does not entail liability unless there is transgression. The footnote from Shuraih reinforces the principle: a lessee is not liable, but if he exceeds the conditions, both the rent and liability become due. This distinguishes the ajir khas from the ajir mushtarak (common worker) who may be liable in some cases.

Key Terms
اجير خاص (ajir khas): A special employee hired exclusively for a specific period, earning wages by making himself available.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or exceeding the limits of permission.
امانت (amanah): A trust; property held by someone with permission but without liability for loss unless through negligence or transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a shepherd for one month to tend his goats. The shepherd is an ajir khas. If a goat dies naturally without the shepherd's negligence, is the shepherd liable?
A) Yes, because the goat was in his care.
B) No, because he is a special employee and the goat is an amanah.
C) Yes, because he should have prevented the death.
D) No, because the goat was old.

Key Takeaway
The special employee (ajir khas) is not liable for property damage in his custody without transgression, as his possession is an amanah.

Definition and Wage Entitlement of Ajir Khas
Definition and ruling of ajir khas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ajir khas and state the condition for his wage entitlement in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
An ajir khas earns his wage by mere availability, not by actual work.

In Hanafi fiqh, not all hired workers are treated the same. The ajir khas (specific hired worker) is hired exclusively for a fixed period. His entitlement to wage rests on a unique principle: he becomes owed his full wage simply by making himself available during that period, even if no work is assigned. This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri lays out the definition and ruling clearly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the Arabic and Urdu text to extract the definition of ajir khas. Note the key phrase: 'الذي يستحق الاجرة بتسليم نفسه في المدة' (the one who becomes entitled to the wage by surrendering himself during the period).
Focus on the condition of taslim al-nafs (surrendering oneself).
2
Contrast with ajir mushtarak
The passage implicitly contrasts ajir khas with ajir mushtarak (common worker). Understand that ajir mushtarak earns wage by actual work, not mere availability.
This distinction is crucial for application.
3
Extract the ruling
State the ruling: Ajir khas is entitled to full wage even if he does no work, as long as he makes himself available for the entire contracted period.
The ruling is based on the contract's nature – the wage is for availability, not output.
4
Apply to examples
Work through the examples given: hiring for a month of service or grazing sheep. Notice that the worker need not actually perform to earn.
This illustrates the practical effect of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1183 (28) والاجير الخاص هو الذي يستحق الاجرة بتسليم نفسه في المدة وان لم يعمل كمن استأجر رجلا شهرا للخدمة او لرعى الغنم
