 اجیر خاص اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ خاص مدت میں اسی کا مزدور ہو کسی اور کا نہ ہو۔ اور اس مدت میں اس کا کام کر سکتا ہو کسی اور کا نہ کر سکتا ہو ۔ جیسے صبح سے لیکر شام تک مزدور کو اجرت پر لیتے ہیں کہ اس کا کام کرے گا کسی اور کا نہیں یا مثلا ایک ماہ تک مالک کی خدمت کرے گا یا ایک ماہ تک مالک کی بکری چرائے گا۔ تو یہ اجیر مشترک نہیں اجیر خاص ہے۔ اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ کام کم کرے یا زیادہ کرے یا نہ کرے، صرف صبح سے شام تک مدت متعینہ میں مستأجر کو سپر د کر دے اسی سے وہ اجرت کا مستحق ہو جاتا ہے۔
And the specific hired worker (ajir khas) is the one who becomes entitled to the wage by surrendering himself during the period even if he did not work, like one who hires a man for a month for service or for grazing sheep.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage defines the ajir khas (specific hired worker) and its ruling on wage entitlement. The text states that an ajir khas is a worker hired exclusively for a specific period, such as a month. He becomes entitled to his full wages merely by making himself available to the hirer for the contracted duration, regardless of whether he actually performs any work. For example, if a person hires a servant for a month to serve or to graze sheep, and the servant presents himself for work, he has earned his wage even if no work is assigned. The commentary clarifies that the ajir khas is distinguished from the ajir mushtarak (common worker) because he works exclusively for one hirer during the period and cannot work for others. The ruling is based on the principle that the wage is in exchange for the availability (taslim al-nafs), not for the actual output of work.

Key Terms
اجیر خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): A hired worker who is contracted exclusively for a specific period and cannot work for others during that time.
اجیر مشترک (ajīr mushtarak): A hired worker who works for multiple people or is available for hire by the general public, e.g., a tailor or doctor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes an ajir khas entitled to his full wage according to the passage?
A) Completing the assigned work
B) Working for the entire period without absence
C) Surrendering himself for the contracted period
D) Both working and being available

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the exclusive hire worker (ajir khas) earns his wage by making himself available for the entire contracted period, not by actual work performed.

Liability of the Specific Hired Worker (Ajir Khas)
States the rule of non-liability for ajir khas unless transgression occurs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the liability of an ajir khas and explain the condition that triggers liability.

Core Idea
An ajir khas holds property as an amanah; he is not liable for loss unless he commits transgression (ta'di).

This lesson examines a key principle in Islamic contract law: the liability of a specific hired worker (ajir khas). Unlike a common worker, the ajir khas is entrusted with property as an amanah (trust), and he is not automatically liable for loss. The Hanafi school derives this from an athar of Shuraih and the general principle that an amanah does not incur liability without transgression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Read the Arabic passage and find the statement that begins 'ولا ضمان على الاجير الخاص...'. What is the default rule for the ajir khas? He is not liable for loss.
The default rule is non-liability.
2
Locate the exception (condition for liability)
Look for the phrase 'الا ان يتعدى فيضمن' (unless he transgresses, then he is liable). What is the condition that changes the ruling? Transgression (ta'di).
Transgression can include negligence or exceeding the permitted scope of work.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The passage cites an athar from Shuraih: 'ليس على مستكرى ضمان فان تعدى فجاوز عليها الوقت فعطبت قال شريح يجتمع عليه الكراء والضمان'. Identify the source and understand how it supports the ruling.
The athar explicitly states no liability for the hirer unless transgression occurs.
4
Understand the rationale (amanah)
The commentary explains that the property in the worker's hand is an amanah. Why does that rule out liability? Because an amanah only incurs liability due to transgression or negligence.
This distinguishes the ajir khas from the ajir mushtarak (common worker) who may have different rules.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Although not detailed in the passage, note that the Shafi'i school holds the ajir khas liable even without transgression. The Hanafi response is that the property is an amanah, not a guarantee.
This difference has practical implications in legal systems.

Source Text

[1184 (29) ولا ضمان على الاجير الخاص فيما تلف في يده ولا في ما تلف من عمله الا ان يتعدى فيضمن. ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے وہی کیا جس کا اس کو حق ہے۔ ہاں ! زیادہ چیرنے سے ضامن ہوگا، کیونکہ اس کا حق نہیں تھا (۲) اثر میں ہے عن شريح انه قال ليس على مستكرى ضمان فان تعدى فجاوز عليها الوقت فعطبت قال شريح يجتمع عليه الكراء والضمان (الف) ( سنن سيھتي، باب لاضمان علی المکتری فیما اکتری الا ان بعدی، ج ساد، ص ۲۰۳ نمبر ۱۱۶۷۱/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الکری جعدی به، ج ثامن، ص ۲۱۲، نمبر ۱۴۹۲۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقام مناسب سے تجاز کرے گا تو ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اول جسم چیرنے میں حدود سے تجاوز کرے گا اور نقصان ہوگا تو اجیر پر ضمان ہوگا۔ اور حدود میں رہ کر چیرا تو ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ فصد : فصد کھولنا، جسم چیر کر خون نکالنا ۔ بزغ : نشتر لگانا جسم چیرنا - الموضع المعتاد : جہاں جہاں تک جسم چیر نا مناسب ہو۔ اور نہیں ضمان ہے اجیر خاص پر اس کا جو ضائع ہو جائے اس کے ہاتھ میں اور نہ جو ضائع ہو جائے اس کے عمل سے مگر یہ کہ زیادتی کرے۔
تشریح اجبیر خاص کے ہاتھ میں جا کر کوئی چیز ضائع ہو جائے یا جو منافع وجود میں آئے تھے ان میں سے کچھ نفع ضائع ہو گیا تو ان دونوں کے ضائع ہونے پر اجیر خاص پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ مثلا بکری چرانے کے لئے اجیر خاص کو دی اور بکری اس کے پاس سے بغیر اس کی تعدی کے ہلاک ہوگئی تو اجیر پر بکری کا تاوان نہیں ہے۔ یا بکری کو بچہ ہوا اور اجیر کے پاس مر گیا تو اس بچے کا تاوان اجبیر پر نہیں ہے۔
اجیر خاص کے ہاتھ میں جو کچھ ہے چاہے عین شی ہو یا اس کے منافع ہوں وہ مالک کی اجازت سے ہیں اور اس وقت کسی اور کا مال اجیر کے ہاتھ میں نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ مال امانت کے طور پر اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے اور بغیر تعدی کے امانت ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہوتا نہیں یہ کے پر اس کے ہاتھ اور تو پر لازم ہوتا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شریح فرماتے ہیں کہ کرایہ دار پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر تعدی کی اور شرط سے تجاوز کیا اور ہلاک ہوا تو حضرت شریح نے فرمایا اس پر کرایہ اور ضمان دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔
And there is no liability on the specific hired worker for what is lost in his hand nor for what is lost from his work unless he transgresses, then he is liable.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability (daman) of the ajir khas (specific hired worker). The ruling states that the ajir khas is not liable for any loss of the entrusted property or its benefits that occurs while in his possession or due to his work, as long as he does not commit transgression (ta'di). If he transgresses, he becomes liable. The text provides the example of a worker hired for grazing: if the sheep dies without his negligence, he is not liable; but if he exceeds the limits (e.g., grazes in a dangerous area), he is liable. The proof is an athar from Shuraih: 'There is no liability on the hirer (mustakri) unless he transgresses; if he transgresses and the time exceeds and it perishes, then both hire and liability are due.' The commentary emphasizes that the property in the hands of the ajir khas is amanah (trust), and amanah is not subject to liability unless there is ta'di. This is a key principle distinguishing the specific worker from the common worker (ajir mushtarak).

Key Terms
تعدی (ta‘addī): Transgression beyond the limits of what is permitted or contracted, including negligence or misuse.
امانت (amānah): Property held in trust, where the holder is not liable for loss unless due to negligence or transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does an ajir khas become liable for the loss of entrusted property?
A) Anytime the property is lost
B) Only if he transgresses (ta'di)
C) Only if he is paid in advance
D) He is never liable

Key Takeaway
The specific hired worker (ajir khas) is not liable for lost property unless he commits transgression (ta'di).

Conditions That Invalidate Ijarah: The Hanafi Position and Proofs
Ruling with proof: ijarah invalidated by conditions analogous to sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions that invalidate an ijarah contract according to the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A condition granting an extra unauthorized benefit invalidates ijarah, just as it invalidates a sale.

This lesson examines the principle that invalid conditions in a lease contract mirror those in a sale. You will learn the Hanafi ruling that such conditions make the contract fasid (voidable), and how two key hadith support this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Ijarah is a contract for usufruct. The text states that conditions which invalidate a sale also invalidate ijarah. So the ruling here is that such conditions make ijarah fasid.
Focus on the parallelism between bay' and ijarah.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: the prohibition of the price of a dog, earnings of a prostitute, and fee of a soothsayer; and the prohibition of the stud fee of a stallion. These are from Bukhari and Muslim.
These hadith are examples of prohibited contracts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition (nahy) indicates that these contracts are invalid (batil or fasid). By analogy, any ijarah containing an invalid condition that provides an extra benefit is similarly prohibited and thus fasid.
The nahy implies fasād in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school holds that any condition giving an extra benefit invalidates the contract, while the Shafi'i school restricts invalidity to conditions that contradict the essence of the contract.
This difference affects practical fatwa.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the general prohibition and analogy. Later Hanafi masters have relied on this view as mufta bihi.
The authority is zahir al-riwayah from the six core books.

Source Text

[1185 (30) والاجارة تفسدها الشروط كما تفسد البيع۔ 
 اجارہ کو فاسد کر دیتی ہیں شرطیں جیسے وہ فاسد کر دیتی ہیں بیع کو۔ 
 جو شرطیں بیع کو فاسد کرتی ہیں وہ شرطیں اجارہ کو بھی فاسد کرتی ہیں۔ مثلا ایسی شرطیں جن میں اجیر کا فائدہ ہو یا مستاجر کا فائدہ ہو تو ان شرطوں سے اجارہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اجارہ بھی بیچ کی طرح عقد ہے۔ فرق یہ ہے کہ بیچ میں عین شی کی بیج ہوتی ہے اور اجارہ میں منافع کی بیچ ہوتی ہے۔ تو چونکہ دونوں عقد ہیں اس لئے دونوں میں شرط فاسد سے عقد فاسد ہو جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابی مسعود الانصاري ان رسول الله لا نهي عن ثمن الكلب ومهر البغى وحلوان الكاهن (ب) بخاری شریف، باب کسب البغی والا ماء ص ۳۰۴ نمبر ۲۲۸۲ ر مسلم شریف، باب تحریم ثمن الكلب وحلوان الکا ھن دھر النبی ص ۱۹ نمبر ۱۵۶۷) اس حدیث میں زنا کی اجرت اور کاہن کے پاس جا کر اجرت دینے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ایسا اجارہ فاسد ہو گا (۳) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال نهی النبي عن عسب الفحل (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب حسب المحل ص ۳۰۵ نمبر ۱۲۲۸۴ مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم بیع فضل الماء... تحریم بیچ ضراب المحل ص ۱۸ نمبر ۴۰۰۵/۱۵۶۵) اس حدیث میں سانڈ کی جفتی کی اجرت سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیا جارہ فاسد ہے۔
And ijarah is invalidated by conditions just as they invalidate sale.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage states that ijarah (hire/lease) is invalidated by the same types of conditions that invalidate a sale (bay'). The commentary explains that conditions which provide an extra benefit to either party without being part of the consideration render the contract fasid (voidable). For example, if a condition stipulates that the ajir must do extra work not agreed upon, or that the hirer must pay more than the agreed wage under certain conditions. The reason is that ijarah is a contract like sale, except sale exchanges a physical object while ijarah exchanges usufruct (manafi'). Since both are contracts, invalid conditions affect them similarly. The text supports this with two hadith: (1) the prohibition of the price of a dog, the earnings of a prostitute, and the fee of a soothsayer, indicating that such contracts are invalid; (2) the prohibition of the stud fee of a stallion, showing that hiring for prohibited purposes is invalid. These examples illustrate that conditions contrary to Shariah or involving haram elements invalidate the ijarah.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (sharṭ fāsid): A condition that invalidates the contract because it provides an additional unauthorized benefit or contradicts Shariah.
عسب الفحل (asb al-fahl): The fee for mating a stallion, considered unlawful and invalid in ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what effect do invalid conditions (shurut fasidah) have on an ijarah contract?
A) The condition is invalid but the contract remains valid
B) The entire ijarah becomes fasid (voidable)
C) The ijarah becomes batil (void) automatically
D) The condition is ignored and contract continues

Key Takeaway
Conditions that invalidate a sale also invalidate an ijarah; such conditions make the contract fasid.

Traveling with a Hired Slave
Ruling statement with exception condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on traveling with a hired slave and identify the condition that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
Travel with a hired slave is prohibited unless stipulated in the contract.

This lesson examines the limits of a hire contract. A slave hired for service in a settled area cannot be forced to travel; the hirer must specify travel at contract formation. The ruling illustrates how conditions modify default obligations and is supported by the hadith on honoring conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
What is the default rule for hiring a slave for service regarding travel? The text says 'it is not permissible' (lā yajūz) to travel with him.
The default is prohibition.
2
Recognize the exception
Under what condition is travel allowed? The phrase 'unless he stipulates it in the contract' (illā an yashriṭa fī al-ʿaqd) indicates a conditional exception.
The condition must be explicit at contract formation.
3
Understand the rationale
Why does the school impose this restriction? Travel involves hardship (mashaqqa) and service in travel is difficult; the hire was originally for ḥaḍar.
Preventing hardship is a key principle.
4
Connect to the evidence
How does the hadith on conditions support this ruling? The hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' makes stipulations binding, so without a travel condition, the default stands.
The hadith is cited as dalīl naqlī.
5
Apply the ruling
In a scenario where a person hires a slave for city work and later wants to travel, determine permissibility: not allowed without a stipulation.
The slave has the right to refuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1186 (31) ومن استأجر عبدا للخدمة فليس له ان يسافر به الا ان يشرط في العقد۔ 
 کسی نے غلام کو خدمت کے لئے اجرت پر لیا۔ پس اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کو ساتھ لیکر سفر کرے مگر یہ کہ اس کے ساتھ اس پر شرط لگائے عقد میں ۔ کسی نے غلام کو حضر میں خدمت کے لئے لیا تو اس کو بغیر اس کی مرضی کے سفر میں نہیں لے جاسکتا۔ جب تک کہ عقد کرتے وقت شرط نہ لگائے کہ میں اس کو خدمت کے لئے سفر میں لے جاؤں گا۔ ہاں ! عقد اجارہ کرتے وقت یہ شرط لگائے کہ غلام کو سفر میں بھی لے جاؤں گا تو لے جاسکتا ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ 
 سفر میں مشقت ہوتی ہے اس میں خدمت کرنا مشکل کام ہے اس لئے حضر میں اجارہ ہوا ہے تو غلام کی مرضی کے بغیر اس کو سفر میں نہیں لے جا سکتا (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ وقال النبی الا الله المسلمون عند شروطهم (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب اجر السمسر ۃ ص۳۰۳ نمبر حاشیه : (الف) حضرت شعمی فرماتے ہیں کہ ماہانہ اجیر پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہے (ب) حضور نے منع فرمایا کتے کی قیمت سے، زنا کی اجرت سے اور کاہن کے پاس آنے سے (ج) حضور نے روکا سانڈ کی جفتی کی اجرت سے (د) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان شرطوں کا پاسبان ہے۔
And whoever hires a slave for service, it is not permissible for him to travel with him unless he stipulates it in the contract.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of hiring a slave for service in a settled area (hadar). The ruling is that the hirer cannot take the slave on a journey without the slave's consent (or without stipulating it in the contract). The reason given is that travel involves hardship, and the slave was hired for service in hadar. If the hirer wishes to travel with the slave, he must explicitly mention this condition at the time of the contract. The commentary cites the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' to support the idea that conditions in the contract must be honored. The passage implies that the slave's willingness (or the condition) is necessary because traveling changes the nature of the service and increases the burden on the slave. If the condition is not stipulated, the slave has the right to refuse travel.

Key Terms
حضر (ḥaḍar): Settled, non-travel area; the opposite of safar (travel).
شرط في العقد (sharṭ fī al-‘aqd): A condition explicitly mentioned in the contract that modifies the default terms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Obtain the slave's permission after hiring
B) Stipulate travel in the contract at the time of hiring
C) Pay extra wages
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
A hired slave cannot be taken on a journey unless travel is explicitly stipulated in the contract.

Liability of the Specific Hired Worker (Ajir Khas)
Ruling on non-liability of specific hired worker unless transgression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default rule of non-liability for a specific hired worker and identify the condition (ta'addi) that triggers liability.

Core Idea
The specific hired worker is a trustee; he is not liable for loss unless he transgresses.

This lesson addresses a key rule in Hanafi muamalat: the liability of a specific hired worker (ajir khas). Many assume that anyone handling another's property is automatically responsible for loss, but Hanafi law distinguishes based on the nature of the contract. The passage provides the ruling and its proof, clarifying that the ajir khas is an amin (trustee) and only liable if he exceeds his bounds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage states that the specific hired worker is not liable for loss unless he transgresses (ta'addi). The hukm is non-liability as a default.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar from al-Sha'bi: 'The monthly hired worker is not liable for guarantee.' This is a transmitted evidence (naqli) of the ruling.
The athar is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation of liability in the athar indicates that the default rule is no guarantee. The word 'ضمان' (guarantee) is negated, establishing the principle of non-liability.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih; some schools may hold the hired worker liable as a guarantor. Understand the Hanafi position and its basis.
5
Apply the principle
In practice, if a specific hired worker causes loss accidentally without negligence, he is not liable. Liability only arises upon transgression.
This distinguishes ajir khas from ajir mushtarak (general worker) who is liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا في ما تلف من عمله الا ان يتعدى فيضمن ۱۱۸۵ (۳۰) اس لئے اجیر خاص پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال ليس على اجير المشاهرة ضمان (الف)(مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۵۴ فی الجیر یضمن ام لا ؟ ج رابع ، ص ۳۱۵ نمبر ۲۰۴۸۷ ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ضمان الاجر الذي يعمل بیده ، ج عامن ص ۲۱۷، نمبر ۱۴۹۴۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اجیر خاص پر تعدی کے بغیر ہلاک ہو جائے تو ضمان نہیں ہے۔ اصول اجیر خاص کے ہاتھ میں مالک کا مال امانت ہوتا ہے۔
And he is not liable for what is lost of his work unless he transgresses, then he is liable. (30) Therefore, the specific hired worker is not liable for guarantee. (2) There is an athar: from al-Sha'bi who said: The monthly hired worker is not liable for guarantee. (Ref: Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this athar it is known that the specific hired worker, if his work is destroyed without transgression, there is no guarantee. The principle: The property in the hands of the specific hired worker is a trust.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the liability of a specific hired worker (ajir khas) in the Hanafi school. The matn states that the hired worker is not liable for loss of his work unless he exceeds his bounds (ta'addi). The commentary explains that the ajir khas is like a trustee (amin) — if the property in his hands is lost without his fault, he is not liable to pay compensation. The proof is an athar from al-Sha'bi that a monthly hired worker is not liable. This establishes that the default rule is non-liability; liability only arises if the worker is negligent or transgressive.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A specific hired worker who is employed exclusively for a particular task or period, as opposed to a general worker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The specific hired worker (ajir khas) is not liable for loss of the property in his care unless he transgresses or is negligent; he holds the property as a trustee (amin).

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

6 min
Invalid Conditions in Ijarah: Principle and Proofs
Ruling that invalid conditions in ijarah invalidate the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an invalid condition (shart fasid) renders an ijarah contract fasid, and identify such conditions using the provided proofs.

Core Idea
Conditions that contradict the purpose of ijarah or give unilateral benefit invalidate the contract.

In this lesson, we explore how the Hanafi school treats conditions in ijarah (hiring/leasing) contracts. The text establishes a core principle: just as invalid conditions void a sale, they also void ijarah because both are contracts. The argument is reinforced by prophetic prohibitions against certain wages, extending to any ijarah with an invalid condition. Understanding this will help you identify when a rental or service agreement becomes legally defective.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the general rule: invalid conditions (shart fasid) make ijarah fasid. This applies to any condition that benefits one party unfairly or contradicts the contract's nature.
Note the term 'fasid' means voidable, not absolutely void.
2
Examine the qiyas with sale
The text draws an analogy (qiyas) between ijarah and sale. Since both are exchange contracts, the rule about invalid conditions applies equally. Identify the underlying cause (illa): both involve exchange of property (substance vs. usufruct).
Difference: sale transfers ownership of the substance, ijarah transfers usufruct.
3
Analyze the first hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari forbids the price of a dog, wage of a prostitute, and fee of a soothsayer. These are examples of ijarah with illegitimate subject matter, thus invalid. Connect: if the subject matter itself is haram, the contract is fasid.
Implication: any ijarah for a prohibited purpose is invalid.
4
Analyze the second hadith proof
The hadith from Ibn Umar forbids the stud fee of a stallion ('asb al-fahl'). This is a specific instance where the benefit (breeding) was considered impermissible to rent out. Thus, similar conditions that involve deriving benefit from a thing in a prohibited manner also invalidate ijarah.
Hadith strengthens the principle: conditions leading to haram use invalidate.
5
Synthesize the legal operation
Combine the analogy and the hadith: invalid conditions are those that either (a) make the subject matter haram, or (b) introduce an unjust benefit (e.g., extra work without pay). Both make ijarah fasid.

والاجارة تفسدها الشروط كما تفسد البيع جو شرطیں بیع کو فاسد کرتی ہیں وہ شرطیں اجارہ کو بھی فاسد کرتی ہیں۔ مثلا ایسی شرطیں جن میں اجیر کا فائدہ ہو یا مستاجر کا فائدہ ہو تو ان شرطوں سے اجارہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اجارہ بھی بیچ کی طرح عقد ہے۔ فرق یہ ہے کہ بیچ میں عین شی کی بیج ہوتی ہے اور اجارہ میں منافع کی بیچ ہوتی ہے۔ تو چونکہ دونوں عقد ہیں اس لئے دونوں میں شرط فاسد سے عقد فاسد ہو جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابی مسعود الانصاري ان رسول الله لا نهي عن ثمن الكلب ومهر البغى وحلوان الكاهن (ب) بخاری شریف، باب کسب البغی والا ماء ص ۳۰۴ نمبر ۲۲۸۲ ر مسلم شریف، باب تحریم ثمن الكلب وحلوان الکا ھن دھر النبی ص ۱۹ نمبر ۱۵۶۷) اس حدیث میں زنا کی اجرت اور کاہن کے پاس جا کر اجرت دینے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ایسا اجارہ فاسد ہو گا (۳) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال نهی النبي عن عسب الفحل (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب حسب المحل ص ۳۰۵ نمبر ۱۲۲۸۴ مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم بیع فضل الماء... تحریم بیچ ضراب المحل ص ۱۸ نمبر ۴۰۰۵/۱۵۶۵) اس حدیث میں سانڈ کی جفتی کی اجرت سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیا جارہ فاسد ہے۔
Conditions invalidate ijarah just as they invalidate sale. For example, conditions that are beneficial to the hirer or the lessor — such conditions render the ijarah invalid. Because ijarah is a contract like sale. The difference is that in sale the substance is sold, while in ijarah the usufruct is sold. Since both are contracts, an invalid condition invalidates the contract. (2) There is a hadith indicating this: from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari that the Messenger of Allah forbade the price of a dog, the wage of a prostitute, and the fee of a soothsayer. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith prohibits the wage of prostitution and paying the soothsayer, indicating that such ijarah is invalid. (3) Another hadith: from Ibn Umar: the Prophet forbade the stud fee of a stallion. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith prohibits the rental of animals for breeding, indicating that such ijarah is invalid.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage discusses how invalid conditions affect ijarah. The matn establishes the principle that conditions that invalidate sale also invalidate ijarah, because both are contracts. The commentary explains that if a condition benefits one party unfairly, it renders the contract fasid (invalid). Two hadith are cited: the prohibition of the price of a dog, prostitute's wage, and soothsayer's fee, and the prohibition of stud fees. These show that ijarah involving prohibited acts (like zina or soothsaying) or prohibited uses (like animal breeding for a fee without ownership transfer) are invalid.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition that contradicts the nature of the contract or introduces an unlawful benefit.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease, where the owner transfers usufruct of an asset in exchange for payment.
عسب الفحل ('asb al-fahl): The stud fee paid for breeding services of a male animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person hires a slave for service but stipulates that the slave must also work for a third party without extra pay?
A) The condition is valid because it benefits the hirer.
B) The condition invalidates the entire ijarah.
C) The condition is invalid but the ijarah remains valid.
D) The condition makes the ijarah makruh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that any condition in an ijarah contract that gives one party an unfair benefit or contradicts the contract's purpose renders the contract fasid, based on analogy with sale and prophetic prohibitions.

Taking a Hired Slave on a Journey: The Stipulation Requirement
Ruling on hiring a slave for service and travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking a hired slave on a journey and apply the hadith proof concerning contractual conditions.

Core Idea
Without an explicit stipulation, the hirer has no right to take the slave on a journey.

This passage tackles a specific scenario in ijarah contracts: when a slave is hired for service in a town, can the hirer later take him on a journey? The answer hinges on the initial agreement. Let's examine the ruling, its rationale, and the prophetic evidence that governs it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is taking a hired slave on a journey when the hire was for service in the town. The default ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz) unless stipulated in the contract.
The text explicitly states: 'فليس له ان يسافر به الا ان يشترط عليه ذلك في العقد'.
2
Understand the rationale (illah)
Travel involves extra hardship ('safar fiihi mashaqqa') and service during travel is more difficult. Therefore, the default contract (for town service) does not include travel without the slave's consent.
This protects the slave from un-agreed burdens.
3
Locate the dalil and its legal implication
The author cites the hadith: 'المسلمون عند شروطهم' (Muslims are bound by their conditions). This establishes that conditions in a contract must be honored. Since no travel condition was made, the hirer cannot impose travel.
The hadith implies that the agreed terms define the scope of service.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن استأجر عبدا للخدمة فليس له ان يسافر به الا ان يشترط عليه ذلك في العقد کسی نے غلام کو خدمت کے لئے اجرت پر لیا۔ پس اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کو ساتھ لیکر سفر کرے مگر یہ کہ اس کے ساتھ اس پر شرط لگائے عقد میں ۔ کسی نے غلام کو حضر میں خدمت کے لئے لیا تو اس کو بغیر اس کی مرضی کے سفر میں نہیں لے جاسکتا۔ جب تک کہ عقد کرتے وقت شرط نہ لگائے کہ میں اس کو خدمت کے لئے سفر میں لے جاؤں گا۔ ہاں ! عقد اجارہ کرتے وقت یہ شرط لگائے کہ غلام کو سفر میں بھی لے جاؤں گا تو لے جاسکتا ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ سفر میں مشقت ہوتی ہے اس میں خدمت کرنا مشکل کام ہے اس لئے حضر میں اجارہ ہوا ہے تو غلام کی مرضی کے بغیر اس کو سفر میں نہیں لے جا سکتا (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ وقال النبی الا الله المسلمون عند شروطهم (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب اجر السمسر ۃ ص۳۰۳ نمبر حاشیه : (الف) حضرت شعمی فرماتے ہیں کہ ماہانہ اجیر پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہے (ب) حضور نے منع فرمایا کتے کی قیمت سے، زنا کی اجرت سے اور کاہن کے پاس آنے سے (ج) حضور نے روکا سانڈ کی جفتی کی اجرت سے (د) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان شرطوں کا پاسبان ہے۔
Whoever hires a slave for service may not take him on a journey unless he stipulates that in the contract. Someone hired a slave for service in the town; then he cannot take him on a journey without his consent, unless he made a stipulation at the time of contract that he will take him on a journey. Yes, if during the ijarah contract he stipulates that he will take the slave on a journey, then he may do so; otherwise not. Because travel involves hardship and service is difficult; therefore if the ijarah was for the town, he cannot take him on a journey without the slave's consent. (2) There is a hadith: 'The Prophet said: Indeed the Muslims are bound by their conditions.' (Bukhari) (Footnote: ...)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on taking a hired slave on a journey when the hire was for service in the town. The matn says it is not allowed unless stipulated. The commentary explains the rationale: travel involves extra hardship, so the default is that the hirer cannot impose travel without prior agreement. The hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' supports that if the condition is stipulated, it must be honored. If no condition, the hirer cannot force travel.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition agreed upon in the contract that must be fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a slave for one year to work as a cook in his home. Midway, he wants to take the slave on a pilgrimage to Mecca. Can he do so without amending the contract?
A) Yes, because the slave is his employee.
B) No, because the contract was for service in the town only.
C) Yes, if he pays extra.
D) No, because the slave is not a camel.

Key Takeaway
The hired slave's travel requires an explicit contractual stipulation; otherwise, the hirer cannot force it.

Hiring a Camel with a Litter: Custom as a Determinant
Ruling on hiring a camel with a litter for two riders to Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of 'urf (custom) to determine unspecified terms in an ijarah contract and cite the dalil from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi ijarah, unspecified terms are filled by custom ('urf), supported by Quran and Sunnah.

This lesson examines a classic ijarah scenario: hiring a camel to carry a litter for two riders to Mecca. The matn rules it permissible, but the sharh expands on a key detail—what if the litter size is not specified? The Hanafi answer is that custom ('urf) determines the standard. We will unpack the ruling, the proof, and how this principle applies broadly in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage: the contract is permissible (ja'iz). But the hirer must use the customary litter if not specified. Note that the ruling comes with an implicit condition.
The condition is not a pillar but a shart (condition) derived from 'urf.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites two proofs: the hadith of Hind (Bukhari) and Quran 4:6. Both use the term 'ma'ruf' (customary). Identify the exact wording and its authority.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but the Quranic verse is qat'i.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The term 'ma'ruf' indicates that in contractual matters, what is customary and reasonable is binding. This is a core Hanafi usul principle: 'al-ma'ruf 'urfan ka al-mashrut shartan' (what is customary is like a stipulated condition).
This principle is derived from the dalil and applied via istihsan.
4
Examine the Commentary Expansion
The sharh clarifies that if the litter is not specified, the hirer must use the customary one—neither too large nor too small. This prevents disputes and ensures fairness.
The commentary uses the word 'mu'tad' (customary) and emphasizes that custom removes ambiguity.
5
Apply to Analogous Cases
Think of other ijarah contracts: hiring a truck without specifying load weight, hiring a room without specifying size. The Hanafi rule is the same: refer to local custom ('urf) to fill the gap.
This reduces gharar and validates many transactions that would otherwise be void due to ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن استأجر جملا ليحمل عليه محمله وراكبين الى مكة جاز وله المحمل المعتاد کسی نے اونٹ اجرت پر لیا تا کہ اس پر کجا وہ رکھ کر دو آدمی سوار ہو اور مکہ تک سفر کرے تو ایسا کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور اجیر پر لازم ہے کہ عام طور پر جو کجاوہ اونٹ پر رکھا جاتا ہے وہ کجاوہ اونٹ پر رکھے۔ نہ زیادہ بڑا ہو اور نہ چھوٹا ۔ جب کوئی خاص کجاوہ طے نہ ہو تو ایسی صورت میں معروف کی طرف پھیرا جاتا ہے۔ اور معاشرے میں معروف و مشہور جو ہو وہی لازم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں بھی متعادو معروف کجاوہ ہی رکھ سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت هند ام معاوية لرسول الله الله ان ابا سفيان رجل شحيح فهل على جناح ان آخذ من ماله سرا؟ قال خذى انت و بنوك ما یکفیک بالمعروف (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب من اجری امر الامصار على ما يتعارفون بينهم في البيوع والاجارة ص ۲۹۴ نمبر ۲۲۱۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابوسفیان کے مال میں سے جو معروف ہو وہ آپ لے سکتی ہیں۔ آیت میں بھی ہے۔ ومن كان فقيرا فليأكل بالمعروف (آیت ۶ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت میں بھی ہے کہ غریب آدمی یتیم کے مال کی تجارت کرے تو معاشرے میں جتنی معروف اجرت ہو وہ لے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں بھی کجاوہ طے نہیں ہوا ہو تو معروف کجا وہ رکھ سکتا ہے۔ و کوئی چیز طے نہ ہو تو معاشرے کی معتاد چیز کا فیصلہ ہوگا۔ محمل : اٹھانے کی چیز جمل سے مشتق ہے مراد ہے کجاوہ ۔ المعتاد : عادة سے مشتق ہے جو عام عادت ہو۔ [۱۱۸۸]
Whoever hires a camel to carry his litter and two riders to Mecca is permissible, and he should use the customary litter. Someone hired a camel to carry a litter so that two persons ride to Mecca; so doing this is permissible. And it is obligatory upon the hirer that he places the litter that is normally placed on the camel, neither too large nor too small. When no specific litter is agreed, then it refers to what is customary. And whatever is customary and well-known in society is binding. Therefore, here also he can place the customary litter. (2) There is a hadith indicating this: from Aisha that Hind Umm Muawiya said to the Messenger of Allah: 'Abu Sufyan is a stingy man, is there any sin on me if I take from his wealth secretly?' He said: 'Take what is sufficient for you and your children with ma'ruf (customary).' (Bukhari) This hadith indicates that one may take what is customary. Also the verse: 'And if he is poor, let him eat with custom.' So here also, if the litter is not specified, the customary litter should be used.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage addresses hiring a camel for a specific purpose: to carry a litter with two riders to Mecca. The matn states it is permissible and that the customary litter should be used. The commentary elaborates that if the litter is not specified, the default is the customary one ('urf). The proof is the hadith of Hind and the Qur'anic verse about orphans, both using the principle of 'ma'ruf' (customary). This shows that in ijarah, unspecified details are resolved by referring to local custom.

Key Terms
محمل (mahmil): A litter or howdah used for riding on a camel, specifically the customary type.
المعتاد (al-mu'tad): That which is customary and normal in society.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi ruling require when a person hires a camel for a litter and two riders, but the type of litter is not specified in the contract?
A) The contract is void due to ambiguity.
B) The hirer may choose any litter he likes.
C) The hirer must provide the customary litter in that locality.
D) The owner of the camel decides the litter.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, unspecified terms are resolved by reference to local custom ('urf), supported by Quranic and Prophetic authority.

Recommendation for the Camel Owner to See the Litter
Recommendation for pre-hire inspection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the camel owner inspecting the litter before the journey and explain why it is recommended rather than obligatory.

Core Idea
Inspecting the litter is recommended (mustahabb), not required, to ensure mutual satisfaction.

This short passage from a Hanafi fiqh work addresses a practical point in camel hire: should the owner inspect the litter before the journey? The text gives a clear recommendation but stops short of making it obligatory. Understanding this distinction helps you appreciate how the school balances contractual freedom with good practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the action: the camel owner seeing the litter. Determine its legal status from the text (mustahabb / sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
The text uses 'اجود' and 'بہتر' (better), indicating recommendation, not obligation.
2
Understand the reason
The text gives the purpose: to achieve satisfaction (رضا مندی) and settle the matter (بات طے) before the journey. This is a practical aim.
In contract law, mutual consent (rida) is foundational; this recommendation facilitates it.
3
Contrast with obligatory acts
Consider what would change if this were obligatory. Since it is not, the contract remains valid even without inspection. The absence of inspection does not affect legal validity.
This distinction is key to avoiding over‐regarding recommendations as requirements.
4
Apply to modern analogues
Think of a modern rental: a car rental agency showing the condition of the vehicle. The same principle applies: it is recommended but not mandatory.
The underlying illa (reason) is avoiding future disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان شاهد الجمال المحمل فهو اجود اور اگر اونٹ والا کجاوہ دیکھ لے تو زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ اونٹ والا کجاوہ دیکھ لے تو سفر سے پہلے رضا مندی ہو جائے گی اور بات طے ہو جائے گی اس لئے دیکھ لینا بہتر ہوگا۔ [۱۹] (۳۴)
And if the camel owner sees the litter, that is better. If the camel owner sees the litter, then before the journey satisfaction will be achieved and the matter will be settled. Therefore, seeing it is better.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This is a simple recommendation (istihbab) that the camel owner should inspect the litter before the journey to ensure mutual satisfaction and avoid later disputes. It is a practical guide to good contractual practice.

Key Terms
شاهد (shahida): To see/be a witness; here it means view/inspect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary benefit of the camel owner seeing the litter before the journey?
A) To ensure the camel can carry it.
B) To achieve mutual consent and avoid disputes.
C) To test the camel's strength.
D) To calculate the hire charges exactly.

Key Takeaway
The camel owner viewing the litter is a recommended practice (mustahabb) to ascertain mutual consent, but not a legal requirement.
